Page 4

Germany Expresses Willingness: to Participate in the Eastern European Non-Aggression Pact; Three Countries Agree on Compromise Measures with Germany; Central European Issues Awaited Until the Mid-May Conference 28

Stresa: The final meeting of the Stresa Conference adjourned at 9:30 this morning. The delegates wished to complete their discussions quickly so that they could depart for Geneva this afternoon. Today's agenda was very full, including (1) Germany's re-entry into the League of Nations; (2) the issue of the rearmament of Austria, Hungary, and Bulgaria, which is closely related to the Little Entente countries of Czechoslovakia, Romania, and Yugoslavia; (3) the Central European Pact, including the status of Austria. Since German leader Hitler agreed to join the Eastern European Pact, the British representative was greatly excited and will strive today to persuade Germany to re-enter European coordination. As for France's preparation to demonstrate against Germany's decision to rearm at the League of Nations Administrative Council on Sunday, it can be ignored. French figures expressed doubt about Hitler's decision to join the Eastern European Pact, but trusted the effectiveness of the League of Nations demonstration. The French hoped to gain British and Italian assistance to create a mechanism that could impose financial and economic blockades on Germany in the future if treaties continue to be violated. Italy may support France's proposal, but Britain, fearing that Germany would not comply, still does not want to be involved. It is expected that the League of Nations Administrative Council will refer the matter to a committee for review, and the result may be the shelving of the issue. According to today's news, Italy will soon present Germany with concrete measures for non-interference in Austrian affairs, which Germany has agreed to consider. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

Stresa: Looking at the results of the British, French, and Italian conference, its attitude toward Germany can be summarized as follows: Germany's actions in violating the Treaty of Versailles, which have already been implemented, will be recorded by the League of Nations Administrative Council based on France's application, and no further action will be taken. As for the issues themselves, Britain will be responsible for further negotiations with Germany, this is the first point. As for the future, if unilateral treaty violations occur again, the relevant countries will resolutely implement economic sanctions, this is the second point. It is said that this compromise is a success of British diplomacy. (National Telegram, 12th)

(Paris) According to a telegram from Stresa today, the contents of the French resolution to be submitted to the League of Nations against Germany's rearmament include, in addition to a moral condemnation of Germany's actions, a suggestion to establish a three-person committee to discuss how to use economic and financial sanctions to prevent the continuation of unilateral denials of treaties. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

Stresa: Britain and France have requested Italian Prime Minister Mussolini to issue invitations before the end of April to hold a conference of Danube countries in Italy in mid-May. The location of the conference has not yet been determined, but it will likely be in Rome. Austria's neighbors, such as Germany, Hungary, Czechoslovakia, Yugoslavia, as well as France and Italy, will participate in the conference. The participation of Romania and Poland is also under consideration. The purpose of this conference is to sign a concrete agreement to protect Austria's independence. It is also possible to conclude a Danube Pact. Britain's decision to support France and Italy's policy towards Austria has led to the decision to convene this new conference. (National Telegram, 13th)

(Paris) The major powers related to the Central European Pact will meet in Rome on May 20, as decided by the French and Italian representatives at the Stresa conference this morning. At that time, France, Italy, Austria, Germany, Poland, Hungary, and the Little Entente countries will send representatives to participate. The talks this morning were quite extensive. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini advocated the rearmament of Austria, Hungary, and Bulgaria this morning. Although Britain expressed sympathy, French Foreign Minister Laval strongly stated the danger of hastily deciding on such an important matter. It is believed that Britain, France, and Italy will soon issue a statement reiterating that they will not allow foreign interference in Austrian affairs. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

Three-Power Conference Achieves Tangible Results; Britain Continues to Urge Germany to Return to the League of Nations 29

Stresa: The Stresa Conference has achieved the following tangible results:

(1) Germany is now willing to join the Eastern European Pact, even if several signatory countries conclude mutual assistance agreements separately and record them in another document.

(2) France and Italy have decided on a concise agreement to guarantee Austria's independence.

(3) Britain and Italy agree to support France in appealing to the League of Nations regarding Germany's implementation of compulsory military service.

(4) Britain is now making renewed efforts to persuade Germany to rejoin the League of Nations. Germany's willingness to participate in the Eastern European Pact was announced by British Foreign Secretary Simon at yesterday afternoon's meeting. Other representatives were surprised and delighted upon hearing this. The news was relayed by German Foreign Minister Neurath to the British Ambassador in Berlin, who telegraphed it to Simon. When announcing the news, Simon also stated that Britain is willing to consult with Germany again before making any decisions regarding the overall European situation.

Berlin now says that the German government's move is due to the expressions of goodwill from other countries, and therefore Germany is making this major concession. It is expected that Germany's change of attitude will have a profound impact, not only on the outcome of the Stresa Conference but also on the overall European situation. Germany's decision is particularly welcomed by the Polish government. Previously, France and Russia had agreed in principle that if Germany and Poland refused to participate in the Eastern European Pact, then France and Russia would conclude an agreement themselves. Poland was in a difficult position, but now that Germany does not object to the Franco-Russian agreement, Poland has no reason to dislike it.

Another important result of the conference is that France and Italy have decided on a concise agreement to guarantee Austria's independence. Hitler has expressed his willingness to study the agreement.

At the same time, Britain's renewed efforts to invite Germany to rejoin the League of Nations are also seen as one of the major results of the conference. The conference will close today.

Italy and Britain now agree to support France's appeal to the League of Nations regarding Germany's violation of the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles. It is reported that a resolution opposing Germany's actions will be drafted by the Council of the League of Nations. The French representative has explained in detail to the Italian and British representatives the reasons for the French government's appeal, and the Italian and British representatives have made this decision. The representatives' opinion is that the final resolution to be submitted in Geneva should stipulate that the League of Nations closely study ways to prevent the continuation of unilateral actions denying treaty obligations. Regarding the issue of sanctions, the representatives have not reached an agreement. The conference also decided to continue studying the Air Pact and explicitly stated the positions of Britain and Italy.

It is expected that a large conference involving all relevant countries will now be held. According to widespread rumors, this conference may be held in London. This conference will lay the foundation for the two treaties mentioned by Simon, which will allow League of Nations member states, including Germany, the United States, and Japan, to join.

According to a formal French statement, Britain, France, and Italy, in view of Germany's rearmament, have unanimously decided that the organization of European security must be strengthened. It is reported that France's plan has been prepared and will be implemented soon. Italy is also preparing to do the same.

Judging from the situation, it is not impossible for the conference to be extended to Sunday, as the issues of disarmament and Germany's return to the League of Nations have not yet been discussed. In addition, the drafting committee for the final communiqué still has much work to do.

It is reported that the issue of allowing Austria, Hungary, and Bulgaria to rearm was also discussed, but the representatives did not delve into this issue. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini agreed that any expansion of the armaments of the three countries must depend on the attitude of the Little Entente (Czechoslovakia, Romania, and Yugoslavia). It is reported that the only condition put forward by Germany for joining the European Pact is that the two pacts must be completely separate and not combined into one document: one is the Eastern European Non-Aggression Pact, and the other is a separate and supplementary Mutual Assistance Pact, to be concluded by the willing countries. (Reuters, 12th)

Stresa: The tone of the memorandum submitted by France to the League of Nations has been softened in order to accommodate Germany's new attitude. A British spokesperson declared that Britain, France, and Italy have now established a general agreement as follows: (1) the three countries' attitude towards Germany's specific unilateral abandonment of the treaty; (2) measures to deal with future unilateral abandonment of military clauses in the treaty. At the meeting yesterday morning, the French delegation published a secret report on German armaments. Prime Minister Flandin solemnly expressed France's concerns about security and its due preparations. However, it is reported that since Germany has made new expressions, future meetings may take a completely new path. (National Telegram, 13th)

Stresa: The Havas News Agency's correspondent stationed in Stresa believes that the Stresa Conference has now achieved its intended goals and can be officially closed on Saturday or Sunday. The three governments have unanimously decided that the three countries should maintain close ties regarding the French government's application to the Council of the League of Nations regarding Germany's rearmament. In addition, the representatives of the three countries unanimously advocated that the European security organization should increase its strength. France has taken the lead in initiating methods to strengthen the security organization, and good results can be obtained in a short period of time. Italy is also preparing to take the same path, but Britain is taking a more reserved attitude. Britain believes that without further consultation with Germany to obtain a responsible statement from the German government leaders, substantial progress may not be easily achieved. However, such consultations do not necessarily require a separate meeting to be convened with Germany's participation. In short, Britain will be responsible for conducting consultations with Germany, but the negotiations currently underway between the various governments regarding the establishment of supplementary security systems can still proceed as usual and will not be hindered by the consultations with Germany. The planned diplomatic procedures in the next few weeks will therefore not be changed. (Havas, 13th)

Germany's Agreement to Participate in the Eastern European Pact Causes a Sensation in Berlin 30

Yesterday, Foreign Minister Neurath informed the British Ambassador to Germany that Germany was prepared to join the Eastern European Non-Aggression Pact. This shows that Germany has now changed its original attitude towards the Eastern European Pact. This news came from foreign sources, and political figures in Berlin were quite sensationalized upon hearing it. However, Germany's exact attitude is still unknown. Yesterday, British representative to Germany Newton met with Neurath and inquired about Germany's attitude if other countries concluded the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact. After consultations between Neurath and Hitler, he replied that Germany still considered it inappropriate to conclude the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact, but Germany, while opposing the Mutual Assistance Pact, could still sign the Eastern European Non-Aggression Pact. (Havas, 13th)

(London) Germany's decision to participate in the Eastern European Pact is a major step forward compared to the opinions expressed by German representatives to Simon and Eden during their recent visit to Berlin. Responsible sources in London claim that at that time, the German representatives expressed support for multilateral pacts that did not contain arbitrarily selected guarantees. The significant meaning of Germany's new decision lies in its agreement to arbitrarily selected guarantees. This change in opinion may have important consequences. (Reuters, 12th)

(Paris) According to the opinion of most observers here, Germany's preparation to participate in the Eastern European Non-Aggression Pact does not provide much assistance in various matters. They now believe that only Germany's participation in the Mutual Assistance Pact would be valuable, but Germany's willingness to sign the Non-Aggression Pact is also sufficient to indicate its willingness to cooperate with other countries. (Reuters, 13th)

Stresa: Regarding the German government's preparation to sign the Eastern European Non-Aggression Pact, some people here believe that Germany's attitude has changed and it is willing to cooperate with other countries again. Most people believe that this approach by Germany has no real value and is still of no practical help unless it signs the Mutual Assistance Pact. The so-called Non-Aggression Pact only reiterates the existing restrictions, such as the Kellogg-Briand Pact. What Germany intends to do should be inquired by the British government. French Foreign Minister Laval, without waiting for the results of the inquiry, will still go to Moscow on the scheduled date in order to sign the Franco-Russian agreement. The outline of this agreement has been agreed upon in Paris. When Laval goes to Geneva to participate in the extraordinary meeting of the Council of the League of Nations, he will jointly confirm it with Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov. The last item discussed at the Stresa Conference was the Western European Air Pact plan, with particular emphasis on the mutual assistance measures between the British and Italian air forces, and it is scheduled to end its work today. (Havas, 13th)

(London) Regarding the Stresa Conference, the impression obtained by various newspapers can be represented by the views of The Times, which stated: "The countries of Europe, feeling threatened, have been prompted by this conference to unite, and the desire of the countries to see Germany return to the League of Nations, and the will of the countries to continue to work towards this end while a glimmer of hope remains, have also been expressed by this conference." The Daily Mail believes that the Stresa Conference is a prelude to another expanded conference that will accommodate Germany's participation. The Daily Telegraph reported that what British policy has always been concerned about is Germany's return to the League of Nations. The newspaper also quoted the conditions put forward by German leader Hitler for returning to the League of Nations, namely, demanding the return of pre-war colonies or accepting a mandate to govern them. In addition, Foreign Secretary Simon stated at the Stresa Conference yesterday that Germany was prepared to participate in the Northeast European Non-Aggression Pact. The opinion expressed by the various newspapers can be represented by the views of the Daily Telegraph, which stated that "the security guarantees that can be given by the non-aggression pact proposed by Germany differ greatly from those already given by the Covenant of the League of Nations. It has already been acknowledged by that country that the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact, which is being carried out by France, Russia, and Czechoslovakia, should not be regarded as an obstacle to Germany's participation in the work of the peace organization." (Havas, 13th)

(Berlin) The Berlin Evening News published an article written by a reporter stationed in Stresa, saying, "The three-power conference of Britain, France, and Italy is an important international conference. Since 1914, only the Stresa Conference can be called a true 'peace conference.' The three major countries that signed the Treaty of Versailles have in fact recognized Germany's equal right to armament. As for the compromise reached by Britain, France, and Italy on the application to the Council of the League of Nations, it is nothing more than a mutual reconciliation to deal with the past and embellish the façade." (Havas, 13th)

Central European Countries Expand Armaments; Italy and France Hold Slightly Different Views; Four Mediterranean Countries Will Also Sign a Pact 31

Stresa: The three-power conference of Britain, Japan, France, and Italy discussed the issue of the rearmament of Central European countries. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini stated to the representatives of Britain and France that the Austrian army currently has only 30,000 troops, which poses a great danger to its territorial independence and political integrity. Furthermore, it seems inappropriate to disarm Germany's neighbors while Germany has illegally rearmed. French Foreign Minister Laval then spoke, saying that there would be many problems if Central European countries suddenly decided to rearm. If the Little Entente saw the neighboring three countries of Austria, Hungary, and Bulgaria rearm, they would inevitably be alarmed. Furthermore, the current balance of power among Central European countries should not be disrupted until prior arrangements have been made. It would inevitably cause the Central European countries to be alarmed if they decided to rearm before the appropriate time. In short, maintaining peace is the most important thing. Therefore, all countries concerned, whether they are former allies or former enemies, should not take such measures without common agreement. Finally, the three-power conference decided that this issue could not be resolved at the Stresa Conference and should be resolved by other means in the future. The afternoon meeting today will be devoted to discussing the Air Pact issue. In addition, today's meeting will also consider the benefits of Italy, Yugoslavia, Greece, and Turkey concluding the Eastern Mediterranean Pact. (Havas, 13th)

Stresa: Today is the last day of the three-power conference of Britain, France, and Italy. French Foreign Minister Laval will probably leave here tomorrow morning to go to Geneva. Before the Council of the League of Nations meets, Laval will first meet with Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov and the foreign ministers of the three Little Entente countries. As for the French government's memorandum to the Council of the League of Nations regarding Germany's rearmament, it will probably be released at noon tomorrow. Furthermore, Germany's proposal to join the Eastern European Non-Aggression Treaty is generally regarded as Germany's willingness to cooperate, but diplomatic circles believe that concluding such a pact has no real significant effect, as the Non-Aggression Pact already stipulates the principle of non-aggression, making it unnecessary. In the future, Britain will be responsible for inquiring about Germany's true intentions, while Laval will proceed to Moscow according to the original plan to sign the Franco-Russian agreement with the Soviet Union. (Havas, 13th)

150,000 American Students Hold Anti-War Movement; Class Strike for One Hour to Petition the President 32

(Washington) 150,000 students across the United States went on strike for an hour today to protest against war. However, riots occurred in various schools in Los Angeles, with the most serious incidents occurring at the University of Los Angeles. Police injured two female students with batons, and more than a dozen other students were also beaten. Several police officers were also slightly injured. This strike was well-organized. Students from hundreds of schools suddenly held meetings at noon and held demonstrations. Classrooms in schools of all sizes were empty. Student leaders expressed satisfaction with the students' unanimous response. The demonstrations held here were quite orderly, and the police adopted a non-interventionist attitude. When passing through Pennsylvania Avenue, a large number of students went to the White House to submit a petition to the President, which stated, "We solemnly swear today that we do not want to defend the government's engagement in any war." Government leaders do not want to express their opinions on this strike. (National Telegram, 11th)

Tsuruga: Soviet Ambassador to China Bogomolov, on his way back to his post, passed through Tsuruga at 2:00 PM on the 13th and will take a connecting ship from Kobe to Shanghai. (United Telegram, 13th)

Current Commentary

How Will Various Industries Cope After Overcoming the "Four-End" Deadline? 36

— Liu

The problem of recovering long-term loans, which was considered the biggest obstacle after the year-end closing of accounts last winter, now seems to have a stable solution in sight. The Money Trade Association decided at its meeting the other day that each money shop would, within its capacity, make changes to overdue loans in order to fulfill the purpose of supporting industry and commerce. Furthermore, the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications are also planning to continue to follow the methods used before last year's year-end closing of accounts by disbursing huge sums of money to relieve the market. There is also talk that the industrial and commercial credit small loans of the banking industry, regardless of whether the government's 2.5 million yuan is allocated, will definitely be lent out before the end of April. All of these are sufficient to stabilize people's minds and maintain the market.

However, things in the world often seem to pass safely in times of temporary or difficult circumstances. But at other times, some minor factor may overturn the situation. Trouble often arises from what is overlooked. Therefore, although the "four-end" deadline can be overcome, the days ahead are long, and the dangers have not yet disappeared. Therefore, it seems that we must be cautious in the aftermath. Here, I will present some simple and easily understood points.

(1) The fact that the "four-end" loan problem was able to be overcome through the joint efforts and division of labor of the silver and money industries is truly an excellent phenomenon. It is hoped that this spirit will continue to be upheld and sustained. Big banks and small banks, money shops and banks, and silver and money industries and various industries can all extend mutual assistance and embrace the idea of coexistence and common prosperity. They must abandon the accumulated habits of infighting and make harmony their mission. Since the market has not yet fully become optimistic, they must act as one member of the market. What would I be without you? Sharing a leaky boat, it is definitely not possible to seek temporary peace by "sweeping the snow from one's own doorstep." It is even more impossible to harbor schadenfreude and hope that others will fail so that I can survive. All of us, apart from working together, can hardly hope to "get through lean years and have good years."

(2) Among the various industries, the operations vary, but in the entire market, there is no place where there is no connection, whether visible or invisible. It would be best to warn and eliminate in the invisible any accidents that are deemed sufficient to cause unease and harm the market. Otherwise, if it is not possible to make amends and its impact is not significant, resulting only in one's own unease, then so be it. Otherwise, efforts should be made to assist them so that they can get through the current situation and then rectify their future. One should not blame the past, saying that it is a deserved retribution, and sit idly by and not help. One must know where people's hearts are going, regardless of the depths. A hasty mood is difficult to contain once it has been released. A single spark can start a prairie fire, so one must be cautious.

(3) Discard selfish and self-serving thoughts. When making careful calculations, think of others and consider your own future. Those who possess huge wealth have usually exhausted the enjoyment of the world. When adversity comes, they do not reflect on themselves, but want to transfer their losses to the public. Their calculations are clever. But they do not think that the difficulties they are facing today are mostly caused by the past. The fruit has already been eaten, but they still want to plant the evil cause of the future. Even if the immediate wound is healed, I am afraid that it will be in vain and only show that it is harming others and not benefiting oneself. We hope that the current relief of the market can be based on the interests of the majority and not on the private interests of the minority. The Shantou white ticket incident can serve as a profound lesson.

(4) Since overseas financial turmoil has occurred repeatedly, baseless rumors have also occurred in the domestic market, causing people to be alarmed and to see everything as a tiger. But since Kong and Song have repeatedly stated that the people have gradually understood the soundness of the government's policies and will definitely not take risky measures. In his speech, Song also mentioned Song Hanzhang's appointment as general manager of the Bank of China, saying that "he worked hard to prevent the Bank of China's banknotes from stopping redemption during the Yuan Shikai era. This appointment as general manager is deeply gratifying." The implication is even more imaginable. What would not be done in the Yuan Shikai era, how could it be done today? Since the authorities have shown people their trust, people should also repay them with trust. Mutual trust will stabilize people's minds and stabilize the market. Accumulated savings will be released and credit will be abundant.

US Economic Survey Group to Leave Japan for Shanghai on the 19th 37

Tokyo: The U.S. Economic Survey Group left Tokyo at 8:30 AM on the 13th to go to the Kansai region and is scheduled to take the President Harrison ship from Kobe to Shanghai on the 19th. (United Telegram, 13th)

Fear of War Reduced as Italy and Albania Both Agree to Arbitration 38

Stresa: According to today's news, Italy and Albania have both agreed to submit the border dispute to the mediation committee for arbitration, and the fear that the tense relationship between the two countries might lead to war has been somewhat reduced. (Reuters, 12th)

World Silver Prices Continue to Soar; US Believes Roosevelt Aims to Suppress Silver Faction; Bank of Japan Raises Price to Four Yen, Unprecedented Since the European War 39

(New York) World silver prices continue to soar, hence rumors are rampant in the market here today, saying that the US Treasury Department will again raise silver prices. The quoted silver price in New York is 68.5 cents per ounce, which is the highest point since January 1926. Merchants generally expect silver prices to continue rising. It is heard that this surge is partly stimulated by the remarks of Senator Pittman, who announced that President Roosevelt intends to raise the Treasury Department's silver purchase price to $1.29 in an orderly manner. According to the Treasury Department's latest report, as of March 29, the Treasury Department held a total of 457,000,000 ounces of silver, including: (1) 62,500,000 ounces held before the silver program was established; (2) 111,900,000 ounces purchased after the implementation of the nationalization policy; (3) 114,400,000 ounces purchased on the open market; (4) 2,800,000 ounces of subsidiary coins. If calculated based on the existing amount of $8,614,000,000 and assuming a silver price of $1.29 per ounce, the US government must continue to purchase 1,101,550,000 ounces of silver to meet the gold-silver ratio of 2:1. However, this amount actually exceeds the total available supply in the world. Today, the Dun & Bradstreet company issued a surprising forecast, saying that we will soon see an amazing development in business in the past 25 years. This statement has attracted the attention of the business community, and the Chicago Mercantile Exchange has seen prices surge as a result. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau issued a statement today denying rumors that the Treasury Department is currently using equalization funds to stabilize public stock prices, saying that this is illegal. The House Interstate Commerce Committee has held meetings to investigate whether there is any reason for such rumors, so the Treasury Secretary quickly issued this denial. (Reuters, 12th)

(Washington) Well-informed observers today generally believe that President Roosevelt's proposal to raise silver prices is intended to suppress the congressional silver faction's requirement of a gold-silver ratio of 16:1. However, this move by the government has apparently failed to discourage the silver faction. Congressman Murdock today proposed a bill to the House of Representatives stipulating that gold and silver be fixed currencies. Murdock's proposal does not specify the gold-silver ratio, but advocates authorizing the Treasury Department to control the market prices of gold and silver. (National Telegram, 12th)

(New York) After the Treasury Department stipulated that the price of raw silver be 71.11 cents per ounce, merchants unanimously predicted that the Treasury Department would further raise silver prices. The government's second step will be to reduce minting fees to 40%, thereby raising silver prices to 77.58 cents. Silver merchants here are particularly concerned about China's reaction to the gradual increase in silver prices. (National Telegram, 12th)

Mexico. The Mexican government hopes that the silver mining tax can bring in 72 million pesos annually. Speculators are competing to buy silver today in anticipation of continued price increases. It is heard that banks are also competing to buy silver coins. (National Telegram, 12th)

(Tokyo) According to a telegram received by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs from Ambassador Saito in the United States, the US President raised the price of domestically produced silver to 71 cents per ounce on the 10th. According to an investigation by the US Treasury Department on April 8, the number of silver holdings was 915 million yuan, and the number of gold holdings was 8.6 billion yuan. To reform the gold-silver reserve ratio of 3:1, the government needs to buy 1.95 billion yuan of silver. Now, when China and the United States are conducting negotiations focusing on the issue of the outflow of Chinese silver, the US government's move to raise silver prices is quite noteworthy. According to a foreign telegram from London on the 13th, due to the soaring silver prices in London, the Japanese financial community had no choice but to raise silver prices from 1.861 yuan to 3.911 yuan. Such a silver price of nearly four yuan has not been seen since the World War. According to observations by the Japanese Suiyokai (Wednesday Society), silver prices are likely to continue to rise in the future. (United Press, 13th)

(London) The Financial News commented on the relationship between the US silver policy and Far East diplomacy, saying, "The US silver purchase policy has caused a reaction in China, but the US authorities have ignored it. Chinese public opinion has therefore become increasingly unhappy. Japanese diplomacy aims to increase Japan's influence in China by promoting cooperation between China and Japan. Now, because the United States continues to raise silver prices, Japan's policy has become more successful. Recently, there has been much talk about British and American loans to China. It is doubtful whether these loans can become a reality. Even if British and American loans are successful, Chinese public opinion may not forget the pain caused by the US silver purchase policy." (Havas, 13th)

(London) The Daily Express today commented on the US Treasury Department's increase in silver purchase prices, saying that the US silver situation has a humorous flavor. What President Roosevelt fears most is the expansion of Japanese influence in China, but his consultations with domestic parties related to silver are precisely helping what he fears most. Japan knows very well that President Roosevelt's silver policy will worsen China's economic situation, so it can wait and see when China will be unable to resist Japanese aggression. The Financial News said that the US silver policy will drive China into the arms of Japan. Even if British and American loans can be realized, they may not be able to make the Chinese people forget the pain inflicted by the US's reckless silver policy. (Reuters, 13th)

Guo Taiqi's Speech: Progress in Sino-Foreign Relations 40

(London) Chinese Minister Guo Taiqi delivered a speech today at the Scottish Association of China in Edinburgh, saying that there has been significant progress in the relationship between the international community and China, which is deeply gratifying. In the past, when various countries interacted with China, they often regarded China as a true "Celestial Kingdom." In other words, they regarded China as a country on another planet. Their relationship was superficial and not genuine. Up to now, China's communication with other countries and its political and commercial relations have been completely changed. In terms of trade, most economists are seeking ways to remedy the stagnant state of global commerce and finance, and they all say that improving trade with China is the key. In terms of politics, the important issues recognized by the governments of Europe and the United States invariably have a bearing on China's survival. This truth has been recognized by the general public for several years, and it was particularly evident last year. This is indeed the best sign of the world's return to equilibrium, and the progress that China has worked hard to achieve last year has also been consolidated as a result. I firmly believe that China has no sense of fear towards the Western Hemisphere, nor does it go against it and isolate itself. If people say that China will re-adopt the "Asia for Asians" policy, it is tantamount to saying that China is unwilling to handle international relations with a broad mind, which is indeed inconceivable. Recently, there have been many rumors about China's neighbor, Japan. It is said that Japan is trying to persuade China, saying that the "Asia for Asians" policy is more suitable for China, and it has explained it in detail. I have heard people say that if Japan has such a plan, even if it spends all its money and efforts, the future of the Asian continent will definitely be hopeless as a result. This is not a blessing for China, nor is it beneficial to Japan. (Havas, 13th)

Lord Marley Criticizes Missionaries in China for Seizing Positions Through Deceptive Practices 41

(London) At a debate held by the Leysian Club today, Lord Marley, leader of the opposition in the Upper House, who traveled to Shanghai in 1932 and planned to initiate an anti-war conference, proposed a motion entitled "China Should Be Allowed Freedom to Decide Its Own Future." In his speech, Marley severely criticized European missionaries in China, saying that the clergy had seized positions in China through a kind of extremely deceptive international behavior that is rare in the world. A Sino-French treaty drafted by a certain Catholic priest stipulated that the meaning of the treaty should be based on the French text. There was a clause that was only found in the French text but not in the Chinese text. This clause allowed the church to acquire land. As a result, the church purchased the best land and maintained its ownership by force. He also said that the most egregious pioneering behavior he had ever heard of was seen in Annam. Mr. Mackeefley opposed the motion, saying that the various things done by the British in China had improved the situation of its people. The motion was ultimately defeated by six votes. (Reuters, 12th)

Quezon Remains in the United States to Continue Discussing Future Independence 42

(Washington) Philippine Senate President Quezon declared today after a meeting at the White House that President Roosevelt insists on the policy of Philippine independence and hopes to establish an autonomous government as soon as possible. I have informed the President of the gratitude of the Filipino people and the proper handling by Governor-General Murphy. Quezon and Murphy will remain in Washington to continue meeting with the President, but other Philippine representatives are scheduled to return to the Philippines on Monday. It is understood that although officials claim that the talks are limited to discussing the organization of an autonomous government, Quezon's extended stay here is enough to indicate that the US-Philippine talks have expanded in scope. Quezon was optimistic after talking with the President, saying that we had discussed organizing a fact-finding mission to examine the commercial relations between the two countries after the establishment of an autonomous government. The Mixed Committee is now the official committee to negotiate with the Philippine delegation. The first joint meeting will be held in Manila or Washington to prepare the necessary laws for the congressional meeting in January next year. Quezon further stated that we are currently considering discussing the textile industry issue when the parliament meets in July. We do not want to raise the living standards of the Filipino people, but we want to find a way to prevent the American textile industry from losing the Philippine market. However, this matter has not been thoroughly considered. (National Telegram, 12th)

Japanese Cabinet: Four Elders Meeting Agrees on Steps to Form Deliberation Council 43

(Tokyo) Regarding the issue of establishing a Cabinet Deliberation Council, the four elders of the Cabinet, Prime Minister Okada, Minister of Communications Tokonami, Minister of Commerce Machida, and Minister of Finance Takahashi, gathered at the Prime Minister's official residence at 11:00 this morning and did not adjourn until 1:30 in the afternoon. It is heard that the following matters were decided today:

(1) According to the regulations of the Cabinet Deliberation Council, Prime Minister Okada will serve as the Chairman of the Council, and Minister of Finance Takahashi will serve as the Vice Chairman.

(2) Whether the laws of the Council need to be submitted to the Privy Council for approval before they can be established will be further studied to resolve the question.

(3) Former Prime Minister Saito Makoto and former Minister of Interior Yamamoto Tatsuo have promised to serve as members. Other members and the Director of the Investigation Bureau will be selected by the three ministers Takahashi, Tokonami, and Machida and Chief Secretary Yoshida, and recommended to Prime Minister Okada for appointment. (China United Press, 13th)

Japanese Population to Exceed 100 Million 44

(Tokyo) The results of the Fourth National Census of Japan were announced in the Official Gazette today, and will be implemented from 00:00 on October 1 this year. This survey is not the major survey conducted every ten years in accordance with the law, but an interim report of the simplified survey. In 1930, the total population of Japan, including the colonies, reached 90,396,043. If calculated based on an average increase of 2 million per year, the total population will exceed 100 million. (Den Tsushin, 13th)

Major Fire at Taiwan Oil Well; Extinguished After Seven Days 45

Taipei. The No. 32 well of the Jinshui Oil Field, Taiwan's deepest oil well, suddenly caught fire on the evening of the 11th. 100 million cubic feet of kerosene were sprayed out per day, turning into flames as high as 40 meters, presenting a tragic scene. All kinds of machinery were melted by the heat. The cause of the fire was that when the oil well was dug to a depth of 1,500 meters, methane gas suddenly erupted, touching the power lines and causing the fire. Fire prevention work is now being carried out with utmost effort, but it will take seven days to extinguish the fire. The damage is estimated to be no less than one million yuan. (Nichiren, 12th)

International Commercial Telegrams—April 13, Special Commercial Telegram from Reuters— 50

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today is 144 shillings and 2.5 pence, up 1.5 pence.

London Silver Market: This morning, the market situation was very uncertain before the close of the morning session. The East and speculators bought or sold in large quantities, and the transactions were quite large. The spot price was 31.3125 pence, unchanged. The futures price was 31.375 pence, down 0.0625.

Mount Isa Silver: This morning, the futures prices did not change much. The opening price was 25 pounds lower than yesterday's closing price.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was quiet, and the fluctuations were not large. The British-American exchange rate opened at $4.845, down 0.25 from yesterday's American-British closing price. Later, the price hovered between $4.8475 and $4.845. The closing price was $4.84625, up 0.125 from the closing price.

British-French: The opening price was 73.25 francs, down 9 pounds from yesterday's closing price. The closing price was 73.26 francs, up 1 pound.

Cotton and Wheat

New York Cotton Market: Today, the opening price rose by about 4.5 cents per bale. The sales from local and southern areas were absorbed by foreign demand. The demand gradually ran out before noon, and the southern pressure did not decrease, so the price trended downward.

Chicago Wheat: The opening price was slightly lower today, but the drought in the southwest remained, so the wheat market price was still able to support it. The situation in Winnipeg was stable, and the price was unchanged.

Liverpool Wheat: This morning, it rebounded. The closing price for July futures was 5 shillings and 9.625 pence, up 1.125 pence from yesterday's closing price.

Liverpool Cotton: Higher today, the closing price for July futures was 6.38, up 6 pounds from yesterday's closing price.

Rubber

London: Today's market situation was stable. At noon, the transaction price for July-September futures was 5.75 pence, the same as yesterday's closing price.

New York: Today's futures market was still stable. The opening price was about 5-7 pounds higher than yesterday's closing price. The stability of the London market and the improvement of the labor strike in the American rubber industry were the main reasons for the slight increase in the market price here.

Ministry of Communications Formulates Rules for Radio Charges for Ships 55

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications has formulated rules for radio charges for ships, consisting of 14 articles, which have been promulgated. All telegrams transmitted by ship radio stations to coast radio stations or other ship radio stations are collectively referred to as ship radio telegrams, and are divided into domestic ship telegrams and international ship telegrams. Domestic charges are collected in national currency, and international charges are collected in gold francs. The price list for telegrams will be specified separately. (Special Dispatch, 13th)

China-France Savings Association Proposes Alternative Measures for Prize-Linked Savings 56

(Nanjing) For the method of banning prize-linked savings, the China-France Savings Association proposed an alternative method. All those who have previously joined the savings plan will be transferred to a special savings account from the month the prize draws are discontinued. For those who originally saved 15 yuan, 3.75 yuan will be deducted each month. For those who originally saved 12 yuan, 3 yuan will be deducted each month, and so on. The repayment period will be shortened from 15 years to 14 years. It has been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval. It is heard that the International Savings Society is also planning alternative measures. (Special Dispatch, 13th)
