Notes on Northwest Inspection 88

— Special Correspondent Geng Ya of this Newspaper

Pingliang, the First City of Eastern Gansu

Pingliang is the most prosperous area among the seventeen counties in eastern Gansu, leaning against the Liupan Mountains in the west, controlling the Longban area in the south, reaching Ningxia in the north, and connecting to Chang'an in the east. The city borders the right side of the Jing River, with tall buildings and a hub of vehicles and horses. The markets are prosperous, and industry and commerce are relatively developed. The county is 160 li long from east to west and 110 li wide from north to south, covering an area of approximately 170,000 square li, with a population of approximately 240,000. The annual tax revenue and grain revenue total approximately 28,000 yuan. The main product is wheat. Thanks to irrigation from mountain springs and the Jing River, it has been self-sufficient in recent years and can also be exported to Shaanxi or southern Gansu. The next product is fur. Local sheepskin is sold for eight yuan per piece, which can be used to make greatcoats. The wool is interwoven diagonally, resembling floating silk from outside Lanzhou. It is soft, warm, and very suitable for winter clothing in the Northwest. There are also Haiyuan fur coats, which can be used as Ningxia beach fur. Shops sell both, and it is difficult to distinguish between genuine and fake. Commerce was very developed in the 13th and 14th years of the Republic, but gradually declined after the great drought in the 17th and 18th years and the conflict between Sun Weiru and Chen Guizhang in the 20th year. Moreover, due to convenient transportation, goods from Shaanxi and Lanzhou can be transported directly, and it has recently lost its position as a hub for passenger and freight traffic. However, the number of opium businesses has increased from dozens to over two hundred, showing a distorted development, not including opium dens. Opium addicts account for approximately 30%.

Industry includes the government-run Minsheng Factory, which produces carpets, towels, and leggings. The Fulong Match Company was founded by Zhang Dingchen, the former garrison commander. After several suspensions, it is now maintained by the Chamber of Commerce and can barely produce goods. The Coal Company produces coal worth approximately 10,000 yuan annually. Compared to Minsheng and Fulong, it is promising. The most abundant coal reserves are found in the Tugudui mining area. According to mining experts, the coal reserves can supply the entire Gansu Province for 300 years. Currently, most of the fuel in eastern Gansu comes from this area. However, due to limited capital, manual mining is mostly used, resulting in a shortage of supply. Moreover, many good coal seams have excessive water content that cannot be drained, causing the goods to be abandoned on the ground. In the future, when the Longhai Railway extends westward, converting to mechanical mining will bring unlimited profits.

This spring, the price of wheat flour is three yuan per hundred jin, wheat is seven or eight jiao per dou (40 jin), meat is nine jin per yuan, clear oil is ten jin per yuan, and cabbage is four hundred jin per yuan. Textiles and daily necessities come from the east, and their prices are about one and a half times higher than in Tianjin and Shanghai. Large pieces of coal weigh 70 to 80 jin per "zhuang" (sack) and cost over three mao, while slag coal costs two mao. Transporting coal to the city by donkey costs one yuan per hundred jin. It is said that the Central First Division unit in Tianshui, southern Gansu, requires five yuan per person per month for food, while three yuan is sufficient here. The standard of living is on average half that of Lanzhou, but it is still common for people to struggle to make ends meet, especially with the collapse of the rural economy. Merchants dare not extend credit to rural areas, and there is no cooperative organization. Farmers have no access to loans and have to sell livestock and grain cheaply to meet urgent needs, making their livelihoods extremely difficult.

There are three provincial schools: the Second Middle School, the Seventh Normal School, and the Second Girls' Normal School. The Second Middle School has over 400 students, while the other two schools each have 120-130 students. The county has eleven elementary schools and three affiliated public schools. Few parents know to send their children to school, and due to economic difficulties, many drop out halfway. Most students are from poor families, especially in elementary schools. Therefore, all schools waive tuition fees. The graduation exam held at the end of the 23rd year had a passing rate of 80%, which is a considerable achievement. However, it is regrettable that such a large city lacks facilities such as a public education hall, library, and reading room. It is said that very few people subscribe to the "New Long Daily."

There are scenic spots such as Willow Lake, Parks, Kongtong Mountain, and the Dragon King Temple. Willow Lake is located below the north city and was formerly the Willow Lake Academy, now converted into the Seventh Normal School. I once visited it and saw the words "Willow Lake" on the plaque of the gate (i.e., the school gate), with a couplet on the right saying "People rest by the willow" and on the upper left saying "Spring comes on the lake." Upon entering, I saw the plaque "Willow Lake Academy," originally inscribed by Zuo Zongtang. The garden has Hanyutang and Leyuting pavilions, where one can sit and rest. The scenery is beautiful, with willow colors and lake light being the best features. Dozens of steps in front of the garden, a spring gurgles from the ground, with green leaves growing in it, resembling plantain. It drifts along the stream, with the same color in winter and summer. The city is built on a slope, and the northeast gates are upward when entering the city. Small carts and rickshaws require a lot of effort. The Zhongshan Bridge has protruding road surfaces on both ends, making it inconvenient to go up and down. If the road surface can be filled in and the slope reduced, it would greatly benefit traffic. I visited County Magistrate Wang Kai in the evening and talked until about eight o'clock before returning to the Northwest Hotel. Upon exiting the east gate, although there were guards, there was no light in the darkness. I groped in the dark, worrying about falling. After passing Zhongshan Bridge, the city was crowded with people, and the traffic was heavy. People with opium faces were shouting, "Who wants a pair of padded pants?" "Who wants the key to the general dismounting?" The shouts were deafening. However, it was quiet soon after nightfall. As I approached the hotel, people were performing rituals to redeem the souls of the dead, setting up incense tables on the street, with bright lights. Taoist priests were playing flutes and cymbals, reciting scriptures, and offering a paper tablet with the words "True Nature of the Ma Family, Soul Position." A middle-aged man knelt beside him, continuously burning paper money in a bucket, with a kitchen knife placed on the rim of the bucket. Also, after the death of people in Anxi, Taoist priests must recite scriptures to the well, tie a copper cup with a red thread, and sprinkle water in all directions. After burning half of the paper money, they throw it into the air, relying on the heat to fly high and dance like ash butterflies. I don't know what the purpose is. When I returned to the hotel and went to bed, the sound of gongs and drums from the theater was still carried by the wind, becoming clearer and clearer. This is perhaps the only embellishment of the night.

Panic in Osaka Meat Market Due to Impact of China-Japan Exchange Rate and Interruption of Shandong Cattle Imports 89

The Osaka Asahi Shimbun reported on the 5th of this month that due to the recent increase in silver prices, there has been a sudden change in the China-Japan exchange rate. Most of the beef consumed in Osaka is imported from Qingdao, averaging over 50,000 heads per year. This beef is inexpensive and of good quality, sufficient to meet the needs of the people of Osaka. Unexpectedly, due to the exchange rate relationship with China this year, imports have been completely interrupted. The number of Manchurian cattle imported from Dalian and Lushun is only 700 heads. Osaka, which has the largest beef consumption in Japan, has been severely affected by this blow, creating a significant problem. The total beef consumption in Japan is approximately 300,000 heads per year, while domestic production is only 110,000 heads. If this continues, it will be necessary to slaughter domestic bulls to replace Qingdao cattle. Although approximately 70,000 heads have been imported from Korea as an emergency measure recently, it is still not enough to meet social needs.

Xu Yuanquan Reports Breakthrough of Xiao-He Bandits Nest, Heavy Losses for Bandits in the Tower-Crouch Battle, Bandits Surrounded and Fleeing to Sichuan 90

Hankou Dispatch: The remnants of the He Long and Xiao Ke bandits have been entrenched in western Hunan for four months. Last month, the Hunan and Hubei armies, led by He Jian and Xu Yuanquan respectively, launched a joint campaign to suppress them, repeatedly thwarting the bandit offensive. The Hunan army first captured Dayong, and the Hubei army also captured Sangzhi. Recently, Yongshun County was also recovered by the Hunan army, which joined forces with the Hubei army to pursue the bandits. Due to overwhelming pressure, the bandits moved the pseudo-Sichuan-Guizhou-Hunan-Hunan Soviet government to Tawa in the northern part of Yongshun, and the main force was also concentrated there, resisting the Hunan and Hubei armies on one side and attempting to flee west into Sichuan on the other. The National Army has established a four-pronged encirclement plan. Heavy troops are stationed in western Hubei and eastern Sichuan to block the bandits. The He-Xu troops in Hunan are responsible for pursuing and suppressing the bandits. The Tawa bandit nest was broken by the Guo Rudong division of the Xu's forces on the 8th. The remnants of the bandits were in a state of panic. Yesterday, the Headquarters received a victory telegram from Xu, which stated: "It has been confirmed that the Yu Shen Division of the Third Column of my unit captured the bandit positions on the north and south highlands of Huangshijie. Subsequently, on the same day, they continued to attack the Tawa bandit nest. According to reports from Guo Rudong and Luo Qijiang, the commander and deputy commander of the team, respectively, Luo Qijiang's Independent 34th Brigade of our vanguard arrived at Lengshui Village at noon, due to rain and slippery roads. About a thousand bandits were stationed on the road to Tawa, east of Tawa, and on the mountains inside. Also, about two thousand bandits who had fled from Yongshun this morning were stationed there. Brigade Commander Luo led two regiments to launch a fierce attack on the bandits in Changxi. The bandits resisted fiercely, and after climbing the mountains and fighting hard, they were finally defeated at 4 PM and fled towards Tawa. Our army took advantage of the situation to pursue them towards Tawa, and sent another battalion to pursue the bandits who fled towards Sanjiatian, inflicting heavy blows. The bandit forces weakened, and fled towards Shaba in a panic. As it was getting dark and the situation of the bandits in front was not clear, the brigade maintained contact with the bandits at the Tawa Pass, only three li from Tawa, throughout the night. On the morning of the same day, they attacked the north side of Tawa. Unexpectedly, about two thousand bandits who had fled from Cheping Zuoyan Slope, about fifteen li from Tawa, launched a fierce attack on the line of our Luo Brigade in the morning. After the brigade fought hard, charging back and forth fiercely, the bandits still stubbornly resisted. Commander Guo urgently ordered the 76th Brigade of the 26th Division to rush to the rescue and cooperate in the attack. After another fierce battle until noon, the bandits were finally defeated. The two brigades immediately followed up and advanced, completely occupying Tawa at 1 PM. The bandits fled towards Longjiazhai. In this battle, the Luo Brigade killed more than 500 bandits, captured more than 100 rifles, captured more than 80 bandit soldiers from the fake 538th and 54th Regiments alive, captured the fake Minister of Food, and seized countless bandit flags and printed matter, rescued more than 100 hostages, and gave each hostage five jiao and five sheng of rice to help them return home. The brigade suffered more than 20 officer and soldier casualties. The 76th Brigade of the 26th Division also killed hundreds of bandits and captured more than ten rifles. Overall, this battle was a testament to the bravery and agility of the officers and soldiers. Brigade Commander Luo Qijiang personally supervised the battle, commanding effectively. The rapid support of Brigade Commander Zhu Zaitang of the 26th Division was commendable." (12th)

Beiping-Tianjin Garrison Command Burns Large Quantity of Narcotics — Twelve Drug Dealers Executed in Succession — 91

Beiping Dispatch: This morning (10th) at 10:00 AM, the Beiping-Tianjin Garrison Command held a narcotics burning ceremony in front of the Temple of Heaven. A high tower and straw shed was erected in front of the temple, surrounded by soldiers. Representatives from various agencies and groups, including Xu Zhizhong, Chief of the Law Enforcement Section of the Gendarmerie Command, Cui Nanshan, representative of the Ping-Sui Railway, Leng Jiaji, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Guo Shizhen, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Song Yanji, representative of the Fifth Outer District, Liu Futang, representative of the Military Sub-Committee, and Deng Qiupu, representative of the Municipal Government, attended the ceremony to supervise. Yao Zhenyi, Adjutant of the Beiping-Tianjin Garrison Command, Xiao Zhengqing, Chief of the Logistics Department, and Teng Shaozhou, Chief of the Secretariat Section, led over 20 adjutants and guards in two large trucks, carrying narcotics to the site. Approximately 700 to 800 people gathered to watch. After the participants gathered, Teng Shaozhou, Section Chief of the department, reported on the significance and process of burning narcotics, briefly stating that today, the headquarters, by order of the Military Sub-Committee, will burn the narcotics related to serious narcotics cases. He briefly reported the details of the process to everyone: On July 13, 23rd year, the headquarters received an order from Chairman Chiang, together with the Gendarmerie Command, the Public Security Bureau, the governments of the Dawan and Daxing Counties, the Ping-Sui, Ping-Han, and Bei-Ning Railways, and the joint military-police office, to conduct the search and arrest of serious narcotics addicts. In total, there were 84 cases and 146 narcotics criminals. Except for 12 people who were approved by the Military Sub-Committee for execution, 40 were sentenced to imprisonment, and 74 were sent to serious narcotics rehabilitation centers, the remaining 5 cases and 11 criminals have been transferred to the Public Security Bureau on December 2, in accordance with Chairman Chiang's telegram order. After that, narcotics cases will be handled independently by the city and county. However, the narcotics confiscated during the period handled by the headquarters from July 13 to December 2 were also considerable. For the sake of closure, the Military Sub-Committee was approved to conduct the burning ceremony in front of the Temple of Heaven this morning. After the report, the burning began in public, including four large bags of lactose, one willow bundle of opium, and one large cabinet of white powder. On the spot, Yao Zhenyi, Adjutant of the Garrison Command, used a knife to cut open the entire package of opium to ensure credibility. The burning was completed at 11:00 AM. (10th)

Ministry of Industry Releases Mining Report on Actively Rescuing National Coal and Unifying the Mining and Management Rights of Gold Mines 92

Beijing Dispatch: The Ministry of Industry is actively carrying out the rescue of national coal and the reorganization of the mining industry. The Mining Department of the Ministry released a written report yesterday on the progress. The following is a record of it:

Rescuing National Coal: The Ministry continues to promote the rescue of national coal in accordance with past policies. All measures beneficial to coal operators are taken. Issues such as streamlining transportation, reducing transportation costs, and exempting additional taxes have been successively consulted with the Ministry of Railways, the Ministry of Finance, and the political organs of various provinces, and considerable results have been achieved. However, since the equipment of coal mines in various provinces is mostly incomplete and costs vary, to make up for deficiencies, it is necessary to understand the actual situation. The Ministry has dispatched mining investigators Zhang Baoshi, specialist Chen Wei, and members of the National Coal Relief Committee Zhang Hu et al. to investigate the coal mines along the Ping-Han and Ping-Sui railways, to comprehensively investigate the internal organization, engineering equipment, transportation status, and recent business conditions of each mine, in order to comprehensively plan and prevent loopholes, so that domestic coal can be fully developed. The investigation lasted for five months, and the areas covered include: the Liuhegou, Yili, Zhonghe, Lincheng, Sanfeng, Jizhong, Xingbao, and Xiezhong mines along the Ping-Han Railway; the Datong, Baojin, Jinbei, Tongbao, Baoheng, Baoxing, Tianxing, Houfeng, Zhaizhang, Mentougou, and Zhongying mines along the Ping-Sui Railway; the Zhongfu Company on the Daoqing Railway; and the Jingxing, Zhengfeng, Yangquan, Baojin, Pingji, Jianchang, and Guangmao mines on the Zhengtai Railway; The Minsheng and Qiugou Mines on the Longhai Railway. In total, there are 26 mines above, and a list comparing the overview, coal quality analysis, and production, transportation, and sales conditions of each mine has been compiled. In addition, a report on the quantity of coal sold in major ports such as Shanghai, Tianjin, and Hankou has been compiled separately and submitted to the Ministry for review. As for how the mines should unite and how the costs should be reduced, a fundamental solution can be found after the National Coal Relief Committee prepares a plan and submits it for review.

Reorganizing Gold Mines: (1) The Ministry, according to reports, discovered a gold mine in the Yangtigou area in the south of Daixian, northern Shanxi, which covers a large area. The Shanxi Provincial Department of Construction has established a gold mine management office and drafted 19 provisional measures for the area. It has issued a special order to the Department of Construction to investigate and ascertain whether the gold mine discovered in the Yangtigou area is abundant in reserves, what the structure of the ore bed is, and what the mineral composition is, and report it to the Ministry accordingly. It has also ordered the Department to submit the specific development plan that it has drafted for review. (2) The Ministry, according to reports, heard that the Shandong Provincial Government plans to establish a gold mining bureau to mine the gold mines in Yishui, Zhaoyuan, Pingdu, and other counties. It immediately drafted an order to inform the Department that if it is indeed considering this plan, it should submit the plan, its scope, and detailed information for review, in order to unify mining administration and bring it within the scope of the law.

Restricting Small Mines: The Ministry believes that small mines in various provinces have the greatest impact on the rights of large mines. If they are allowed to continue to be divided and registered without any restrictions, it is feared that the entire coalfield will be excavated and fragmented. Those who apply for mining rights legally in the future will not be able to start work, and it will be more difficult to remedy the development in the future, causing harm to mining interests. Moreover, according to the Mining Association, it has requested the strict formulation of measures to ban small mines, so that progress can be made and safety can be ensured. The Ministry is currently studying how to carefully draft these banning measures. The regulations should be based on the premise of not violating the Mining Law and not hindering large mines, while also taking into account the customs of the indigenous peoples of various provinces, so that the proposed measures can be easily implemented. In accordance with the provisions of Article 59 of the Mining Law, only those small mines in places with inconvenient transportation, or with very small reserves, or in areas where mining is underdeveloped, can be approved. No people are allowed to establish small mining rights within the large coal mines that have been established in various provinces, such as Zhongyu, Liuhegou, Cixian, Lincheng, Jingxing Jiawang, Huaiyuan, Pohe, Zhongyuan, and the Kailuan and Luda mines.

Page 11

Investigating Iron and Manganese: The Ministry believes that there are many iron and manganese resources in our country. After dispatching personnel to investigate, it has been calculated that (1) the Chaling iron mine has an estimated reserve of 3 to 4 million tons; (2) the iron ore in Hengshi area of Xixiang County, Ningxiang County (with an iron content of more than 50%) has about 8 million tons of high-grade ore, and there are also several million tons of inferior ore; (3) geological maps have been drawn for the manganese mine in Leping, Jiangxi and the Yongxin iron mine; (4) geological and mineral resources in Yunnan have been investigated by dispatched personnel and are still ongoing; (5) the coal mine in Mengxian Yezhenzhen, western Henan contains oil. The Henan Geological Survey Institute has dispatched personnel to investigate and has obtained results. The Henan Provincial Department of Construction has been ordered to forward the investigation report, the original coal, and the crude oil samples from the test results to the Ministry for reference. (Daily News)

Zhe Qu County: Coal Mine Discovered in Guoxi Mountain 93

Quzhou Dispatch: In Guoxi Mountain, Yuchun Village, in the western part of the county, sand veins run crisscross, with many layers of large rocks. The area is rich in coal deposits. Unfortunately, the villagers have not paid attention to exploration and mining, preventing the development of this resource. Recently, a farmer named Mao Rongbang from the village, due to a difficult livelihood, independently reclaimed mountain land there for planting miscellaneous grains to increase production. Not long after the start of his work, he suddenly discovered piles of coal in the depths of the mountain land. Upon further excavation, even more inexhaustible mineral resources were revealed. Mao was overjoyed and decided to first try mining for a month. After achieving good results, he planned to raise shares and hire workers for full-scale mining. Simultaneously, he submitted a request to the county government to dispatch personnel to conduct an on-site survey. After the county government dispatched an autonomous roving assistant to inspect the mountain, a detailed report on the area of the coal region, the shallow and deep coal seams, has been submitted to the county government for record. (9th)

Pseudo-Datong Company Formally Sells Pseudo-National Certificates, Directly Under the Pseudo-Ministry of Civil Affairs, Tianjin Has an Office, Capital is 500,000 Yuan 94

Tianjin Dispatch: The pseudo-organization restricted the passage of our citizens out of the pass, effective April 1st. The pseudo-Ministry of Civil Affairs has newly promulgated fourteen regulations, stipulating that anyone leaving the pass must purchase a pseudo-entry certificate. The Datong Company, responsible for selling these pseudo-entry certificates, was originally an agency temporarily established by the Japanese to provide relief to drifters. Now, it has been formally reorganized as an agency directly under the Police Department of the pseudo-Ministry of Civil Affairs. The company has offices in Shanhaiguan, Gubeikou, Xifengkou, Malanyu, Panjiakou, and Yiyuan, all assisted by resident Japanese military police and pseudo-border police. Initially, each pseudo-entry certificate was sold for two pseudo-yuan. From April 2nd, the price was reduced to five jiao. Recently, despite the strict restrictions, the number of people leaving the pass has not decreased. Therefore, the price has been suddenly increased to two yuan per certificate, and office hours are set from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM and 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM. As a result, whether traveling by train or not, those leaving the pass face delays and must stay in Yuguan for one or two days before they can purchase a pseudo-entry certificate. In Gubeikou and other places, which are not crucial transportation hubs, the company is even more arbitrarily difficult, intending to prevent our citizens from leaving the pass. In Tianjin, the company's office appeared half a month ago, located at No. 36 Naniwa Street, Japanese Concession, on the right bank of the Fourth River. Passengers traveling by boat from the Tianjin pier to areas outside the pass must purchase a pseudo-entry certificate from this company before boarding. Even those traveling by train purchase pseudo-entry certificates in Tianjin in advance to avoid waiting at inns upon arrival in Shanhaiguan. As a result, many people go to purchase the certificates every day. The office hours of the pseudo-office are the same as those in Yuguan. Generally, those purchasing pseudo-certificates arrive very early to wait. When the doors of the pseudo-office open, Japanese concession military police and concession criminal police officers go to maintain order, using rattan whips and wooden sticks to beat the crowd, forcing them to line up and advance in order. After entering the room, they must squat on the ground, not allowed to speak or spit. When approaching the purchase window, a Japanese person interrogates their name, origin, and other details, and they must provide the name of a guarantor within the pass, which is also filled in on the certificate. Therefore, due to the cumbersome procedures, very few people can purchase the certificate on the same day. If someone privately bribes the military police or criminal police officers with a few yuan, they can be placed at the front of the line to purchase first. However, the Japanese interrogation has no set rules. Sometimes, they ask about family history for three generations, and those who hesitate slightly are beaten by the military police or criminal police, even to the point of breaking whips and sticks. Because those who go to purchase the pseudo-entry certificates are mostly laborers from Hebei and Shandong, determined to go outside the pass, they endure inhumane treatment and adopt an attitude of resignation. In addition to selling pseudo-entry certificates, the Tianjin office of the Datong Company also handles intelligence affairs for the pseudo-national intelligence agency. The intelligence officer is a Japanese named Aoki Daisaku, assisted by Tomita Kimura, Mino Ota, Nitta Ryo, and Sakano Yoichiro. It also employs more than thirty Chinese traitors who work secretly in the Pingjin-Ji-Lu area, responsible for various intelligence gathering tasks. All matters related to contact between the pseudo-nation and the Chinese traitors in the Pingjin area are handled by the pseudo-intelligence agency. Therefore, the organization of the Tianjin office of the pseudo-Datong Company is not simple and deserves attention. (7th)

Changchun Dispatch: In order to implement regulations to control laborers "outside the country," the Japanese and puppets have reorganized the Datong Company into a Japanese-puppet joint venture company with a capital of 500,000 Japanese yen. Its business involves handling the "identity certificates" of laborers outside the country and engaging in "recruitment, supply, transportation, protection, and relief" of laborers, as well as other matters. The new president is Japanese Igarashi Fusakichi, and the general manager is Mino Tomoyoshi. After the reorganization and inauguration, the company is actively expanding its business. Currently, in addition to branches in Changchun Seitoku and the Japanese Concession of Tianjin, it has branch offices in Tianjin, Shanhaiguan, Xifengkou, Gubeikou, Tanggu, Qingdao Zhifu, Longkou, Weihaiwei, Shenyang, Changchun, Andong, and Yingkou. (Northeast News Agency)

New Transport Association Issues Organizational Outline of Labor Service Corps and Preliminary Implementation Plan for the Threefold Transformation of Life 95

Preliminary Implementation Plan for the Militarization of Life

Implementation Principles: 1. Spiritual Aspect: Arouse the spirit of martialism and patriotism. 2. Action Aspect: Pay attention to quick and orderly actions. 3. Lifestyle Aspect: Implement a simple and unadorned lifestyle. 4. Habit Aspect: Cultivate the habit of obeying discipline. (Explanation) This movement includes personal appearance and behavior as well as social order and customs, cultivating good habits of distinguishing right from wrong, martial spirit, perseverance, hard work, love of country, emphasis on credibility, emphasis on simplicity, advocacy of thrift, adherence to discipline, and respect for time. It also implements military law, popularizes military knowledge, cultivates a neat and unified social order, and thoroughly eliminates the past flaccid, loose, regressive, decadent, and lax customs.

Implementation Guidelines: 1. Government Employees: (1) When hearing the Party and national anthem and the raising and lowering of the national flag, they must stand at attention on the spot. (2) Implement military training and military management. (3) Absolutely obey the orders of superiors. (4) Wear uniforms uniformly. (5) Clothing should be neat and unadorned, and food should be clean and simple. (6) Meetings and appointments must absolutely observe the time. (7) Have regular routines for daily life. (8) Promote extracurricular sports. (9) Luggage and utensils should be simple. (10) Promote cold water bathing. 2. Teachers and Students of Various Schools: (1) Intensify military training for students, and all teachers must participate. (2) All secondary schools and above must raise and lower the national flag on time, and daily life must be conducted with bugle calls, and military management must be implemented. (3) Hold drills and reviews. (4) Absolutely obey the orders of superiors. (5) Teachers and students must wear uniforms uniformly and wear badges. (6) Promote extracurricular sports. (7) When entering and leaving the playground, one must walk in an orderly manner. (8) Both inside and outside the classroom, there must be silence. (9) Do not take a car or use alternative transportation for short distances. (10) No smoking or drinking. (11) No spitting or wearing hats askew or dragging shoes. (12) Absolutely prohibit going to dance halls to dance, and no entering amusement parks without the permission of teachers or parents. 3. Citizens: (1) All males aged 16 to 40 should receive simple military training uniformly in accordance with the methods of training citizens and be periodically examined and reviewed. (2) Implement air defense drills, fire drills, and first aid drills to train the public in wartime life and first aid knowledge. (3) On national memorial days, households should separately hang flags to celebrate or mourn. (4) Investigate households, train Baojia, and hold a Baojia chief memorial week. (5) Prescribe the daily life and work hours of citizens. (6) Promote various outdoor sports. (7) Implement early morning cleaning and sweeping, supervised by police and Baojia chiefs in each district. (8) Do not talk loudly in theaters, teahouses, restaurants, and on boats and vehicles. (9) At docks, stations, and public places, one must walk in an orderly manner. (10) Wedding and funeral ceremonies should be simple. (11) Prohibit unnecessary social events. (12) Clothing should be neat and simple, and food should be simple and clean. (13) Meetings and appointments must absolutely observe the time. (14) Develop citizen attire and eliminate strange and outlandish clothing. (15) Establish prostitute areas and prescribe dress codes and identification. (16) Abide by government laws.

Preliminary Implementation Plan for the Transformation of Life into Production

Implementation Principles: 1. Financial Aspect: Advocate thrift and savings, striving to increase social resources. 2. Labor Aspect: Focus on cherishing time and operations, striving to increase quantity and enrich quality. 3. Material Aspect: Focus on promoting domestic goods, striving to conserve and cherish goods. (Explanation) This movement aims to restore the virtues of frugality, thrift, valuing time, and diligence of our nation, laying a foundation for the further transformation of life into production in the future.

Implementation Guidelines: 1. Thrift: A. Eliminate waste in weddings, funerals, and birthday banquets. (1) Gifts should be economical. (1) Public officials should strictly abide by the "Provisional Regulations on Wasteful Weddings, Funerals, and Birthday Banquets for Public Officials" stipulated by the National Government. (2) For non-public officials, the maximum value of gifts should not exceed one yuan. (3) Gift certificates in the form of various savings plans should be used. (2) Banquets should be simple. (1) The dishes at banquets should be simple and reasonably arranged, and the cost per table should not exceed twelve yuan. (3) Avoid lavish responses. (1) Use tea and snacks to entertain guests at celebrations and funerals. (2) Do not prepare return gifts upon receiving gifts. (3) Do not use cigarettes to entertain guests. B. Restrict unnecessary social events. (1) Congratulations should be restricted. (1) Those under the age of sixty should not hold banquets to celebrate their birthdays. (2) No gifts should be accepted for the birth of children, except from relatives. (2) Do not send out notices indiscriminately. (1) For weddings, funerals, and birthdays, do not send out notices or invitations indiscriminately, except to relatives or those with genuine affection or friendship. (3) Eliminate ceremonial guards. (1) Do not use feudal or meaningless ceremonial guards for weddings and funerals. 2. Savings: A. Stipulate savings methods for employees of government agencies, schools, stores, and companies. (1) Specify savings categories. (1) The minimum amount that each person should save each month should be from one percent to four percent of their income. B. Promote group savings. (1) Organize various mutual aid societies. (2) Establish charitable granaries. (3) Cooperative insurance. C. Promote postal savings and eliminate prize-winning savings institutions without a solid foundation or with gambling characteristics. 3. Cooperation: A. Approve various cooperative societies. (1) Credit cooperatives. (2) Consumer cooperatives. (3) Marketing cooperatives. (4) Construction cooperatives. (5) Other cooperatives. 4. Labor: A. Maximize labor efficiency. (1) Cherish time. (1) Promote early rising. (2) Strictly observe working hours. (3) Strictly prohibit gambling and time-wasting games. (2) Utilize spare time. (1) Engage in effective work such as land reclamation, bridge repair, dredging of ponds, and forest cultivation. (2) Organize labor literacy education. (3) Send out newspaper and book vendors. (4) Organize firefighting. (5) Organize first aid. (3) Promote family operations. B. Promote labor occupations. (1) Organize employment services. (2) Promote family side jobs. (3) Organize annual worker training. 5. Cherish Materials: A. Promote domestic goods. (1) Daily necessities, if there are no domestic products, must be purchased from domestic goods. (2) Public agency supplies, wherever domestic products are available, are absolutely prohibited from purchasing foreign goods. B. Cherish public property. (1) General affairs management should be rationalized, and it is prohibited to use agency supplies for non-official purposes. (2) Accounting and disbursement should be as economical as possible. C. Sort out and utilize waste materials. D. Promote thin coffins and quick burials, and build public cemeteries.

Preliminary Implementation Plan for the Transformation of Life into Art

Implementation Principles: 1. Self-Cultivation Aspect: Strive for rigor and humility. 2. Interpersonal Aspect: Strive for sincerity and generosity. 3. Action Aspect: Strive for speed and precision. 4. Material Aspect: Strive for frugality and integrity. (Explanation) Art refers to skill, and technique refers to method. The transformation of life into art seeks reasonable skills and methods in life. This section divides life content into four categories: self-cultivation, interpersonal relations, action, and material things, and conducts preliminary artistic promotion to lay a considerable foundation for future movements.

Implementation Guidelines: 1. Self-Cultivation: A. Language: (1) Coarseness should be eliminated. (2) It should be simple and concise. (1) Avoid redundant words. (2) Public speaking should pay attention to time. (3) Emphasize key points. (3) It should be organized. (4) It should be honest and not deceitful. (1) Do not discuss others' shortcomings behind their backs. (2) Do not make excessive criticisms. B. Attitude: (1) It should be amiable. (1) One should smile when talking to others. (2) Do not be easily angered. (3) Always be optimistic. (2) It should be polite. (1) Good morning greeting. (2) Good night greeting. (3) Meeting greeting. (4) Farewell greeting. (5) Thank you greeting. (6) Apology greeting. (7) Request greeting. (Note: Separate regulations will be set for the above etiquette.) (3) It should be humble. (1) Accept loyal advice from others. (2) Do not exaggerate. (3) Do not be complacent. (4) Do not ridicule. C. Actions: (1) It should be dignified. (1) Do not speak carelessly. (2) Do not look around while walking. (2) It should be cautious. (1) Think before acting. (2) Deal with changes calmly. (3) It should be quick and accurate. (4) It should be energetic. (1) Finish today's work today. (2) Be strict with oneself at all times. (5) It should be consistently operational. (1) Constantly review past work. (2) There must be regular routines. (3) Sleep early and rise early. (6) It should be beneficial exercise. (1) At least participate in one type of sport skill. (2) Often travel to the countryside during leisure time. (3) Promote walking. (7) Strict adherence to time. (1) Always pay attention to the clock. (2) If one cannot make an appointment, one should declare in advance. D. Learning: (1) Self-improvement should be unceasing. (1) Develop good study habits. (2) Use time to read books and newspapers daily. (3) Should observe experiments and practices more. (1) You should learn from practice, and practice what you learn. E. Faith: (1) Should uphold the Three Principles of the People. (2) The revival of the nation and country should be the central cause. (3) Believe that individuals have the power to conquer the environment. 2. Interpersonal Relationships: A. Socializing: (1) It should be sincere. (1) Be loyal to one's duties when entrusted by others. (2) Do not praise to the face or speak ill behind one's back. (3) Do not blame others. (4) Respect other people's personalities. (2) It should be moderate. (1) Do not make friends indiscriminately. (2) Do not waste time or money. B. Guidance: (1) Guide others using educational methods. (2) Strict with attendance and do not condone. (3) Fully develop people's strengths. (4) Focus on children's education. C. Obedience: (1) Support the great leader. (2) Be respectful to superiors. (3) Implement orders faithfully. (4) Make contributions and offer suggestions when you see something is wrong. 3. Dealing with Matters: A. Service: (1) There should be a plan for doing things. (1) Search for materials. (2) Organize materials. (3) Raise questions. (4) Formulate plans. (2) Work hard in one's profession without wavering. (1) Work on time and rest on time. (2) Do not slack off arbitrarily. (3) Do not engage in miscellaneous business. (4) Do not be capricious. (3) Serve the public without expecting rewards. (4) Promote public literacy. B. Organization: (1) Develop the habit of living in groups. (1) Understand the interests of the group. (2) Observe group regulations. (3) Obey group discipline. (2) Should cooperate. (1) Should have a spirit of mutual assistance. (2) Should divide labor and cooperate. C. Rescue: (1) Should be compassionate. (1) Do not rejoice at the misfortune of others. (2) Relieve suffering and poverty. (2) Should stand up for what is right. D. Customs: (1) Promote respecting virtue and rewarding merit. (1) Commemorate virtuous predecessors and martyrs. (2) Praise those who have contributed to society. (2) Break superstitions. (1) Do not believe in feng shui. (2) Do not believe in witchcraft, divination, and fortune-telling. (3) Funerals and celebrations do not choose dates. (3) The celebration ceremonies should be simple and harmonious. (1) Wedding ceremony. (2) New Year's greeting. (3) Birthday celebration. (4) Other celebrations are determined separately. (4) Funeral and sacrificial ceremonies should be simple and solemn. (1) Promote thin coffins, quick burials, cremation, and public cemeteries. (2) The funeral and sacrificial ceremonies are determined separately. 4. Dealing with Things: A. Taking and Giving: (1) Taking and giving should be appropriate. (1) Be ashamed of taking unwarranted wealth. (2) Do not indiscriminately give or receive gifts. (3) Be ashamed of begging from people. (2) Taking and giving should be polite. (1) Ordinary recipients must express thanks. (2) The gift-giving ceremony is determined separately. (3) There should be a distinction between public and private. (1) Do not abuse public goods. (2) Cherish public property more than private property. (3) Do not use public property to do favors. B. Consumption: (1) Living place should be clean and hygienic. (1) Sweep frequently. (2) Toilets and kitchens should be separated far away. (3) Open up the sewers. (4) Ventilate the air and allow sunlight. (5) Plant flowers and trees in the yard. (2) Diet should be simple and nutritious. (1) Vegetables and meat should be properly combined. (2) Tableware should be clean and food should be clean. (3) Entertainment should be simple. (4) Smoking and drinking should be avoided. (3) Clothes should be simple, clean, practical. (1) The style should be simple and the materials should be domestic goods. (2) Laundry should be diligent and torn items must be repaired. (4) Use should strive for economy. (1) Incoming and outgoing payments must be counted. (Household bookkeeping is determined separately) (2) Live within your means. (3) Encourage savings. C. Sorting Out: (1) Using resources should strive for efficiency. (1) Always check whether items are applicable. (2) Repair immediately if there is slight damage. (3) Utilize machinery to save labor. (4) Utilize waste to create new items. (2) Dealing with objects should have scientific methods. (1) The placement of equipment and machinery should be in an appropriate location. (2) Documents should be organized using library cataloging methods. (3) Methods of general affairs accounting are determined separately. (4) Number and record items. (3) Transforming the environment should strive for beauty and practicality. (1) Formulate slogan and advertising formats. (2) Plan housing construction methods.

Songjiang: Man Selling Fried Dough Sticks Beaten to Death 96

Xu Baoting, a guest from Huayang Bridge, runs a fried dough stick shop. His partner, Wang Abao, from Changzhou, usually sells them around Deshenggang. On the afternoon of the first of this month, when Wang Abao was calling out to sell in Lu Liutu, the wife of a villager named Zhu Ajin asked to buy on credit, which was refused, and they started arguing. Villagers gathered and beat Wang Abao. After returning to the shop, his injuries flared up, and he was bedridden and moaning. His condition gradually worsened. On the ninth, the shop owner reported to the court for an examination of the injuries and sent him to Songjiang Hospital for treatment. He died of illness on the morning of the tenth. The town police reported to the prosecutor's office, and on the morning of today (the thirteenth), Prosecutor Liu, accompanied by Secretary Qian and an examining coroner, rushed to the scene. The examination revealed that the corpse had three injuries on its left arm, chest, and back. The coroner filled out the death certificate, instructed the coffin to be prepared, and awaited summons for the suspects to be interrogated. It is reported that the suspect in the case made a personal statement to the prosecutor when the deceased's injuries were examined and will be summoned by name.

Baozhang Leads Crowd to Obstruct River Work 97

The Duanshan River in Litahui spans the counties of Song, Jin, and Bing. When the Laiye Guild extended the proposal to dredge the Changshan River, it suggested dredging the Duanshan River as well. It was submitted to the Songjiang County Government and requested approval from Jinshan County. In accordance with the dredging work and river levy regulations, the township head of Litahui Township, Hu Chengian, was instructed to cooperate with the township head of Maoliu Township in Jinshan County to prepare. A report to commence work had already been submitted. However, on the afternoon of the eleventh, Yu Yayun, the sixth Baozhang of Maoliu Township in Jin County, led more than thirty villagers and damaged the first section of the Yangjing Dam, causing the water to flow back in. They also went to Zhu Yu's small teahouse in the town and advocated against the dredging of the river, forcing villagers to sign a petition. The dredging director, Hu Chengian, reported to the water patrol team stationed there, and they arrested Yu, who has already been sent to Song for interrogation.

Wei Dasheng, Guo Xixian, Chen Xianbang, Gao Qijie, and other officials of the Grain Tax Collection Office in this county embezzled more than 60,000 yuan of public funds. County Government Recovers Back Taxes 99

The county's land tax, from the Republic of China year 16 to year 22, actually owed by the people, totaled more than 100,000 yuan. Now, in order to rectify local finances, the county government specifically issued a notice to all property owners yesterday, requiring them to pay all taxes within two months. If they continue to delay, large households will be summoned and arrested, and small households will be ordered to be collected by each household. Large households who refuse to pay after being detained will have their land sealed and compensated, and township heads will be ordered to assist in the collection.

The Supervision Office of the County Public Security Bureau received a confidential report yesterday (the thirteenth) stating that Nian Zhaihao in Jiuchengli on Malu Road had established a red pill den for addicts to consume opium. Inspector Wang, upon receiving the report, dispatched Inspector Ge, leading police officers to search the premises. They also arrested Sun Zhangshi at No. 58 and took them to the bureau for interrogation.

Silk Factory Manager Arrested for Fraud 101

Yuan Hegao, a reporter for the Xin Wuxi News, recently built riverside buildings behind his residence in Huangniiqiaodu outside the South Gate. Yan Zichen, the former manager of the Yulun Silk Factory, was recently in a difficult situation due to business failures. Changzhou: Public Security Bureau Busts Drug Trafficking Organization 102

According to a secret report, the Wuyi Public Security Bureau learned that someone had organized a drug trafficking organization at the closed Laiyuan Hotel on the Renyu Bridge. Director Xu Baoguang sent all the personnel of the Supervision Office, Li Jingchun and others, with the police at about 10 am on the 12th to search the hotel in an unnoticed manner. They arrested Wang Mingchen, Shao Shutang, Xue Ronger, Zhou Zhengcai and other four drug traffickers in Room 8 of the hotel and found a package of heroin weighing 5 qian 4 fen on Shao Shutang. 195 yuan was found on Wang Mingchen. At the same time, the suspects Han Yinguan and Wang Hezhen were arrested in Room 2 and taken to the bureau together. After questioning by Section Chief Wang Chongxian, Han Yinguan was sent to the smoking cessation center for investigation, and Wang Hezhen was sent home by his mother because his Tongji was not disciplined. The four drug traffickers, Wang Mingchen and others, were sent to the county government for interrogation.

Zhenjiang, Jiangsu Province: Recent News on the Handling of Land Reporting 103

In this province, the land tax of various counties has traditionally been managed by general clerks and runners, resulting in deep-seated malpractices. Tax revenues have been consistently deficient. The provincial authorities, recognizing this, have decided to implement land reporting in batches to rectify the situation at its source. The first batch, including Zhenjiang, Liyang, Yixing, and Jiangyin counties, has already been completed, and a reformed collection system has been implemented. Banks now collect taxes, completely eliminating the past practice of clerks overcharging and embezzling. This has proven quite effective. The second batch includes over ten counties such as Jiangdu, Jintan, and Taicang. The land reporting in Jiangdu County has already been completed. The county government is currently reviewing and organizing the registers for each township, ensuring that each plot is clearly defined with distinct boundaries, and that the names and addresses of the landowners are accurate. This ensures that taxes can be accurately levied on a per-plot, per-household basis, eliminating the previous chaotic and complicated system. According to the reported results, although there are no precise acreage statistics available yet, based on the approximate figures reported by each district, the total arable land in the county is estimated to be over two million mu, exceeding the original registered farmland by over one hundred thousand mu. Jintan County has already completed the land number mapping and the register of taxpaying households, and the reporting process, which began some time ago, will soon be completed. Muyang, Suyu, and Pei counties have also begun reporting. Other counties, such as Yangzhou, Taicang, Jiangning, and Yancheng, are actively preparing and compiling information, and it is expected that they will all be completed by the end of June this year.

Nantong: Rescuing the Native Cloth Industry in Tongzhou 104

Native cloth in the Tongzhou region of northern Jiangsu is a crucial secondary occupation for farming families. Recently, the industry has been in decline, with sales plummeting, leading to the closure of weaving households in the villages. Local leaders are striving to revitalize the industry. In addition to hiring experts to improve the looms and establishing dyeing factories to produce higher quality products, they are also constructing a native cloth market to facilitate the inspection and elimination of inferior cloth, thereby safeguarding the reputation of Tongzhou cloth.

Gaoyou: Farmers Commit Suicide Due to Poverty 105

In the vicinity of the Zhu Family Township in the seventh district of this county, a farmer named Zhu Guisheng, approximately forty years old, and his wife, Wu, of similar age, were living in impoverished circumstances. Their son was working as a hired hand elsewhere. Due to the recent spring famine, their livelihood had become completely unsustainable, leading them to contemplate ending their lives. One night, while his wife was asleep, Zhu Guisheng hanged himself from the roof beam. This morning, Wu discovered his body upon waking, and her grief was overwhelming. It was a truly tragic scene.

Hangzhou: Major Fire at Henghe Bridge Yesterday Morning 106

At 12:10 AM on the 13th, a fire broke out at the home of Yang Ahuan, resident of No. 87, Dahe Xia, Henghe Bridge, Hangzhou. The fire, caused by carelessness, was quite fierce. Firefighters and other rescue personnel rushed to the scene and extinguished the blaze by 1:30 AM. A total of twelve two-story houses and three single-story houses were destroyed, with losses estimated at over 4,400 yuan. Additionally, at 9:00 PM on the 12th, a fire suddenly broke out at the home of Hu Shuibiao, No. 9, Xin Kaihe, outside the Taiping Gate. The fire was quickly extinguished by firefighters, but one thatched hut was burned, with losses amounting to over 200 yuan.

Nanping Railway Begins Surveying 107

Construction of the Nanyu section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway is progressing rapidly. The earthwork is largely complete, and track laying and spiking will soon begin. Deputy Director Hou Jiayuan of the Railway Bureau has personally gone to Yushan to oversee the work. It is rumored that the line will be open to traffic by the Double Tenth Festival. As for the Nanping section, an engineering team has been dispatched to survey the area and has returned to the province. A preliminary budget for the surveying work has been prepared and submitted to the board of directors for approval. A team will be formed this month to begin the surveying. The construction cost for this section is estimated at ten million yuan, and efforts are underway to raise the funds.

Ningbo: Gangs Rob Seven Sailing Vessels in Succession 108

On the night of the previous day, at approximately 8:00 PM, in the Tongpenpu River area of southern Yin County, two night-sailing vessels from Fangqiao and Xujia Du were suddenly intercepted by a pirate ship. Three pirates armed with pistols jumped out and robbed both vessels clean. While the pirates were carrying out their robbery, four night-sailing vessels from Jiangkou Nandong, Zhangyu, and Doumen Bridge were also en route to Ningbo. As they passed through the same area, the pirates ordered them to stop and robbed them one by one. Around midnight, the pirates left with their loot. Later, a night-sailing vessel from Xiaowang Temple, Yuanxingbu, was heading back to Fenghua from Ningbo when it encountered the pirate ship and was also robbed. After the robberies, the ships tallied their losses, which were quite substantial.

Xiaoshan: New Tea Enters the Market and Sales Have Begun 109

In the areas of Quanzi Li, Mashe, and Zhouwu in southern Xiaoshan, small hills undulate, making the area a prime tea-producing region. This spring, due to the erratic weather, the tea buds sprouted later than usual. The new tea has now been picked, and tea merchants from Shanghai and Hangzhou have been arriving in succession since the Qingming Festival to purchase it. Sales began uniformly on the 10th. However, the new tea market is not yet thriving, and the amount purchased by each merchant is limited. The price is 1.25 yuan per catty for Qiqiang tea, 0.93 yuan for Benshan tea, and 0.26 yuan for Qingcao tea.

Dongxiang: Silkworm Season Diminished by Cold Weather 110

Recently, the erratic weather has greatly affected the silkworm industry in Dongxiang. The early batches of silkworms, having already passed their first molt, have largely stopped feeding due to the unusually cold weather. Furthermore, frequent rainfall has caused the silkworms to consume wet leaves, leading the silkworms in their second molt to secrete yellow fluid and even die of flaccidity. Except for the silkworm farmers in the Xiaosibu and Nanyang areas, who mostly raise improved breeds this year and have not been significantly affected, the silkworms in the remaining four townships are of mixed breeds and have therefore been greatly affected by the cold. Many of the silkworms have become diseased, resulting in a significant reduction in the harvest.

Local News

The United States Continues to Raise Silver Prices: Our Side Plans to Avoid Impact; Discussion with the American Economic Mission to Shanghai; Song Ziwen Visits Kong Xiangxi in the Evening to Discuss 111

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Chinese government and various sectors of the financial community are paying close attention to the United States' increase in silver prices and are planning measures to mitigate the impact. It has been decided to exchange opinions with the American Economic Mission upon its arrival in Shanghai. The details are as follows:

China Attaches Importance to the US Raising Silver Prices

China was previously affected by the US government's nationalization of silver, which led to a massive outflow of silver from the country, causing panic over a shortage of currency and severely impacting industry and commerce. Fortunately, the Ministry of Finance cracked down on smuggling and established the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee to stabilize the market. In addition to increasing taxes on silver exports, a balancing tax was levied, and the import of foreign silver was encouraged. As a result, the outflow of silver gradually ceased, and the market gradually stabilized. Not long after, the United States suddenly raised silver prices again, which the Chinese government and people are paying close attention to.

Various Industries Consult on Stabilizing the Market

The financial community and various industries in Shanghai, recognizing that China is a country with a trade deficit, suffered greatly from the US nationalization of silver last year. If the United States raises silver prices again, there may be an outflow of silver. Since this is of great importance to our country, and the injured industry and commerce have not yet recovered, repeated impact may be unbearable. Therefore, leaders in the financial community and various industries have been holding informal meetings for days. In addition to finding ways to stabilize the market themselves, they hope that the government will quickly develop concrete measures to avoid impacting Chinese commerce.

The Government Plans to Avoid the Impact

Regarding the United States' increase in silver prices, the Chinese government telegraphed Shi Zhaoji, the ambassador to the United States, to notify the US government to make every effort to avoid impacting Chinese industry and commerce. At the same time, it is also planning ways to avoid the impact. Song Ziwen, chairman of the Bank of China, visited Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Finance, at Xiai Xian Si Road yesterday. It is reported that they discussed the US silver price increase.

Exchanging Views with the Mission

The Shanghai financial community has decided to exchange views with the American Economic Mission upon its arrival in Shanghai regarding the US silver price increase. They also hope that the mission will pay attention to the impact of the silver price increase on Chinese industry and commerce. If China's silver reserves flow out in large quantities again, industry and commerce will be unsustainable, and the purchasing power of the Chinese people will also be drastically reduced. The Economic Mission has decided to come to Shanghai from Japan on the 19th of this month.

Foreign Exchange Market Prices All Rise

Yesterday, the selling price of telegraphic transfers announced by the Central Bank was: London, one national currency per shilling, seven and a half pence; New York, one hundred national currency per US$39.375; Paris, one hundred national currency per 595 francs; Berlin, one hundred national currency per 97.25 marks. According to a reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency, the telegraphic transfer rate in New York has been US$34 to US$35 per 100 yuan for several months. The posted price the day before yesterday was US$37.625, and yesterday it suddenly rose to more than US$39. The increase of 5% in one day proves the great impact of the United States' increase in silver prices.

The Balancing Tax Rate Does Not Change Much

The Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee decided at 10:00 AM yesterday, after consultation between members Xi Demao, Bei Songsun, and Zhang Peishen, that the balancing tax rate would be 6.75%, which is not much different from the usual rate. (According to a late-night newspaper, the balancing tax rate rose to 1.1075. It was found that this number is the exchange rate for the British pound, one shilling, ten and three-quarters pence, and has nothing to do with the balancing tax.)

Agricultural Loan Syndicate: Four Directors Return to Shanghai Yesterday 112

According to the Guowen News Agency, Zou Bingwen of Shanghai Bank, Li Zhongchu of Jiaotong Bank, Yang Yinpu of Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and Wu Xiaoyuan of Jincheng Bank, directors of the China Agricultural Cooperative Loan Syndicate, left Shanghai on March 20 to investigate the conditions of rural areas and negotiate loan matters. They completed their work and returned to Shanghai yesterday (the 13th). According to a director, the group first went to Jinan, then to Tianjin and Beiping, and then to Dingxian to visit the cooperative and rural education programs run by Yan Yangchu. They then went to Zhengzhou, Xi'an, Weinan, Hankou, Jiujiang, Nanchang, and other places in a total of six provinces, and organized offices in Beiping, Zhengzhou, and Xi'an, which are managed by Jincheng, Jiaotong, and Shanghai Banks. It is also planned to organize offices in Jinan, Hankou, and Nanchang, but this must be discussed by the board of directors before a decision can be made. As for the amount of loans, it must also be determined after a meeting of the board of directors. It is estimated that the total amount of loans for the three offices in Beiping, Zhengzhou, and Xi'an is approximately 2 million yuan.

It is also heard that the directors conducted separate negotiations during this trip. As a result of the negotiations, (1) in terms of procedures, the syndicate is completely in a lending position and does not organize cooperatives themselves. The cooperatives are organized by local people introduced by the local cooperative affairs bureaus or local cooperative committees under the guidance of the Central Cotton Improvement Institute, and are responsible for borrowing from the syndicate. (2) The scope of the loan is limited to cotton, wheat, and rice, as they use scientific, economic, and political forces to hope for rural revitalization, while the syndicate is in a helping position, hoping that within three to five years, the country's food and clothing raw materials will be sufficient for self-sufficiency. (3) The syndicate also plans to organize rural warehouses in the loan areas. This plan is still being formulated.

Lawyers' Association Opposes Telephone Price Increase; Letters Sent Separately to the Authorities of the Two Concessions for Review; Second Special District Citizens' Association Investigates Users 116

The Shanghai Lawyers' Association sent separate letters to the Public Concession Bureau and the French Consulate in Shanghai yesterday to oppose the telephone price increase. The original letter is recorded as follows:

Dear Sir/Madam,

The commerce in Shanghai has always been known as flourishing. Since January 28, it has been affected by the global economic panic and the bankruptcy of rural areas, leading to a decline in the market. Factories and businesses have closed down one after another. Even those who can barely maintain their operations have to tighten their belts and implement austerity policies. Under this extremely depressed phenomenon, various parties are working hard to seek relief, such as the citizens' rent reduction movement, the silk industry's acceptance of bills, and banks' generous loans, all with the aim of easing business difficulties and revitalizing the market. However, the Shanghai Telephone Company, ignoring the concerns of all users in the city and unaware of the social and economic situation, is recklessly increasing prices by virtue of its authority, causing public anger and opposition. If this is prolonged, it is bound to lead to accidents.

Telephones are a public utility and a tool for communication, which is related to social prosperity and municipal measures. Therefore, whether state-run or commercially operated in various countries, the interest rates are minimal. How can the company focus solely on the amount of its own profits and insist on going its own way? Even if the company claims that its capital is huge, its expenses are vast, and its official interest and dividends are less than one percent, the company's internal organization lacks an overall plan and does not organize from promoting business and saving expenses. Lower prices and more users will result in higher revenue and thicker profits. Now, it is abandoning the root and pursuing the branch, acting perversely. It has been observed that the previous price increase has already led to a decrease in users. Now, it is changing new rules and doubling the price, which will inevitably further reduce users. Directly reducing the number of households will damage the business. If universal use is possible, the local area will benefit from it, and the company will also benefit. Otherwise, the company will end up losing what it wants to gain. This kind of policy is like drinking poison to quench thirst. There is nothing more clumsy than this.

Your Bureau is the administrative organ of the Public Concession. The telephone company's price increase is related to municipal prosperity, commercial development, traffic convenience, and social tranquility. You must be cautious and detailed. The association, as a legitimate organization of all citizens, is obliged to safeguard the rights of citizens and support public utilities, so we dare not remain silent. We hereby present our humble views and request your bureau to promptly stop or extend the review to alleviate business difficulties and maintain public sentiment.

This is to the Public Concession Bureau, Shanghai Lawyers' Association Standing Committee.

(The letter to the French Consul is similar in content.)

According to Xin Xin News Agency, the Fifth District Branch of the Second Special District Citizens' Association held an executive committee meeting the day before yesterday to oppose the repeated price increases by the Shanghai Telephone Company. They unanimously expressed their firm opposition and sent staff to investigate the number of users in the district. At the same time, they also sent a letter to the general association requesting that the Second Special District Telephone Users' Association be organized as soon as possible to effectively oppose the price increase. The association's announcement is recorded as follows:

Announcement:

In the autumn of this economic depression, when the market is so bad and the economy is so panicked, the Shanghai Telephone Company actually ignores everything and wants to raise prices again. Its greed is unparalleled. Our association specially held a meeting and decided to firmly oppose it. In addition to sending letters to various legal groups for consistent negotiation, we will immediately send staff to investigate the number of users in the district in order to collect statistics for a strong resistance. A questionnaire is attached. Please fill it out and submit it to the association as soon as possible without delay.

French Police in Jinliyuan Wharf Overstepping Authority to Inspect Passengers; Customs Inspector Orders Them to Leave but They Refuse 119

The Jinliyuan Wharf of the China Merchants Bureau's South Wharf is located on bureau property and is not within the French Concession. Therefore, incidents occurring at the wharf can only be handed over to the French Concession police by the wharf personnel. French police cannot exercise their functions at the wharf. This concerns the sovereignty of our country. Recently, due to anti-theft measures at various seaports, the bureau has established a White Russian inspection team, a shipping police team, a South Wharf inspection team, and female inspectors to inspect ships before departure. Unexpectedly, after Liu Hongsheng informed the French Concession police to send detectives to the Jinliyuan Wharf to inspect exports, their police power has extended to the South Wharf and interfered with passengers in the Shanghai-Ningbo wheelhouse at the wharf. The staff in the wheelhouse were helpless. Recently, the Jianghai Customs was ordered to inspect passengers carrying cash and contraband at the South Wharf. Seeing French police inspecting passengers, they believed that this was a violation of sovereignty and negotiated, telling them to respect sovereignty and withdraw from the wharf. The French police refused, showing their intention to make further encroachments. Eventually, the original agreement will be betrayed.

The Three Banks Ordered to Grant Loans: Appropriating Funds for Industrial and Commercial Relief 120

The New Voice News Agency reports that according to the regulations of the Central Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the China Bank, the stipulated business operations cannot engage in credit lending. Moreover, the China Bank cannot engage in goods pledging. The relevant clauses are as follows: In addition to the provisions of Article 7 of the Central Bank's regulations, Article 12 stipulates that the following matters shall not be undertaken. Item 3 states that accepting goods as collateral for loans is prohibited. Apart from the provisions of Article 11 of the China Bank's regulations, Article 12 stipulates that the following matters and other businesses shall not be operated, including Item 1, which prohibits various types of unsecured lending and guarantees. In addition to the types of business operations stipulated in Article 16 of the Bank of Communications' regulations, Article 17 stipulates that the following items shall not be operated, Item 1 being various types of unsecured lending and guarantees.

Three Banks Ordered to Grant Loans

According to the New Voice News Agency reporter's inquiry at the three banks yesterday, the Central Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the China Bank, after receiving an order from the Ministry of Finance, decided to provide relief to industrial and commercial enterprises facing difficulties by the end of April. Any silver firms or money shops wishing to apply for interbank loans can do so following the procedures of last year's final accounting. The Central Bank announces the daily interbank lending rate every day, which has been two cents for several consecutive days. However, although the China Bank and the Bank of Communications are not permitted to grant small-scale credit loans to industrial and commercial enterprises according to regulations, they have decided to maintain the already approved loans, totaling 1.4 million, for the sake of relieving industrial and commercial enterprises.

Total Funds Raised by the Association

The Bankers' Association has raised a total of 1.88 million yuan from its member banks for small-scale credit loans to industrial and commercial enterprises, of which 1 million yuan is from the China Bank and 400,000 yuan is from the Bank of Communications. In addition, banks such as the Shanghai-Zhejiang Xingye Bank, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the China Industrial Bank, the Kenye Bank, the Guohuo Bank, the Xinhua Bank, the Jincheng Bank, the Dalu Bank, the Yanye Bank, and the Zhongnan Bank have contributed a total of 480,000 yuan. The subcommittee will hold a meeting to decide on the implementation date.

Recently, the influx of foreign cotton has caused domestic cotton prices to plummet drastically, jeopardizing the effectiveness of the control measures and leading to a massive outflow of silver, which could undermine the foundation of the nation. National Goods Promotion Association: Officially Opens on a Fixed Date, Constructing the Venue on the 16th, Drawing Lots on the 20th 122

The Shanghai United Association of Chinese National Products Manufacturers and the Shanghai National Goods Promotion Association, previously initiated by the Jiaxu All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, had its opening postponed several times due to the lack of approval from the Municipal Party Headquarters. Now, it is learned that the Municipal Party Headquarters has approved the event. The details are as follows:

Reasons for Postponement

According to Liu Zhongying, a standing committee member of the United Association of Chinese National Products Manufacturers, the association originally intended to use the vacant land opposite the Great World as the venue and set the opening date for January 20. However, the owner of the land had traveled far abroad, making it impossible to contact him. They then negotiated with Mr. Kuang Zhongmou, who agreed to allow the use of the vacant land in the Xiaoximen Penglai Market as the venue. The opening was then postponed to March 15, and the matter was reported to the Municipal Party Headquarters for record-keeping. However, just as the association was beginning preparations, another organization, the National Goods Business Publishing House, also applied to the Penglai Market Office to use the same vacant land for a National Goods Exhibition. As both events were scheduled for March 15, and both aimed to promote national goods in the same location, a conflict was inevitable. The Party Headquarters also found it difficult to make a decision due to this conflict, leading to repeated postponements through negotiations and explanations. Finally, after consultations between the association and the National Goods Business Publishing House, it was agreed that the Shanghai National Goods Promotion Association would be held first. The association then requested the Municipal Party Headquarters to approve and record the matter, which has now been granted, thus confirming the opening date as the 22nd of this month. It was also mentioned that as of yesterday, more than 100 manufacturers had joined the association, and a grand opening is expected.

Registration Notice

The United Association of Chinese National Products Manufacturers' Notice No. 13 states: This is an urgent notice. The Shanghai National Goods Promotion Association, previously initiated by the association and the Jiaxu All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, has been repeatedly postponed due to the lack of approval from the Municipal Party Headquarters. On April 13, the association received Approval No. 2788 from the Municipal Party Headquarters, approving the event. The association's provisional standing committee meeting yesterday afternoon resolved the following: (1) The official opening is set for April 22, and there will be no further postponements. (2) The construction of the venue is set for the 16th, and the drawing of lots to determine location is set for the 20th. (3) All participating manufacturers who have not paid the venue fee must pay it within three days and obtain a receipt for the lottery. (4) Any manufacturers who have not registered but wish to participate must bring the venue fee (35 yuan per booth, including advertising costs) and send staff to the association for registration before the 20th. Accordingly, this notice is recorded and announced. Please do not hesitate any longer to avoid missing the opportunity. United Association of Chinese National Products Manufacturers, April 14, 1935.

Statistics of Chinese Goods Exported to the US in February 123

In February of this year, China's exports to the United States (excluding Hong Kong) decreased by US$1,399,970 compared to January, with a total value of US$4,528,224. However, this is still US$247,262 more than in the same month last year. In the first two months of this year, China's total exports to the United States were US$10,456,418, an increase of US$954,528 compared to the same period last year. In the first two months of this year, China did not ship any silver to the United States, while in the first two months of last year, 762,500 ounces of silver were shipped, valued at US$350,750. In February of this year, China's exports to the United States were dominated by inedible plant products, followed by inedible animal and animal products, and then textiles.
