Sanbei Company: Labor Dispute on the Shouchang Ship; Yichang Seamen's Branch Forcibly Appoints Half of the Crew; Head Office Firmly Denies and Plans to Dissolve the Crew 125

The Sanbei Company's Shouchang ship was forcibly boarded by workers appointed by the local Yichang Seamen's Branch, who expelled the original stewards, causing a labor dispute. The ship has now set sail and is expected to arrive at the port in two or three days. The recent developments in this matter are detailed below:

Sanbei's Reply and Negotiation

Upon learning that the Yichang Seamen's Branch had forcibly appointed workers to board the ship, overtaking the existing stewards and cargo handlers, the Sanbei Company sent a letter to the Yichang Seamen's Branch, stating: "The cargo handlers and crew members of the Shouchang ship were employed from unemployed workers from our company's Dexing and Fuhua ships. How can your branch arbitrarily appoint workers to board the ship? The Shouchang ship's engine department has not yet been fully prepared, and it needs to be docked for repairs upon its return to Shanghai. All crew members will be dismissed. Please withdraw your workers immediately."

Yichang Seamen's Branch's Struggle

After receiving Sanbei's letter, the Yichang Seamen's Branch replied, stating: "Since the Shouchang ship's port of registry is Yichang, the cargo handlers and crew members should be appointed by our branch. We have already made a significant concession by appointing only half of the required workers to the ship, including six cargo handlers and twelve stewards, as the ship needs twelve cargo handlers and twenty-four stewards for the midships section. The workers appointed by our branch have already been informed by the comprador of the ship, Liu Yongzhang. As for the matter of the ship going to the factory for repairs and the dismissal of workers, our branch cannot take that into consideration."

Labor and Wage Disputes

Since the Shouchang ship could not refuse the workers appointed by the Yichang branch to board the ship, it had no choice but to allow them to remain on board and resolve the matter upon arrival in Shanghai. Comprador Liu refused to pay the wages of these eighteen cargo handlers and stewards, as they were not appointed by the head office and had not been recognized by the head office. The Yichang Seamen's Branch has lodged a strong protest, sending a letter to Liu Yongzhang stating that if the wages are not paid, the Yichang Seamen's Branch will not be responsible for any unforeseen circumstances.

Negotiations After the Ship Arrives

Yesterday, when a reporter inquired with the Sanbei Company about how they would resolve the labor dispute on the Shouchang ship, a responsible person stated that the Shouchang ship would arrive soon. The company had already appointed thirty-six crew members for the ship and would not allow others to interfere in personnel administration. They will summon the workers for guidance when the ship arrives in Shanghai. If they do not listen, they will have no choice but to dismiss them for the purpose of repairs and docking.

Sixth Day of the Arts Exhibition Preview: Preferential Measures for School Groups to Visit 127

According to the Central News Agency, yesterday was the sixth day of the Shanghai preview of the London Chinese Arts Exhibition. It was also a Saturday with fine weather, and the number of schools, organizations, and groups from Shanghai visiting the exhibition was extremely crowded. The exhibition's reception staff were very busy. It is estimated that more than 100,000 people will visit the exhibition during its opening period. The exhibition has established reception rules and distributed them to all reception staff to ensure that all visitors are satisfied. The situation is detailed below:

Preferential Treatment for Groups

Recently, there have been numerous requests from schools and organizations to visit the exhibition. Schools such as Guangxia Middle School, Dagong Vocational School, Shanghai Business College, China Vocational School, Zhenru Experimental School, and Hangzhou Art College have all sent letters requesting to visit the exhibition. The exhibition has specifically established preferential measures for schools and art and academic organizations as follows: (1) In order to provide preferential treatment to schools and art and academic organizations, the exhibition has specially created half-price group visit tickets, calculated at a fee of one yuan per person. (2) The schools and organizations are limited to the following: 1. Teachers and staff of primary schools, middle schools, and private colleges and universities registered with the Municipal Education Bureau, and students holding proof documents from the school and the Municipal Education Bureau. 2. Teachers and staff of national universities and students holding proof documents from the school. 3. Art and academic organizations registered with the Municipal Education Bureau and holding proof documents from the organization and the Municipal Education Bureau. (3) The visiting period is limited to Monday afternoons, Tuesdays to Saturdays mornings. The schedule for municipal and private schools and organizations will be arranged by the Municipal Education Bureau and notified to the exhibition in advance. The schedule for national schools will be arranged by the exhibition to avoid overcrowding. (4) The ticket purchase method and location are as follows: Present documents that meet the requirements of the above Paragraph 2 at the ticket office in front of the exhibition hall and pay the price to purchase tickets for admission. (5) These measures will be implemented from May 15. In order to avoid overcrowding, the exhibition has also listed the daily limits on the number of visitors from the Municipal Education Bureau's affiliated schools and art and academic organizations, and has sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau for its information. The restrictions are as follows: Monday afternoon, limited to 500 people; Tuesday morning, limited to 1,000 people; Wednesday morning, limited to 1,000 people; Thursday morning, limited to 1,000 people; Friday morning, limited to 1,000 people; Saturday morning, limited to 1,000 people; Sunday morning, limited to 500 people.

Scheduled Dates

The exhibition has scheduled the visiting periods for national schools as follows: National Jiaotong University, the mornings of the 16th and 17th; National Wusong Merchant Marine School, the morning of the 18th; National Jinan University, the mornings of the 19th and 20th; National Shanghai College of Commerce, the mornings of the 20th and 21st; National Shanghai Conservatory of Music, the afternoon of the 22nd; National Tongji University, the mornings of the 24th and 25th; National Shanghai Medical College, the morning of the 26th; National Sino-French Engineering College, the morning of the 27th.

Lei Zhen Arrives in Shanghai

In other news, Lei Zhen, Director of the Ministry of Education, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning (the 13th) by express train from Beijing on the day before (the 12th) and went to the exhibition to oversee the preview.

Minister Visits

Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahua also visited the exhibition yesterday for a considerable amount of time. Among the visitors in the afternoon, there were many political figures from the capital, as today is a public holiday. This morning is closed, and the exhibition will be open to the public in the afternoon, with ticket sales until 6:00 PM and visits allowed until 7:00 PM. It is expected that the number of visitors will break the record of the past few days.

Value of Antiques

Yesterday, a well-known antique dealer visited the exhibition. According to his assessment of the bronzes and porcelain, each piece is worth at least 20,000 yuan. Some bronzes are even valued at 500,000 yuan overseas, and some rare porcelains are valued at up to 1 million yuan.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables the Ministry of Finance Requesting Exemption of Transit Tax on Rough Tea 129

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce cabled the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, on the 12th of this month, the Municipal Association of Coarse Tea Industry stated in a letter that silk and tea have always been major export commodities of our country. Since the successive development of overseas raw silk and artificial silk, the sales of Chinese silk in the international market have become increasingly narrow. The authorities have been making every effort to maintain and relieve the industry, from issuing public bonds to controlling production. Although the future of the silk industry is unknown, silk farmers and merchants have already benefited greatly. The decline of Chinese tea is no different from the situation of silk. Japan and India are emerging tea-producing countries, and the European market has been completely seized. This is the first reason why the overseas tea industry must be relieved. In recent years, the tea-producing areas in the hinterland have only been relatively peaceful in eastern Zhejiang. In the suburbs of Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, and Hubei, they have been repeatedly ravaged by communist bandits. The collapse of the countryside is unbearable to recall. Merchants who process tea locally must either carry their own rations or find it difficult to get a full meal. This is the second reason why the conditions in the producing areas must be relieved. Tea farmers are sick, and tea merchants are no less sick. Since the September 18th Incident, the North China tea market has been affected by military events. Outstanding accounts are uncollectible, and advances are unrecoverable. The transport of green tea to the north has plummeted. Tea merchants everywhere take Shanghai as the general hub, but since the January 28th Incident, Shanghai's financial situation has suddenly shown signs of collapse, making it difficult for merchants to extend credit and making them afraid to handle goods. After exhaustion, they have all become deadlocked. This is the third reason why the suffering of tea merchants must be relieved. The state's encouragement of Chinese tea has not been slightly biased. Even looking at the new tariff rules promulgated in 1931, the tea industry, in addition to being exempt from export taxes, the transit tax on black tea bricks is still temporarily exempt as before. At that time, because tea merchants did not participate in the discussion, other types of tea leaves did not receive equal benefits. From the perspective of tariff rules, raw black tea, when reported and transported at the first port, is entitled to tax exemption if it has been baked. However, raw black tea that arrives in Shanghai and must also be baked is still required to pay transit tax. The tea tax on raw tea is also the same at other ports. The taxation itself is already unfair. Moreover, the taxed tea is mostly raw tea, that is, coarse tea. The taxation of raw tea has the greatest impact on tea farmers in the producing areas and tea merchants who transport it. In this depleted situation, they are really unable to bear this burden. Try to investigate the conditions of the producing areas and the market situation, and you will naturally see that it is impossible not to provide relief. The only way to provide relief is to request the Ministry of Finance to exempt this transit tax in advance and first relieve the suffering that cannot be delayed, and then discuss other matters. It is also found that due to the transit taxation of raw tea, the reporting procedures are extremely cumbersome. Merchants who handle imports and exports must go through customs three times. During this time, there are opportunities for corruption and acceptance of tips and illegal fees. The amount of tax collected by the state is insignificant, while tea farmers and tea merchants are always sighing about how they come later. The new tea of this year is about to arrive in Shanghai in large quantities. For this reason, we earnestly describe the suffering of the tea industry and ask you to forward it to the Ministry of Finance, taking into account the difficulties of merchants and quickly deciding on a plan." The Chamber of Commerce, after investigating the national encouragement of tea and its sales abroad, not only exempts export taxes when exported from Shanghai, but also exempts transit taxes when transferred from the first port of origin to Shanghai, all in order to reduce costs and facilitate export. This is evident in the case of transit black tea bricks, which are exempt from transit tax. However, this transit tax exemption is limited to brick tea and baked black tea. If raw tea is transported to Shanghai, then baked and exported, it is still necessary to pay the transit tax. The treatment of the same export black tea is different. It is neither sufficient to show public universality, nor are the tea leaves that are transported to Shanghai and then sold abroad only black tea and brick tea. Therefore, the scope of the transit tax exemption set at that time was not able to take everything into consideration. According to the previous letter, it is appropriate to cable to your ministry for review and approval, and to allow the transit raw tea to be exempted from transit tax in the same way as black tea brick tea, which is in the public interest. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce.

Shanghai: Merger of Various White Russian Organizations 133

On Monday evening (the 8th) of this week, approximately 60 representatives from various parties gathered at the new premises of the Shanghai White Russian Emigrant Association, No. 118 Muir Road, Shanghai, for an unusually important meeting. The matter discussed at the meeting was the merger of various Shanghai White Russian organizations into one. The reason is that Shanghai White Russians are not recognized by Red Russia and are therefore stateless. Consequently, they have no government or consular representatives to protect their interests, and their opinions are also not aligned, leading to the division into several organizations, each vying to be representative. The result is that resident White Russians in Shanghai lack a formal organization to protect their interests, and outsiders suspect that these competing organizations are of no benefit to the White Russians and cannot represent them. In fact, they are detrimental rather than beneficial. Enlightened individuals among the White Russian community deeply felt the inappropriateness of this situation. They secretly united with each other, sought agreement from all parties, and brought about mutual understanding among the various groups of resident White Russians in Shanghai. As a result, this meeting took place. The most important thing was to enable the various parties of resident White Russians in Shanghai to understand each other and abandon their respective selfish intentions. Therefore, before the meeting began, the Russian Orthodox Bishop Ioanna, stationed in Shanghai, served as temporary chairman and gave a brief speech. Her speech aimed to encourage mutual understanding among the resident White Russians in Shanghai, to abandon all previous differences of opinion, and to unite the White Russians to create a formal representative body to benefit the White Russian community. After she finished her speech, she retired. The person who succeeded the bishop as chairman was Dr. Kazatchkov, director of the Russian Orthodox Hospital. After delivering a few words, he introduced Mr. Fuming to report to the representatives present. The most important point in his report was that the current situation is serious. Observing the situation of all parties, the various organizations and institutions of White Russians in Shanghai must immediately be merged and united into one. After Mr. Fuming finished his speech, all the representatives present expressed their agreement and support, and the following resolutions were passed on the spot: Mr. Metzler will serve as the formal representative of resident White Russians in Shanghai. The Shanghai White Russian Association will be merged. Mr. Fuming was elected as the president of the Overseas Chinese Federation from among 25 representatives. At the same time, Mr. Metzler will be the formal representative of the White Russian community. Any negotiations with the Chinese and foreign governments or the Shanghai Municipal Council will be handled by him, while Mr. Fuming and the Federation will handle all internal matters of the association.

Zhongnan Bank Doorman Arrested for Shooting and Killing Chauffeur: Parked in Bank's Private Road and Refused to Leave; Doorman Became Angry and Opened Fire 136

At approximately 11:50 AM yesterday, in front of the Zhongnan Bank at No. 110 Hankou Road, an incident occurred in which the bank's doorman shot and killed a chauffeur. Tang Boyuan, secretary of the Bankers' Association, had important business yesterday around 11:40 AM and needed to contact various banks. He instructed his chauffeur, Mao Miaosheng, to drive his private car (Concession Permit No. 3658) from the association to the Zhongnan Bank. After arriving in front of the Zhongnan Bank, he instructed the chauffeur to stop the car and disembarked. The chauffeur, seeing that his employer had gotten out of the car in front of the bank, parked the car in the row of cars on the Zhongnan Bank's private road to wait. Unexpectedly, he was seen by Liu Liangmei (age 42, from Jiangxi), the bank's doorman, No. 549, who stated that except for the private vehicles of bank employees, all other vehicles were prohibited from parking on the private road. Seeing that the car was not an employee's vehicle, he immediately intervened and ordered it to be driven away immediately. The chauffeur, Mao Miaosheng, immediately explained the employer's identity and business to Liu, stating that he would leave soon, so there was no need to make things difficult. However, Liu refused. Mao, thinking that he was unreasonable, locked the car door and went elsewhere. Upon seeing this, Liu became extremely angry and immediately went forward to grab Mao, insisting that he drive the car away. While they were arguing, Yao Guisheng, the chauffeur hired by Gao Shangyou, the owner of a private car with Concession Permit No. 3836, who was next to them, learned of the situation and stepped forward to mediate. Unexpectedly, Liu scolded Yao Guisheng severely. As a result, Mao Miaosheng and Yao Guisheng ignored Liu and walked away together. Unexpectedly, Liu still did not let go and chased after Mao and grabbed them again, stating that if they did not drive away, he would have the car taken to the police station. At this time, Mao and the others also started using abusive language, mocking Liu that if he wanted to take it to the police station, he could drive it himself. "Even if we are beaten to death today, we will not drive the car away," they said. This incited Liu's barbarity, and he did not consider the consequences. He immediately drew the pistol he was carrying on his waist and fired two shots. Mao Miaosheng was quick-witted, saw Liu draw his gun, and knew things were not good. He quickly dodged and avoided being hit. However, Yao Guisheng was unable to dodge and was shot in the waist. He fell to the ground on the spot. There was an uproar among the bystanders, and they immediately reported to the patrolling police, who arrested Liu and telegraphed the Central Police Station to send a car to take Yao Guisheng to Renji Hospital for treatment. Despite the hospital's best efforts, he eventually died at 8:30 PM last night due to the injury being in a vital area and excessive bleeding. The hospital notified the police to transfer the body to the coroner's office for examination. The perpetrator, Liu Liangmei, will be sent to court tomorrow morning for investigation.

Brother Attempts Suicide, Forcing Sister to Die with Him; His Foolishness is Unmatched; Brother Dies, Sister Saved 137

A young traveler, leading a country woman, checked into Room 1128 of the Dazhong Hotel on Zhengjia Muqiao in the French Concession the day before yesterday. After paying the room fee, he signed the register as Zhou Guangdian, from Changzhou, currently an apprentice at a pawnshop. The woman's name was Zhou Qiaozhen, 15 years old, dressed like a country girl. They were siblings. After entering the room, they closed the door tightly and there was no movement at first. Unexpectedly, around 5 AM the next morning, the tea boy on duty suddenly heard moaning sounds from the room. He pushed open the door and entered, only to see the man and woman lying face up on the bed, their faces pale. Knowing that they had taken poison, he felt them. The male guest's limbs were cold, and he had died. However, the woman's eyes were fixed and her mouth was agape, and she was still alive. He quickly reported to the Grande Route Station Police Station, and the head of the detectives sent detectives to investigate and sent her to Renji Hospital. Zhou Qiaozhen had taken a lighter dose of poison, and after examination by the doctor, she gradually recovered. Afterwards, when questioned, Qiaozhen, being a country girl, stared blankly and did not respond. It was heard that Zhou and her brother-in-law both worked at a pawnshop. Usually, her brother-in-law was very strict with her, and if she made a mistake, he would scold her loudly, even resorting to physical violence. Zhou, unable to bear the abuse, suddenly had thoughts of death. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday (the 12th), he took his sister to the inn and secretly took opium to commit suicide. At first, his sister Qiaozhen was unwilling to die. After Guangdian coaxed her repeatedly, she took a small amount of opium juice. As for Zhou's body, it was transported by the hospital to the Tongren Fuyuantang to await examination by the court. In his pocket, 85 yuan in cash was found, which was handed over to his sister to collect.

Truth About the Famous Prostitute Hongfu's Coma in the Hotel: "Chloroform" is Extremely Potent and Can Harm People; Despicable Youngsters Engage in Illegal Activities on the Shanghai Bund—Evil Thoughts Arose from Watching a Captivating Scene in a Movie— 138

The famous prostitute Hongfu Lao Jiu of Huile Lane, Fuzhou Road, was recently lured to the Yangtze Hotel by bandits under false pretenses and drugged, losing her mind and robbed of her precious jewelry. Afterwards, the prostitute reported to the police station, requesting an investigation. It has been briefly reported in the newspaper. Now it is known that the bandits in this case have been arrested by Detective Ruan Taibin of the Yulin Road Police Station: Ruan Zilin, Lu Jianying, Li Jianguang, etc. Ruan is 22 years old, Li is 23 years old, both from Ningbo. Lu is only 21 years old, originally from Hangzhou. These three men are vagrants on the Shanghai Bund and have no regular jobs. This time, Ruan Zilin took the initiative in drugging and robbing valuables. At first, Ruan was not familiar with this kind of trick. Recently, he happened to go to the Grand Shanghai Theater to watch a movie. There was a scene in the movie where someone was drugged with medicine. After watching it, he became obsessed and wanted to imitate it. On the 3rd of this month, he secretly conspired with the two bandits Lu and Li to try it out. After Lu and Li agreed to help, he searched for the drug. However, pharmacies never easily sell drugs containing toxic substances. Because Ruan was friends with Liu Jiaji, a doctor who lived at No. 12 Xuetang Lane, Jing'an Temple Road, he went to visit Liu on the 5th and asked for a drug. Liu asked about its purpose and gave him two small bottles of "chloroform," which has the power to make people lose consciousness, and instructed him on how to use it. He only needed to drop one or two drops on a handkerchief and cover the mouth and nose of the person being drugged. The person would inhale the medicinal gas and immediately fall into a coma. If too many drops were used, the medicine would be very strong, the handkerchief would burn, and it would hurt people. Ruan was taught carefully. On the afternoon of the 8th of this month, he first pawned a coat for 10 yuan. Then, he invited the two bandits Lu and Li to go to the Yangtze Hotel on Yunnan Road and rent Room 523, falsely claiming the name Ding Zhenyu, and paid the room fee of 5 yuan. As for who they wanted to drug, they had no purpose at first. Then, the three bandits unanimously agreed that prostitutes were easier to lure and easier to set up. So, they asked the waiter for the telephone book. After checking it, they decided that the prostitutes in Hongfu's brothel must be richly dressed and must have made a lot of money. They called the porter of Hongfu's brothel at No. 31 Huile Lane, Fuzhou Road, using the name Wang. After a while, Hongfu Lao Jiu (with the small name Wang Yuxian, from Jiaxing) came gracefully. However, the prostitute did not know any of the three bandits. She asked who Mr. Wang was. The bandits falsely claimed that Mr. Wang had gone elsewhere to play mahjong and would be back soon. They offered the prostitute cigarettes and tea, but she declined them. The bandits were afraid that the prostitute would not stay long. So, the bandit Ruan secretly went behind the prostitute and, according to Liu Jiaji's instructions, poured a little of the medicine from the bottle on the handkerchief and suddenly covered the prostitute's face with the handkerchief. The prostitute immediately felt a strange smell entering her nose. Knowing that she had encountered a violent guest, she opened her mouth and shouted for help. The bandits were afraid that the plan would fail. So, Lu Jianying used violent means to restrain the prostitute's hands and feet. Ruan Zilin pressed her mouth tightly with the handkerchief. Li Jianguang, thinking that the medicinal power was too light, disregarded the consequences and poured the bottle of medicine on the prostitute's face. The medicine was indeed very strong, immediately causing Hongfu to fall into a coma and injure her jade face. Seeing that the work was done, Lu and Li took the gold bracelets from the prostitute's arm and fled first. Bandit Ruan, feeling the medicinal gas in the room, immediately closed the door to prevent it from leaking out. Then, he left the prostitute on the bed and saw that she was still wearing a jade ring on her finger. He robbed it and fled. Afterwards, he met the two bandits Lu and Li in front of the Grand Bright Cinema and took the tram together to the Baidu Bridge. Bandit Ruan threw the bottle of medicine with very little left into the Huangpu River. The unused bottle was still hidden on his person. He instructed Bandit Lu to take the gold bracelets to Yucheng Pawnshop at No. 236 Tiantong Road and pawn them for 30 yuan and 4 jiao. After redeeming Bandit Ruan's coat, the remaining money was divided among them. Ruan got 7 yuan, Lu got 8 yuan, and Li got 4 yuan and a jade ring. With the remaining 1 yuan and 4 jiao, the three bandits went to the New Central Cinema to buy tickets to watch a movie and spent it all. Then, they parted ways and disappeared. The drugged prostitute, until after the bandits had fled for a long time, slowly woke up, but felt a lot of pain in her face. The people in the brothel were all gone. When she asked the waiter, he had no idea. At that time, the prostitute felt severe pain in her abdomen and blood came out of her mouth. The innkeeper reported to the relevant police station, and the detectives came to investigate and sent the prostitute back. On the 11th, Detective Ruan received a report that Ruan Zilin was in Suzhou at a friend's place. He immediately went there and arrested Ruan, bringing him back to Shanghai. After questioning, it was learned that the two bandits Lu and Li were hiding at No. 62 Xiude Lane, Gaoyue Road, Zhabei. Yesterday, he joined the police station and arrested them. The stolen goods such as bracelets and rings were also recovered. Yesterday morning, the police station first escorted Bandit Ruan to the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Li Zhishan stated the facts of the case, saying that the two bandits Lu and Li were still detained in the Public Security Bureau and requested a written request to pick them up. The Russian woman, Iher Elkaterte (transliteration), 39 years old, and her lover, Govf Men (also Russian, 50 years old, former soldier), lived at No. 1, Lane 178, Maohai Road. Beef Shop Employee's Prank Leads to Murder: Leather Shoes Used as a Weapon; Leads to Fatal Outcome 140

The Ronghualou Beef Shop at No. 179 Yangzhou Road is owned by Yang Dazhang from Nanjing and has been open for many years. He employs Zhang Caifu (28 years old) from Yangzhou and Chang Houde (41 years old) from Anhui to help with the work. At around 3 AM the day before yesterday, the two employees woke up. They were bored in the pavilion and played dominoes to pass the time while waiting for dawn. After an hour, Chang lost six copper coins. Zhang felt tired and wanted to sleep a little longer, but Chang refused. They argued with each other. Chang angrily used his leather shoe to beat Zhang in the face. Zhang was strong and took the shoe and retaliated by hitting Chang on the head and right eye. They dragged each other downstairs, went out the door, and argued. The nearby patrolling police heard the alarm and arrived, taking the two men to the Yulin Road Police Station. After reporting to the head of the police, they were told that the two were colleagues and had suffered only minor injuries. Chang also stated that he did not want to file a lawsuit. They were both released and returned to the shop. At lunchtime, Chang bought wine and ate it with beef, then went to bed to relieve his troubles. Zhang also apologized to him. Unexpectedly, around 8 AM, the shop owner's wife went to check on him and found his face pale and on the verge of death. She was very alarmed. Her husband Dazhang had returned to his hometown for business. So, she told her brother Yang Daxing to report to the police and call an ambulance to take Chang to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment, but it was too late. He died soon after. She telegraphed the police station, and they sent detectives to the scene. They took the body to the Piren Road Coroner's Office. They arrested Zhang Caifu and took him to the police station for detention. Yesterday, he was sent to the First Special District Court. Labor Bureau lawyer Shu Zhishan explained the situation. Then, Wu Xiaoshanzi, an 18-year-old apprentice from Gaoyou, stated that they had started fighting over the dominoes and that Chang Houde had hit Zhang with his leather shoe first. When questioned, the defendant confessed that he had no grudges against the deceased. He had only suffered a nose injury at the time, but unexpectedly, he had died later. He asked for leniency. Judge Jiang Shuzi ordered him to be detained for further investigation. The coroner Song Genshan of the court went to the office to examine Chang's body and confirmed that the deceased Chang Houde had died from injuries to the brain and right eye. Zhang Caifu was suspected of causing the death and has been detained according to law. The police station should investigate the matter. No family members were found. The body was handed over to the Pushan Villa for burial.

Two Sand Dredging Boats Collide 142

Jinshunfa Boat Head Collapses: Jinshunfa fishing boat, Shanghai Customs stamp No. 95, loaded with sand and mud for sale in Shanghai, arrived at Dongpu Beach on the opposite bank of the Wusong Yunzaobang at 8 AM yesterday. The Lianfeng fishing boat, which was exporting from Shanghai, also arrived at the same place. Due to failure to avoid each other, the head of the Jinshunmao boat was violently hit, causing the head of the boat to collapse. The head mast, head awning, anchor chain, etc. were lost at the bottom of the sea. The six crew members were rescued by other ships and were able to avoid danger. Afterwards, the river patrol boat learned of the situation and rushed to the scene, dragging the fishing boat to a shallow beach to be stranded. The boat owner Zhu Amao reported to Xie Dachang, who reported to the tax agency, prepared a presentation, and sent it to Zhang Huahong of the Customs River Administration to negotiate compensation for the loss with the fishing boat.

Jinjunmao Breaks Three Masts: At the same time, the Jinjunmao sand and mud boat imported and arrived at the Dongpu Bin on the opposite bank of the Zhang Huabang North Railway Pier. There was a small barge named Xindao Nike (transliteration) of the Huidefeng Tugboat Company, towing a large name Tuntaluosi (transliteration) for export. The two wheels arrived at the location, suddenly crossed, and the Jinjunmao was horizontally in the middle. The lead wire rope that towed the giant wheel was attached to the mast and awning rope of the fishing boat, causing the fishing boat to be inclined and about to capsize. At the critical moment, the large and small masts and awning ropes of the fishing boat were all damaged and broken, so it did not capsize and no one was injured. It was very fortunate. Afterwards, the boat owner Jin Alian rushed to report to the Senji Customs Brokerage to prepare a presentation to the Zhang Huabang Customs Boat Administration to negotiate with the company for compensation for the loss for repairs.

Special Party Department of Seafarers Orders Subordinates to Establish Literacy and Writing Assistance Centers for Seafarers 145

The Special Party Department of Chinese Seafarers, recognizing that the majority of seafarers in various regions under its jurisdiction are illiterate, and that even minor tasks requiring writing must be entrusted to others, causing them great distress. To remedy this situation, solve the difficulties faced by seafarers, increase their interest in literacy, and complete the basic work of the literacy movement, the organization section of the department has drafted a method for establishing literacy and writing assistance centers for seafarers. It has requested that subordinate party departments at all levels be universally ordered to establish these centers within the shortest possible time to promote widespread literacy and progress. The methods for the seafarers' writing and literacy assistance centers are as follows: "Methods for Seafarers' Writing and Literacy Assistance Centers": (1) To facilitate seafarers in various regions in commissioning the writing of documents, seeking clarification on difficult words, and assisting in solving difficult problems, this association will establish seafarers' writing and literacy assistance centers in the subordinate district party departments (hereinafter referred to as subordinate party departments). (2) When seafarers encounter the aforementioned difficulties and request assistance, the person in charge of each seafarer's writing and literacy assistance center must use a sincere attitude to first inquire about their name, age, and place of origin, and record them in the register. Then, inquire about the purpose of their visit or the difficult matter, and provide detailed instructions and answers. The questions and answers must be recorded in detail for future reference. (3) Subordinate party departments that have established writing and literacy assistance centers must submit a weekly report to this association, detailing the number of people who have come to inquire, the general meaning of the words being written, and the solutions to the problems. (4) The person in charge of each seafarer's writing and literacy assistance center will be assigned by the original subordinate party department staff on a weekly rotation basis. The timing may be determined by themselves based on the situation in each district. (5) Subordinate party departments that have established writing and literacy assistance centers must formulate regulations based on the actual situation in each district (district branch and district party department are the same) and submit them to this association for approval and implementation.

Wanju Wharf: House Collapse Kills People; Dockworkers Carrying Steel Bars Suffer Tragedy 149

Yesterday at around 8:00 AM, a warehouse house at No. 37 Wanjuma Tou Street, Nanshi, collapsed suddenly, killing a dockworker on the spot and injuring two others. One was sent to Baolong Hospital and died soon after, and the other was sent to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. The details are recorded as follows:

Steel Stacked Inside the House

The owner of the house, surnamed Zhou, entrusted Shen Yuanlai Tung Oil Firm at No. 221 Luma Road to rent out the house. The house was rented out to Renji Steel Firm at No. 618 Luma Road as a warehouse by Sheng Xiqi, the manager of Yuanlai Firm, two years ago. However, the house was built of brick and wood and had been in disrepair for many years, so the Municipal Bureau of Public Works had repeatedly ordered the owner to rebuild it. The owner did not repair it immediately because the house was rented to Renji and was stacked with heavy steel.

Wall Collapses, Beam Falls, People Crushed

Yesterday at around 8:00 AM, when dockworkers Teng Jinhe (42 years old, Wuxi), Tang Quangen (37 years old, Wuxi), and Du Axiang (36 years old, Wuxi) were carrying steel bars in the Renji Steel Firm warehouse, a south-facing brick wall of the house collapsed suddenly due to the excessive pressure of the steel bars and other iron parts, which could not support it. The beams and roof on the wall fell down, causing the three people working there to be unable to escape and were crushed. Other dockworkers tried to get the bodies of the three out one by one.

Teng Jinhe Dies Immediately

However, Teng Jinhe among them, because his head was broken and his brains were cracked, died on the spot. Du Axiang, who was left, was sent to Shilong Hospital for treatment by car, but due to the severity of his injuries, the treatment was ineffective, and he died at about 12:00 PM. Tang Quangen, who was injured, is now being treated at Shanghai Hospital, but his life is also in extreme danger. After the incident, the No. 16 Police Sub-bureau in charge, because the owner of Renji, Shen Songnan, was not in Shanghai, summoned Rong Rongpei, the manager of the firm, for questioning. Because the matter concerned human life, it ordered Lu Yongde, the land chief of No. 16, to report to the Shanghai Local Court for an inquest. Then, at about 5:00 PM, Inspector Xie, commissioned by the court, arrived at the scene with examiners and other personnel for an inquest. After the inquest, it was confirmed that the deceased Teng Jinhe died from being crushed during his lifetime. The body was handed over to his family for coffin preparation and burial. The inquest was completed and returned to the court.

Light Packages Renamed Small Package Mail 159

Post Office News: The "Light Packages" that were opened on April 1 this year, according to the International Postal Convention, are one of the types of mail. Its nature is different from packages. All procedures for delivery and delivery are also handled in the same way as mail. Therefore, it should be renamed "Small Package Mail". This measure is designed to facilitate the public in mailing small items. Various postal countries have already held it. Whether it is placed in a mailbox or handed over to the post office, it can be delivered as registered or express mail. However, because its volume is slightly larger than ordinary letters, and the fee is cheaper, it is called small mail for identification and easy handling.

The total amount of exchange coupon reserves was 6.26 million silver dollars. The cash reserve was 4.71 million silver dollars. The guarantee reserve was 1.54 million silver dollars. The above two items, the cash reserve accounts for more than 75%, and the guarantee reserve accounts for less than 25%. This report is specially made.

In order to make more friends, he plans to sort out the calligraphy pieces he has accumulated over the years: (1) Central hall vertical axis, (2) Screen strips, (3) Couplets, (4) Fan pages, and give them to everyone. Starting from today, gifts will be given to all connoisseurs. The gifts will be given until they are finished. Seal script, Wei inscription, and running script are available for listening and selection, and the Shangkuan can be added. Those who ask for it only need to specify their name and address, and attach 60 cents of postage per piece (limited to 1 to 5 cents). Corner tickets are common. Paper and shipping fees are included. Shanghai Qipu Road Huiye Guild Hall opposite No. 187 will reply to the letters by number, both in the city and outside.

Later, the Donghua generals continued their efforts and attacked together. The Jewish team was very overwhelmed by this. Qian Zuozi found an opportunity in the chaos and gently kicked the ball into the net, and Donghua won with a score of 4-0.

Gu Shangquan still took the kick, making the score 5-0.

Finally, Jia Youliang passed to Li Yichen, who went straight to the Yellow Dragon and kicked it in, ending the game with a score of 6-1. Donghua won a big victory.

City Education Bureau Plans - To Build a Zhabei Sports Ground - Submitted to the City Government for Approval to Allocate the Liuying Road Base 174

The City Education Bureau's plan to build a public sports ground in the Guanshanbei district was initiated in the 16th year of the Republic of China in response to the needs of the citizens and the request of the City Party Headquarters. Several sports experts were hired to engage in design, and the abandoned base of the Liuying Road barracks was found for the purpose of setting up the sports ground. It was submitted to the municipal government on September 6th of the 17th year for approval to allocate its use, establish boundary stones, and issue notices. Later, due to a dispute between the Ministry of Military Administration and the property rights, the layout was temporarily suspended. After repeated negotiations by the municipal government, the Executive Yuan (the 207th council meeting held on the 9th) decided to order the Ministry of Military Administration to allocate the base to the Shanghai Municipal Government. Therefore, the Bureau is now actively preparing for the construction of the Zhabei Sports Ground.

Zhuang, a member of the banking industry, initiated the Qingsheng Cup table tennis competition, notifying all banking institutions to register their table tennis teams. This City Actively Promotes Literacy Education: The Second Plenary Committee Meeting Was Held Yesterday, Deciding on the Directors of the Jiangwan and Huning Experimental Zones; Offices in Various Districts Will Be Established on May 1st; Mayor Wu Will Report on the Measures at Tomorrow's Commemoration Week 182

Proclamation to Compatriots on Promoting Literacy Education

In order to promote literacy education, the committee issued the following proclamation to compatriots yesterday: Dear compatriots, you probably all know the pain of being illiterate. An illiterate person cannot keep accounts, write letters, read newspapers, understand posters on the wall, understand government notices, or understand the general trends of the world. Sometimes, it is simply like having eyes but not being able to see, becoming a seeing blind person. Their suffering is truly indescribable. In China, it is said that 80 out of 100 people are illiterate. Shanghai also has hundreds of thousands of people. To relieve the suffering of the people and revitalize our nation, we must first make these many illiterate people literate. To this end, under the leadership of the Shanghai Municipal Government, we will soon begin a large-scale literacy education movement. It is planned that within this year, hundreds of thousands of illiterate men, women, old and young in Shanghai will have the opportunity to become literate. The methods we use are: First, dividing Shanghai into twelve districts, and establishing dozens of schools in each district, forcing illiterate people to study for one hour a day, not only without tuition fees, but also giving away books. They can graduate after studying for two months. Second, for some people who really cannot go to school to study, we will send teachers to their homes to provide individual guidance. After two months, if they pass our exams, we can also give them graduation certificates. At that time, they will be able to keep accounts, write letters, and read simple newspapers. Not only will it be convenient for themselves, but the entire Shanghai will feel benefited. However, before the investigation, we cannot start these methods, because we do not yet know who is illiterate, how many illiterate people there are, who can go to school in the morning, who can go to school in the evening, and who really cannot go to school. How can we set up schools and send teachers? Therefore, we plan to start dispatching a large number of investigators from April 10th in the Jiangwan experimental zone, from April 20th in the Nanshi experimental zone, and from May 8th in the other twenty districts, wearing signs, to conduct on-site investigations and also persuade illiterate people to go to school. As mentioned above, this literacy education movement is obviously a very heavy and difficult task. We have few people and limited capacity, so we cannot but hope that all sectors of society will support us. May China be fortunate.

Mayor Reports on Implementation Measures

Wu Tiecheng, Chairman of the Literacy Education Committee and Mayor, will report on the implementation of literacy education measures at 9:30 am tomorrow (Monday) during the city government's commemoration week, and has stipulated and notified the following personnel to participate: (1) Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, Shanghai Education Association, Shanghai Farmers' Association, Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions each send two responsible representatives to participate; (2) All staff of the Shanghai Education Bureau participate; (3) Principals or academic directors of all public and private primary and secondary schools in this city participate; (4) Section chiefs in charge of the Public Security Bureau, and directors and chiefs of various sub-bureaus participate; (5) Municipal committee members of various districts participate.

Sixth Day of Reading Movement: Li Ximou Speaks on How to Study Science; Sun Hanbing Will Speak on How to Study Political Science at 3:15 pm Today at Zhongxi Radio Station 183

Yesterday was the sixth day of the National Reading Movement Conference organized by the China Culture Construction Association. The association specially invited Li Ximou, Dean of the College of Science of National Jinan University, to speak on "How to Study Natural Science." Today (14th) at 3:15 pm, the association invited Sun Hanbing to broadcast "How to Study Politics" at Zhongxi Radio Station. The full text of Li Ximou's speech is recorded below:

Definition of Natural Science

The China Culture Construction Association, for the purpose of guiding young people in academic research, has specially invited scholars to give various academic research lectures. Today, I am asked to speak on "How to Study Natural Science." I have little in-depth research on natural science. Today, I can only share the research methods and personal experiences with you. To study natural science, we must first understand what natural science is. We live in the universe. The various forms and things in the universe are constantly changing. If we can organize and classify them in a reasonable way, and use various experiments, investigations, calculations, etc. to prove and explain the unclear or doubtful points, and only stop after the verification is beyond doubt, then the knowledge that specifically studies all the phenomena of nature can be called natural science. Mr. Ren Hongjun once defined natural science as "knowledge that is formed by collecting and regulating the natural phenomena in the universe according to logical methods." I think this definition is quite complete and worthy of our attention.

Motivation for Studying Science

The motivation for studying natural science can be said to come with life. Since the existence of mankind, the interest and need to study natural science can be said to have never been interrupted. If we break it down, there are two reasons: one is due to curiosity and the desire for knowledge. The movement of the sun, moon, and stars, and the changes of wind, rain, snow, and ice in nature have long been felt strange and frightening by primitive people. Therefore, there are traces of early research in astronomy in ancient times. The earliest development of astronomy in natural science is clear evidence of mankind's curiosity and desire for knowledge about natural phenomena. The second reason is due to the needs of the environment. The four major needs of human life are clothing, food, housing, and transportation. If there is a separation from natural science, natural science will naturally grow with human history and become more and more prosperous with the level of human culture. To give the most famous example, the invention of geometry in Babylon and Egypt was due to the needs of the environment at that time.

Science and Non-Science

The distinction between science and non-science has a definite boundary, which we cannot confuse at will. In Chinese history, there are so-called Suirenshi drilling wood to make fire, as well as the invention of the compass, papermaking, paint making, winemaking, gunpowder, printing, the manufacture of boats and vehicles, the invention of porcelain, etc. Generally, people think that ancient Chinese natural science was very prosperous. In fact, these are just fragments of scientific technology and scientific knowledge, and not what is now called true science. True science must have systematic explanations and reasonable analyses. For example, drilling wood to make fire, why can drilling wood make fire? This is because the friction of the object increases, heat is generated by friction, combustion occurs by heat generation, and the function and effect of fire are generated by combustion. Such a systematic explanation and the resulting conclusion is scientific. Therefore, the difference between science and non-science is that science pursues the causes of its occurrence, the phenomena in the process, and seeks its conclusions. If it is a fragment of scientific skills and scientific knowledge, we cannot call it science.

Conditions and Spirit

Regarding the method of studying natural science, the British scholar Russell once said that the scientific method has a necessary condition, one is observation and the other is inference. The so-called observation is to put it in the laboratory to experiment, and the so-called inference is to use our reason to infer. Only experiments can observe correctly, and only inferences can be accurate. Personally, I think Russell's two sentences are indeed true. As for the spirit of studying natural science, one is to respect reality, the second is to value accuracy, the third is to observe signs, the fourth is to judge, and the fifth is to maintain doubt.

Basic Knowledge of Science

Studying natural science is just like studying other subjects. If you want to study ancient Chinese society, you must have a deep foundation in oracle bone inscriptions, ancient geography, and ancient history. The basic subjects for studying natural science are mathematics and mechanics. Assuming that there is no solid foundation in mathematics and mechanics and in-depth research, it is impossible to even touch the threshold of natural science. Scientific knowledge is so superficial and narrow among the Chinese intelligentsia, and the interest of Chinese students in mathematics and mechanics is so low and lacks interest. When we recall the close relationship between natural science and the strength of modern countries, it is really regrettable.

Methods of Studying Science

Finally, I want to give you a serious attention. We will not talk about saving the country, but if we want to talk about saving the country, we must study natural science. Otherwise, empty talk about saving the country is like the late Southern Song Dynasty. Empty talk about science is no different from the Qing Dynasty's restoration. Young students across the country should be afraid of the nation's decline, the country's crisis, and the shrinking of its territory. If you want to work hard to save the country and the people, it cannot be reversed by the courage of blood and the strength of an ordinary person. You must be down-to-earth and deeply enter the garden of science. To study natural science, you must have the following four basic methods. The first is mental training. To make your understanding clear and your thinking thorough, you must study philosophy, logic, and psychology. Those who study natural science can go deeper into the hall and gain deeper knowledge only after being trained in philosophy, logic, and psychology. The second method is to work hard and study diligently. Chinese scholars are harmed by taking a quick glance and not seeking thorough understanding. If you want to study a profound subject, you must not study it repeatedly day and night, and what will you gain? The second method must be focused. One day of exposure to the sun and ten days of cold will not help. You must exhaust your life's energy to gain something. The fourth method is to experiment. Natural science certainly requires hard thinking, but also emphasizes practical observation. The equipment in the laboratories of our major middle schools is either simple or even lacking experimental equipment. Now that vocational education has been set as the national education policy, I hope that all education administrative agencies and school authorities across the country will pay close attention to it.

City Education Bureau Implements Model Teaching for Elementary School Teachers: Pilot Programs to be Conducted in the Shanghai South and Zhabei Districts Starting on the 22nd of This Month 184

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education yesterday issued an order to public and registered elementary schools, stating: "In order to enhance the effectiveness of elementary school teachers in this city, the bureau has formulated the 'Outline of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education's Implementation of Model Teaching for Elementary School Teachers.' Therefore, the outline of the program and the list are urgently dispatched for compliance. This order is hereby issued." Attached are the "Outline of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education's Implementation of Model Teaching for Elementary School Teachers" and the "Second Semester of the Twenty-Third Year, Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, List of Model Teaching for Elementary School Teachers" as follows:

Outline of the Program: Outline of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education's Implementation of Model Teaching for Elementary School Teachers, Article 1: The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education (hereinafter referred to as "the Bureau") hereby formulates these measures in order to improve the professional development of elementary school teachers in this city and to enhance teaching effectiveness. Article 2: Model teaching will be implemented separately in seventeen districts, including Shanghai South, Zhabei, Yinxiang, Yinhang, Wusong, Jiangwan, Pengpu, Zhenru, Pusong, Fahua, Caojing, Niusitang, Qiaoyang, Yangjing, Luxing, Gaohang, and Gaoqiao, with the primary education research association's leading school in each district serving as the location for implementation of model teaching. However, the Shanghai South and Zhabei districts may make appropriate modifications. Article 3: Teachers responsible for model teaching will be introduced and designated by the Bureau's Office of Supervisors or the principals of the respective schools. The Shanghai South and Zhabei districts will hold two sessions each semester, while other districts will hold one session each semester. Article 5: The implementation of model teaching will temporarily be divided into three types: teaching in various subjects, mixed-grade teaching, and single-grade teaching. Schools in urban areas will focus on teaching in various subjects, while schools in rural areas will focus on mixed-grade teaching. Low-grade design teaching, mid-grade problem teaching, and high-grade individual teaching may be implemented as appropriate according to actual needs. Article 6: When model teaching is conducted, the Bureau will designate teachers from municipal and private elementary schools near the respective schools to attend and observe. Article 7: Teachers responsible for model teaching must prepare a teaching plan before teaching. Teachers from various schools must prepare observation notes during observation. The teaching plan and observation notes must be submitted to the Bureau for record after the event. Article 8: After the model teaching is conducted, a discussion meeting may be held or a centralized discussion may be held in the primary education research association. Article 9: When model teaching is conducted, the Bureau will assign appropriate personnel to attend. Experts may be additionally hired to participate if necessary. Article 10: All matters related to the implementation of model teaching shall be presided over by a committee organized by the Bureau Director. Article 11: Teachers responsible for model teaching who demonstrate teaching that is truly consistent with the name may be rewarded by the Bureau as appropriate. Article 12: These measures may be amended at any time if they are not perfect. Article 13: These measures shall take effect from the date of promulgation.
