Women's Sphere

Survival and Reproduction 188

— Biwu

Many people who are unwilling or dare not face the current situation are running back to embrace the corpses of the past, and are blowing the terms "motherhood," "motherly love," etc., to the skies. However, the facts tell us that women are indeed seeking to lose their reproductive functions, but cannot. Some would rather sacrifice and not marry or be absolutely celibate in order to avoid falling into the "mother" prison. Some carefully brave dangerous waves, and finally get into big trouble, and use abortion to fight with their unborn children. The so-called "mother" is more cruel than jackals, tigers, lions or enemies.

The gentlemen who uphold morality may see these facts as being made by women of the new and liberated era, and denounce them. In fact, their old eyes are blurred. Truly new and liberated women do have abortions for the sake of life and work. But a large number of modern girls have abortions, but it is not for the sake of liberation. In addition to these two types of women who have abortions, there is a third type of women who do this, but they have long been overlooked by the gentlemen who uphold morality. Because they were originally self-generated and self-destructed like weeds, and their actions in life are difficult to hang on people's words. But in fact, the number of small lives strangled or destroyed from the wombs of these weed-like women is many times more than the first two types of women. It's just because their actions are silent and in the dark corners of the house, so there is no way to count them.

According to the report, a young woman from Zhenjiang, Shen Chen, came to Shanghai to work as a servant due to poverty, but she was already pregnant. She was deeply worried that it would be inconvenient to work for a long time, so she privately used a dried radish to try to get the fetus to fall. Unexpectedly, the effect was not seen, and the woman was in extreme pain. Later, a doctor removed it for her, and she was fortunate to be reborn. However, because the abortion violated the criminal law, the court sentenced her to two years in prison.

The fact that this matter was able to appear in the newspaper is because it happened in civilized Shanghai, with well-informed patrol houses and newspaper reporters. The second is because it was not medicine that was used, and although the fetus moved, it did not fall, so it was revealed. If there were not these two conditions, it would have been nothing. Don't you see that in the countryside, it is difficult to find one or two out of a hundred poor women who die from abortions who are told about?

Everyone knows that abortion is harmful to health and even life-threatening, and there is also the terror of punishment. However, women still take the risk. What is it that gives them the courage? It's nothing more than to get "survival". The desire for survival is stronger than anything else. For the sake of survival, they can build or destroy all the respectable, lovely, terrible and terrifying human things. In recent years, most women have embarked on a dead end. She can't take care of herself, how can she be expected to accept the great righteousness of cultivating talents for the country? Today, it is natural to watch the race die out day by day.

Perhaps some people curse women for being so selfish and wanting to survive, and not willing to reproduce. However, okay! What happens if women even dispel their desire to survive? What can you do?

Since society ignores the survival of women and does not give her a way to survive, she cannot give society reproduction. Even if the laws are strict, her contraception, which is more passive than abortion, cannot be stopped by anyone. If so, this ground may only leave green grass for others to graze.

Since we still have a breath left, we always want our nation to last for ten thousand years. For the many facts that we have heard and seen about women who are unwilling to reproduce, I really hope that society will liberate women, so as to liberate society itself, and open up a way for the survival of the nation.

Women's Issues Lecture

Section 2: The Enslaved Life of Women 189

— Junhui

In ancient Greece and Rome, with the development of private property and the strengthening of the slave system, men had already taken away women's right to participate in social production. They were no longer the main producers of wealth in the national economy! They were driven from the vast field of social production into the family, and transformed from social beings into family slaves!

What is a family slave? The meaning of her existence is first to satisfy the sexual desires of her husband, that is, the head of the family; second, to bear the husband's offspring; third, to ensure the accuracy of the husband's legitimate children and not to communicate with other men; and fourth, to be confined to the bedroom and kitchen, as long as they are docile and obedient, and not to resist!

The male-centered Greek Athens was the first to set various moral laws and laws to deprive women of their freedom and punish women's resistance. The so-called Solon's new law for the republic stipulated that women who committed adultery would be punished with death, or their husbands would sell them as slaves, but men were allowed to be free. This is a typical law of a male-dominated country!

The wives and daughters of free citizens in Greece and Rome naturally had much better material lives than female slaves, but they were also equally without rights and unfree. Married women were completely subordinate to their husbands, living a long-term "prostitution" slave life in a cage-like family. Unmarried women were subordinate to their parents, without the right to choose their husbands, and were deeply imprisoned in their boudoirs, waiting for their parents to sell them. Their precious lives were consumed in dark bedrooms and kitchens until the day they died!

Regarding the life of Greek women at that time, a comedy writer described it as follows!

"Of all things, spiritual and physical,

Ah! The most miserable existence, is really us women!

We have to be sold to our husbands with a dowry, - the worst is that our bodies also belong to him.

No matter what kind of person he is, good or bad,

This danger is most alarming - because divorce is an insult to women, and women are not allowed to refuse their husbands.

......Excerpt......

Men can avoid the troubles at home, and can find comfort outside,

Beside friends, in the ranks of peers - while we have to stay at home alone!

They often say that women are in no danger,

Staying at home during their war.

What a foolish fallacy! I would rather go to the battlefield three times than go through childbirth once!" (See "Women and Society")

However, on the other hand, men strictly prohibited other men from infringing on their wives and daughters, but they themselves constantly pursued the wives and daughters of others. Thus, in order to alleviate this contradiction, the famous prostitution system in Greece was born! Solon, who drafted the new law of Athens, actually set up state-run brothels and openly practiced a perverted polygamy system. A shameless Athenian man openly said:

"We marry a woman because we want legitimate children and a loyal mistress of the house. We use maids for bedside care and daily service. We prostitute ourselves for the enjoyment of love." (Ibid.)

However, prostitutes at that time were not female slaves who could be bought and sold at will, but female citizens who bravely lived a free life, transcending all moral laws that bound women! They had noble education and were quite accomplished in learning, and they bravely participated in political activities. For example, Aspasin, Lais, Phryne, Leona, Archeanassa, etc. are all famous prostitutes in history. Archeanassa was the lover of the great philosopher Plato, Aspasin was a good friend of the great philosopher Socrates, and Phryne was also a social butterfly in the Greek aristocracy! Leona, a prostitute around 500 BC, participated in the political conspiracy to oppose the usurpation of the power of the republic by the usurper at that time, and was arrested together with his comrades. Under cruel torture, she refused to confess the truth, and bit off her own tongue and spat it on the face of the judge!

In this way, the prostitutes at that time had noble knowledge and character, and freely associated with the upper class. This can be said to be another manifestation of women's resistance to the bondage of male power after the collapse of the matriarchal system!

In addition, there were outstanding female scholars in Greece, and they made many contributions to culture, and many of their disciples were thinkers. For example, Asfo was a famous female poet, Agnozhika was the first female doctor who wore men's clothes to study medicine and engaged in medical skills, and Ibachia, a beautiful female professor from Alexandria, was a great philosopher. Scholars from all over the world came from thousands of miles away for her lectures!

In this way, although women at that time were absolutely oppressed by male power on the one hand, they fully demonstrated the spirit of struggle and resistance on the other hand! Let's take a look at the famous Greek comedy "Women's National Assembly"! Here, the heroine, Prok-Su-Go-La, actually proposed a bill for the common ownership of property, which is noteworthy. She proposed:

I demand that everything should be shared in common, and everything should belong to everyone. From now on, the rich and the poor should be eliminated. It should be eliminated that some people do not even have a burial ground while others own vast land. Women should also become common property. They should be allowed to have children with the men they like. (See "Labor Women's Revolution")

Obviously, this is a bill proposed by Greek women against private property, forced marriage, and the slave status of women. This is a protest raised by women around 400 BC, that is, 2,500 years ago, but it has not been realized to this day! No! Sure enough, in some parts of the world, it is being better realized!

German Women Under Hitler (Continued) 190

— Translation of Mrs. Wulen's Speech

Expulsion from Public Life

The most achievable thing for Hitler after seizing power was the complete expulsion of women from public life and from the industrial world! From 1919 to 1932, female parliamentarians from all parties except the National Socialist Party could participate in the German parliament, and they all completed their missions well. Among them, such as population issues, food issues, and the protection of productive labor women, their achievements in the parliamentary committee related to women were the most remarkable.

However, since the general election in 1933, there have been no female members of parliament. No women have participated in the important positions in various government departments, and men have replaced the positions of female school operators and married female teachers. What is most noteworthy is that the intervention of the Third Reich even extended to civil servants. The Constitution of 1919 "repealed all discriminatory treatment against female civil servants." As a result, women who had been confined before actively participated in various occupations. However, according to the latest regulations, women with 35 years of continuous work can obtain the status of permanent staff. In particular, regardless of the Aima Constitution, even though labor is the same, women's wages are lower than men's, which is very detrimental to women.

Family Life in Crisis

The fact that women are withdrawing from the industrial world can be seen concretely in the changes in numbers. When the National Socialist Party first seized power, the number of women employed was 11.5 million, accounting for 36% of users. Only 6 million women were employed. By May 1934, it had dropped sharply to 3 million.

Germany's policy of expelling productive labor women in order to revive family life is actually destroying families. On May 13, 1934, Dr. Bleek, the Minister of the Interior, said: "Whoever can truly fulfill their biological obligations should be given special rights. Therefore, it is impossible and unjust for mothers with many children to work in the workplace. On the one hand, mothers are burdened with the burden of life, and on the other hand, their health is weakened by several pregnancies and births. They do not need to engage in factory labor, and young and strong women should also stay at home."

Although all freedom of speech has been deprived, it is noteworthy that the call against the abolition of women's employment is issued by women themselves. For several weeks, the outline of the employment regulations issued by the Berlin City Council was posted on bulletin boards throughout Berlin.

The organ magazine of the National Socialist Women's Department, the July 1934 issue, recorded the following on this issue:

"This program, of course, gives abnormal shock and fear to senior professional women and even staff members over the age of . In particular, the following items are very abhorrent to all intellectual women. That is,

"(3) German young women - clinging to pots and pans, sweeping the floor, etc., in this way, you can get your wishful husband. Recognize your calling - act according to your calling! Do not think that the ease of stores and offices is more valuable than your future duties as a housewife. Home will make you healthier, more vibrant, and more vigorous."

(4) Labor women—instead of engaging in affairs, it is better to learn to be a wife. Don’t leave men at home, go home yourself, and let your profession be given to men. Otherwise, they will have no other prospects except being indirectly supported by your little bit of work. In fact, old-age insurance is useless. Make your life meaningful! Otherwise, your spirit and body will have nothing but ruin?”

“(7) Our housewives—don’t take away the work of your husband and son. Servants at home are needed because you don’t do it.”

The seventh item deprives middle-class women of the right to paid labor, and they have to dismiss their servants and handle all housework themselves.

The National Socialist Party prohibits women from engaging in paid labor, and women are in a state of semi-slavery of unpaid labor. The following is recorded on the public announcement of the Minister of Labor.

“In the spring of 1934, 60,000 female students graduated from elementary education, most of whom could not find employment. However, sitting idly by is not their wish. Therefore, they have to be engaged in "housework practice", and open German families for this purpose as much as possible.”

In this way, housewives of all classes dismiss the servants they have always used, and unconditionally use these girls as unpaid semi-slaves. Because the girls who practice housework are sent to the landlords' homes in the countryside to engage in agricultural work. According to the report of the headquarters of the Labor Exchange Bureau, "There are no more unemployed women. On March 31, 1934, there were still 575,074 unemployed women. However, the Ministry of Finance wants to completely eliminate unemployed women in 1934. The remaining must choose one of marriage, housework practice, and farming. In any case, all owners of cities are not allowed to hire women to occupy men's positions."

What women fear most is engaging in agricultural work, so they often do not register even if they are unemployed, but such things are punished when the authorities know about it.

In this way, under the current situation in Germany, women have completely reduced some of the results that they have worked hard to obtain for decades, and are sent back to the Middle Ages. (The End)

People Lingering on the Line of Life 191

— Zhi Yun

I spent two autumns lying in my own bed, and one spring living among those suffering people. When I felt a certain kind of pressure on my health, I would remember that hospital, remember that group in the hospital. All oppression can be resisted, only health oppression is the most irresistible.

A person who has never stayed in a hospital will not be terrified of hospitals.

People who love life are brought here to seek life, and people who love death are also carried here to force them to live; but people who love life often cannot live, while many people who love death leave alive. Many children are carried from the delivery room to the nursery, and many people are carried from the ward to the morgue. The hospital is like this, a place that eternally stages this terrible drama.

Almost every two or three days, someone who attempted suicide is carried in. The reasons for their desire to die are often very complicated. Human psychology is truly incomprehensible. A person who is willing to die and is almost dead is always revived with surgery. But when they can feel themselves struggling on the edge of life and death, they are left there unattended, as if the matter is over. When these rescued people can walk, they often appear in the corridors outside the wards with their weak bodies. Are they truly saved? I cannot know.

People always love life more. As long as they are given another chance to live, they always want to live. So many people endure so much torment on hospital beds year after year, all for the sake of living. They don't know when a high fever or pain will strike them. Delirium and moans constantly fill the space; sometimes they are carried down covered with a large white cloth, and when they are carried back up after being butchered, they still haven't opened their eyes. Tian Han put it well: a person is a machine, and when it breaks, it has to be brought here to be repaired, but doctors are not omnipotent mechanics! When they ask the doctor, "When will I get better?" the doctor points to the sky and says, "Ask Him." They look at the tall trees outside the fence, from bare branches to tender leaves, from tender leaves to being covered in green. All living things climb upwards, but what about them? They have no spring. They are people lingering on the line of life. They want to live, but they have no ability to make themselves live well. So they think of death: "Let me die, this suffering!" They cried. But as long as they think that they have not reached the extreme of life, they endure and carry on.

This is a painful crucible. In addition to their own illnesses, the unfortunate people don't care about unequal material treatment (of course, not everyone is a property owner!), and they cannot get spiritual comfort. The most peaceful time for them is when relatives and friends bring news from outside. I don't think any hospital is reasonable! In the weeks after I was discharged, I often went to see them. Although I went to see the few I knew, I remembered many things about them. When they sighed and said, "I won't get better," I always comforted them, but I knew for sure that two of them, who had been there for more than two years, would never be healthy. Every time I went, I would be restless for two or three days; after that, I didn't go much anymore. I became so afraid of this hospital. When I got sick again last autumn, the doctor wanted me to be hospitalized. I shook my head at him. He said, "Do you know you're courting death?" I thought that as long as half of me hadn't died, I would never go back in. After that, I never went again, but I knew that not all of the few I knew would be able to escape this chain of suffering.

Spring has come again, and I remember those who have no spring, those who linger on the line of life!

A Casual Visit to a Women's Labor Night School 192

— Qian

The sky was drizzling with rain of a moderate size, and the wind was blowing harder and harder. After running through several long streets with a bare head, I jumped onto the tram. The warm and comfortable atmosphere in the carriage made me feel like I had instantly ascended from hell to heaven. Among the crowd exhaling warm air, just after securing a seat, a strange yet familiar voice, somewhat vague, suddenly came from across:

"Ah, you are...!"

I looked up at a woman with a long, flat face who looked like an elementary school teacher, and also couldn't help but shout:

"Ah, you are...!"

Just like that, in this accidental opportunity, I ran into one of my close classmates from eight years ago; Ms. Zhang Yuying. She was weighed down by the burdens of her family, working as an elementary school teacher like a beast of burden during the day, and teaching at a women's labor night school run by a youth association from seven to nine in the evening. I was drawn by our old friendship, and escorted her all the way to the school, taking the opportunity to observe her work.

The night school itself had no school building. It borrowed three classrooms on the upper floor of an elementary school that had classes during the day. There were more than one hundred students in total, divided into three levels: elementary, advanced, and special. The study period was set at half a year for each level to graduate. The courses included correspondence, Mandarin textbooks, arithmetic, geography, and so on. The most students were in the elementary level, about sixty or seventy, forty or fifty in the advanced level, and more than ten in the special level. It is said that the ladies rarely reach the special level, because they slowly get married, leave, and some cannot continue studying due to changes in their environment.

Although the rain was gradually getting heavier that night, the three large rooms were gradually filling with people. They entered the classroom, and as soon as they sat at their desks, they either started copying or reading. Although there was an unfamiliar person like me among the teachers, they seemed not to see me. Their eagerness for knowledge and the sincere attitude was probably something that was hard to find even in one or two out of a hundred students in noble girls' middle schools and universities.

Soon, a special level student opened a storage box and took out a wall newspaper made by themselves and pasted it on the wall. The content of the wall newspaper included both pictures and articles. The pictures were all selected and clipped from the Shanghai Shen Bao picture special issue. Under each picture, they had their own comments. For example, a picture of a Soviet Russian food sales point, with two or three women in white uniforms selling bread, they wrote below: "The lives of Soviet Russian female workers are so idyllic, what about our lives?" The articles included discussions on "The Death of Ruan Lingyu," "Our Way Out," "Our Enemies," and so on. They knew that Ruan Lingyu's suicide was caused by society.

There were also obvious differences in the clothing and appearance of the one hundred plus people. The people in the elementary level, many of whom were relatively older, were not dressed very well. The special level students were so-so, but already had the appearance of students. The advanced level students were all girls around eighteen years old, and eighty percent of them were very beautifully dressed and made up. If you saw them on the street, you would never recognize them as female workers, especially their shiny black hair, fair skin, delicate and skillful figures and postures, which were simply like old-fashioned rich ladies and young mistresses. I think this also had something to do with their work, because they did light work - female workers in cigarette factories. According to my friend, most of them had very light family burdens, or no family burdens at all; otherwise, they would have to do other work at night, so how could they have the time to study. I suddenly understood, these were probably the so-called "daughters of small families." Their wages, it is said, can earn several to more than ten yuan per month. According to the wall newspaper, the working hours are as long as twelve hours a day.

Although it only costs five cents for registration and buying books is enough for the female workers to enter this labor night school, there are countless people who cannot enroll due to their own living environment, and there are also many people who are limited by the enrollment procedures. It is said that this kind of night school is quite strict in accepting students. Without someone's introduction, without a guarantor – that is, a guarantee that they are good workers – don't even think about getting in. Therefore, the scope of this charitable事业事业 run by the youth association is not very widespread. However, in any case, this is a hundred times more meaningful than the miserable children's carnival they hold on Christmas, if the people involved are really working for the female workers, and not for God.

Diary of a Concubine (Continued) 193

— Guan Lu

April 28th

I moved into the hospital this morning. Chen Ma accompanied me. Usually, Chen Ma doesn't dare to tell me things at home, but here in the hospital, she tells me everything. She has been talking to me almost all day, from the moment I entered the hospital until now. Some problems that I think are too simple, she weeps about and sighs for me. Sometimes, things that I think are too embarrassing, she finds ordinary.

She told me that when she first went to work for many rich wives, she often saw those wives crying and weeping. She always felt that the richer the wife, the more "insatiable" they were. They had so much money to spend and still felt bitter, and still argued with the master. If these wives were all turned into housemaids like her, marrying a poor husband and having to find food as servants, wouldn't they all hang themselves? Wives are too domineering. After watching for a long time, she slowly began to understand some of the suffering of the wives. The only thing that wives have better than maids is that they spend more money, but the anger and rebuffs they suffer are still the same.

She cried again when she said this. She talked about how she was a child bride in the past, how she was scolded as a man's prostitute. When she was farming at home, what kind of suffering she endured for production. Now her husband has a mistress and doesn't want her anymore. As she spoke, she hinted to me: this time, Mr. X sent me to the hospital, and he probably won't take me back to the mansion in the future; he said that he would rent a house for me to live in outside after I give birth.

When I first heard this, I felt a little unnatural, but after calming down, it wasn't a big deal. This is not just my ending, it is the ending of women.

May 29th

It's been more than a month since I wrote in my diary. The doctor said that I am now a very serious "hysteric," and told me to take special care of myself before and after childbirth. They haven't let me do anything this month, they won't even let me write letters, and they've taken away my pen and ink. Yesterday I said I wanted to write a letter to my father, and I only managed to trick them into giving me a pencil. But Chen Ma is constantly watching me all day long. Actually, what benefit is there to me from this kind of surveillance? Even if I don't write in my diary for a year, it won't cure any of my illnesses.

Having moved into the hospital, tonight is the quietest night, and also the loneliest night. Mrs. Wang didn't come to see me, even Miss didn't come, and even Chen Ma was called back by the old lady, and she still hasn't come back by this time.

The shadows of the parasol trees imprinted through the gauze window seem to be telling people: it's late at night, telling people: the world is quiet, telling people: life has come to an end; at the same time, they are also telling people: although it is late at night, a pitch-black late night, but, in the shadows of the parasol trees, there is still the reflection of the bright moon, and in the midst of looking up at that bright moon, there are still people who are clear, bitter, and struggling!

Miscellaneous News: Detailed Regulations for Inspection of Plant Pests and Diseases (Continued) 210

(Article 14) After a plant inspection certificate has been issued for plants exported from within the country, if the packaging needs to be changed, the inspection bureau shall be notified for approval to send personnel to supervise the repackaging and re-labeling. (Article 15) During the execution of the inspection, the applicant shall be subject to the direction of the inspection personnel for the handling, movement, or disassembly of plant packaging. (Article 16) The inspection bureau shall not be liable for compensation for any unavoidable damage to the reported plants due to necessary procedures in the implementation of the inspection. (Article 17) If, after inspection, the reported plants and their packaging are found to contain diseases or pests, the applicant shall transport them to the designated location for incineration or, after undergoing fumigation and disinfection procedures, apply for re-inspection. However, the inspection bureau may, at its discretion, permit the original applicant to request the return of plants exported from within the country or to request that plants imported from abroad be transported back to the exporting country using appropriate methods to prevent the spread of pests and diseases. All fumigation, disinfection, and transportation costs mentioned in the preceding paragraph shall be borne by the applicant. (Article 18) After plants imported from abroad have passed inspection, if they need to be transported in batches to various locations, a distribution report form may be filled out, together with the original certificate, and submitted to the inspection bureau for verification and issuance of a distribution certificate. (Article 19) If plants that have passed inspection at Bureau A are transshipped to the location of Bureau B, a transshipment report form shall be filled out, together with the certificate issued by Bureau A, and submitted to Bureau B for verification. If it is confirmed that the original packaging is consistent with the certificate, the word "Released" shall be signed and noted on the original certificate, and the plants shall be exempted from inspection. However, if any discrepancy is found, a new inspection shall be conducted. (Article 20) If an application is submitted for reissuance or replacement of a certificate in accordance with Article 13 of this law, and the inspection bureau finds that there is no sufficient reason, a new inspection may be conducted. (Article 21) Plants that are re-inspected in accordance with the preceding two articles shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of Article 4 of these detailed regulations. (Article 22) If a certificate is lost within its validity period, in addition to applying for reissuance in accordance with the law, the original certificate number and the circumstances of the loss must be published in a prominent local daily newspaper for two days or more, declaring it invalid. (Article 23) The Inspection Bureau may formulate supplementary measures for the implementation of plant disease and pest inspection, but it must be submitted to the Ministry for approval and record. (Article 24) These detailed regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (Promulgated by Ministry Order on October 5, 1934) (End)

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Children's Life 211

— Only Through

Children's life, I think it's quite flavorful. Although I am no longer a child now, I still think that children's life is worth reminiscing about.

Children have no worries about sex, no economic distress, no difficult problems, and their needs are met. Every day they wake up in their mother's arms, jump and skip to school, receiving basic education for making a living. After class, they play with friends and eat candy. In the evening, yawning, they fall asleep to their mother's lullaby.

Thinking back on this kind of life now, it's truly like ascending to immortality.

Today's children are becoming more and more fortunate. Not only can children bathe in their mother's love, growing up in maternal affection, but also have patient and kind teachers guiding them on how to strengthen their bodies, how to pay attention to their health, how to practice manners, and how to live a communal life, and they will no longer taste the rod.

In addition, look, modern children have so much extracurricular reading material to read. In addition, look, modern children have a joyous and enthusiastic Children's Day. In addition, look, everyone feels that children are China's most hopeful, everyone feels that such a small seed will not be difficult to become a great talent and can be made into a great vessel in the future.

However, I feel that today's children are quite capable of shouldering the great responsibility of revitalizing our country and nation... Here, with one hundred and twenty percent sincerity, I bless the lively and lovely children.

Kant's Words 212

— Zeng Zhi

Kant was a German philosopher who was proficient in various disciplines. He cherished time very much, so he often told people, "A person lives in this world for at most a hundred years; in these hundred years, every second that passes is one second less, so we should cherish time." He was not only a person who cherished time, but also had a fixed schedule for work, study, and rest. People asked him why he did this? He said, "A person's life, with a set time, can be done step by step. Not only can knowledge progress, careers can succeed, but also the body can be trained, and the spirit can be happy."

Children, Kant's cherishing of time and disciplined life is truly worthy of our emulation!

Burning 213

— Zhen

On that Sunday, Fen'er and Fang'er were sitting at home, asking each other about the week's work at school.

Fen'er said first, "Sister! I am very afraid of arithmetic, but even though I am afraid, I still pay attention to it and never neglect it. Sister, what subject are you afraid of?"

Fang'er thought for a moment and said, "I am afraid of science, because this subject requires understanding the principles inside and memorizing them firmly, how difficult! My favorite subject is arithmetic. Which one do you like the most?"

Fang'er said, "I like science, because it is very interesting, why does oxygen and hydrogen combine to form water, isn't this very strange? And it is closely related to our future. If we don't pay attention to science, I am afraid we will not be able to stand in society. Sister! You must work hard!"

Fen'er listened to her sister's words and thought carefully, it was very true.

"Fen'er! Fen'er! Bring me a box of matches!" Fen'er's mother shouted in the kitchen.

Fen'er quickly went to give it to her mother.

When Fen'er came back, she asked her sister, "Sister, I want to ask you, is the weight of straw after it is burned heavier or lighter than before it is burned?"

Fang'er smiled and said, "Sister, are you silly? Straw turns to ashes after it is burned, how can it be heavier than before?"

Fen'er said, "Bah! You're wrong. The weight after burning must be heavier!"

Fang'er said, "I say it must be lighter!" They argued back and forth.

Their father came in from outside, heard them arguing, and said, "You don't need to argue. The right and wrong of everything must have considerable proof."

Their father first found a porcelain bowl, put some iron powder in it, and then weighed it on a scale, knowing its weight. Then it was placed on a triangular iron frame, and fire was used to burn it below. After burning for about four or five minutes, the fire was removed, and when the bowl was cold, it was placed on the scale again, and it was found that the weight was a little heavier, and the iron powder in the bowl had turned into a reddish thing, like iron rust.

Their father said, "Look! The iron powder in the bowl absorbed oxygen when it was burning, so we know that it must be oxygen that causes the change with the iron powder. The weight increases after burning, it must be the weight of oxygen. In short, the weight of everything increases after burning, because it increases a part of the gas."

The Important Problem of Bowel Movements 214

— Yi De

The older brother got out of bed, put on his slippers, and hurried to have a bowel movement. The younger brother smiled and said, "Brother! If you're any later, you're afraid you'll pee in the bed, right?"

The older brother, while having a bowel movement, also smiled and replied, "Brother! This is because you usually don't pay attention to me, I'm not like this today, I'm like this every day. The first important task after I get out of bed every morning is to have a bowel movement. The timing of bowel movements is really an important issue. Think about it: if you suddenly have to have a bowel movement while eating, isn't it annoying? If you suddenly have to have a bowel movement while in class, isn't it annoying? If you suddenly have to have a bowel movement during a competition, isn't it annoying?..."

The younger brother hurriedly said, "That's right, that's right! If you have a bowel movement at that time, it is indeed very annoying."

The older brother said, "So we should schedule our daily bowel movements; but scheduling them after getting up in the morning is the most appropriate. Because after having a bowel movement in the morning, you don't have to worry about it all day, whether you're eating, in class... And it's even more convenient for traveling. If you suddenly have to have a bowel movement halfway when you're traveling and can't find a toilet, isn't that a very painful thing?"

After the older brother finished his bowel movement, the younger brother also went to have a bowel movement. The younger brother strained his face red and asked loudly, "Brother! I can't pee at all, what's the reason?"

The older brother: "This is because you don't usually have a bowel movement at this time. Don't be impatient now, sit for a while longer, you can pee out a little. In the future, as long as you have a bowel movement at this time every day, it will become a habit."

Wang'er on Children's Day 215

— Zhu Ying

Wang'er was the son of a poor father. His father had a food stall in front of the Rende Elementary School. Children from poor families, even if they are of school age, do not have the right to receive education. Not only do they not have the right to receive education, but they also have the obligation to help their fathers produce. Wang'er's father was very poor, so naturally he was no exception, so he also wore a tray on his chest every day, with a piece of paper pasted on the tray, and cheap food hidden under the paper, following his father, near the Rende Elementary School, luring elementary school students to play the trick of "hitting the jackpot with a copper coin."

That day happened to be April 4th, early in the morning, he followed his father to the front of Rende Elementary School as usual. But that day, he saw that the situation in Rende Elementary School was a bit special. People were so busy going in and out of Rende Elementary School, and those elementary school students were also particularly happy, but there were particularly few people who came to him to hit the jackpot. He felt surprised, so he pulled a familiar elementary school student and asked him what the school was doing today. The child said the three words "Children's Day" and jumped to school again. Then, the school emitted beautiful piano music, melodious singing, applause, and laughter.

Half a day passed like this, and the father and son had not made three hundred cash. In the afternoon, the school led the entire school's students to play in the suburbs. Obviously, there was no hope of doing business in the afternoon. But the hunger in his stomach made Wang'er's father see stars, so he vented his anger on Wang'er for no reason, beating Wang'er's face blue. Wang'er cried while thinking in his stomach: "Children's Day? What is called Children's Day? Is Children's Day the day I should be beaten?"—He didn't know what the meaning of Children's Day was, but he cursed Children's Day like crazy.

"Money" 217

— He Gongchao

When we talk about "money," we think of silver dollars with Sun Yat-sen's image on them, copper coins with national flags, and colorful banknotes. In fact, there are many kinds of "money" in the world. If we look at this picture, we will understand how many strange kinds of money there are in the world.

In very ancient times, there were no copper coins or banknotes like today. If you wanted to say that this family was rich, you would say, "He has how many livestock, how many slaves." In this way, livestock and slaves were the "money" of that time. Later, the exchange of goods between people (such as exchanging rice for cloth) became busier and busier, and it was necessary to determine something as a standard for exchanging goods with each other. Therefore, leather, shells, iron bars, ivory, tea cakes, and salt blocks were used for this purpose.

Even in modern times, in several civilized countries, certain things are sometimes used as "money." For example, Canada uses beaver pelts, Newfoundland uses dried fish, Germany uses soup cubes, and Virginia uses tobacco. For example, in 1914, in Harrison, USA, eggs were once used. People had to hold eggs and hand them to the ticket counter to buy tickets to the cinema.

Animal Riddles 218

(1) Wearing a ruyi on its head and a green robe on its body; with a slender waist and a large belly, holding double knives in its hands: it loves to swing back and forth in the grass. (Praying Mantis)

(2) Living in a deep mountain stream, my parents raised me too strangely; everyone else is skin and bones, only I am bone-covered skin. (Turtle)

(3) A cat came from the sea, its tail is like scissors; although it lives in the mud, it is many feet above the mud. (Swallow)

(4) Carrying a house on its back and a horn on its head; the house is a shell, and the horn is two strips of meat. (Snail)

(5) My home is in the bend of the bay, the front and back doors are not closed; I am not afraid of jackals, wolves, lions, or leopards, only afraid of the little tiger coming down the mountain. (Mouse)

Rural Friend's Life Notes 219

— Zi Ming

March 12, Tuesday.

There have been many children coming to school these past few days, and even desks are lacking. It is said that this is the result of the school implementing compulsory education. All children aged six to thirteen must receive compulsory education. That is, they are only considered to have completed their educational obligations after graduating from the fourth grade of primary school. If children of school age do not attend school, the school will ask the police to enforce it.

This is the case in all countries: however, the length of compulsory education varies from country to country. England has nine years, France has seven years, Germany has eight years, Belgium has eight years, Italy has nine years, Switzerland has nine years, Sweden has seven years, the United States has nine years, and Japan has six years: they have been very successful in their implementation, so the people are very intelligent. Although China has set compulsory education at four years, it has not been universally implemented. Our principal is a very enthusiastic educator, who has specifically formulated compulsory education implementation measures, obtained the permission of the county government, and announced them to the public; if any children do not study, they will be punished. Therefore, there are extremely many children coming to our school these days.

At 9:00 a.m., the tenth anniversary of the death of the Premier was held, and the school's national flag was only raised to half-mast. Thinking about it, a great man who saved China and the world has been dead for ten years: time is so fast, and the pain only intensifies! Many people often take "inheriting the legacy" as a catchphrase: what is the reality of the performance now?—The country is about to perish—

The Adventures of Sinbad the Sailor (13) 220

— Xin Qing

I ran as fast as I could, not stopping until evening, when I sat down to rest for a while, ate some food I had brought with me, and then set off again. When my food ran out, I ate coconuts, because coconuts can be used as both food and drink. But on the eighth day, I saw the sea. I saw many people, like me, _______________ because there was a strong fragrance that was produced near the coast.

When these people saw me, they left their work and came up to talk to me. I was happy to hear them speak in my native dialect, which let me know that I was with friends.

I told them about the shipwreck and my life with the black people, and they were all delighted to see me. They thought it was very fortunate that I was able to escape from the hands of those black people.

Finally, we all boarded a ship carrying a large batch of spices and set sail, arriving on time at the place where these new friends of mine had originally departed. They took me to see their king, and I told him all kinds of adventures. Immediately, he ordered the courtiers to take care of me and give me everything I needed.

I had a very happy time in this place. Soon I held a very high position in the dynasty. In short, no one was luckier than me, and everyone in the court and the town asked to be my friend.

Before long, everyone no longer regarded me as someone from another place, but as someone from their hometown.

One thing that surprised me very much was that when a person went out on horseback, I saw that he was riding on the bare back of the horse, without reins or stirrups. I went to the king to ask him why this was so.

I told him about the things we used in Baghdad. He didn't know what I meant, because he had never heard of the things I was talking about.

So I got someone to make a saddle for the horse's back, and also made stirrups to hang on both sides of the horse, and I also made a horse's bit and reins, and gave them all to the king.

The king ordered us to put them on a horse, then jumped on the horse and sat on the saddle, holding the reins.

He immediately saw their effectiveness. He was very happy to have these things, and gave me a large number of gifts. I made more of these things for the local dignitaries, and the gifts they gave me soon made me even richer.

Shen Bao China Travel Agency Travel Supplement

Traveling in Hangzhou 222

— Hao

The good thing about spring is the mild climate. It is green all over the fields. Everything is full of vitality and interest.

In the large glass windows of Shanghai department stores, if you see green and yellow window decorations, you will know that the so-called "Foreign Qingming" is approaching. Especially in Sullivan's window, with the American flag and Washington's portrait hanging, and many Qingming eggs, you will feel that this is a symbol of the arrival of spring. You should go out to relax.

People in Shanghai will think of traveling when they mention spring. They will also think of Hangzhou. Hangzhou seems to be the only destination for Shanghai people to travel. Going to Hangzhou, once a year, Hangzhou is never tiring. Here, I will write about the scenery of Hangzhou.

In recent years, Hangzhou has indeed made progress. The asphalt road allows you to sit in the car smoothly to the hotel. There are many standard clocks on the road. There are also urban red and green advertisements on the clock pillars. When each train arrives at the city station, crossing the overpass, crowding out of the gate, you will hear the hustle and bustle of hotel greeters. Of course, going to Shanghai, Beijing, or any big city, there are these greeting sounds. But when you arrive at the city station and hear the high and long greetings, you will obviously feel that you have arrived in Hangzhou.

In fact, when you arrive in Hangzhou, in West Lake, on the road, in the park, you will meet familiar people you often see in Shanghai. Or, you may meet friends in Shanghai that you can't often see, and you will meet with a smile. Meeting old friends in a foreign land.

In spring, everything in Hangzhou is expensive. The small boats floating on the lake, in the hot summer and cold winter, the daily cost is only one yuan. Now in spring, unless you spend four or five yuan, you will not be able to enjoy yourself on the lake. At noon, when the boat is rocked to the inner West Lake, the boatman will surely eagerly persuade you to have lunch at Lou Wai Lou. When you have eaten your fill of West Lake vinegar fish and stir-fried chicken, the boatman downstairs will also be full of wine and food, and look forward to it in high spirits. Of course, you have unknowingly paid for the boatman's meals. In addition, the boatman is very good at catering to your psychology. He will say what you want to say. He will very respectfully pin up the things you bought everywhere. But you must be careful. When the day's hard work is over, you should pay more tips for the wine. Otherwise, the face at parting is very ugly.

Speaking of Hangzhou's hotels, there are many. The hotels in the inner West Lake area have good Lounges, good rooms and bathrooms, which are specially for high-class foreigners and Chinese to live in. If you are financially well-off, why not step into these magnificent hotels and enjoy a few days of leisure. Originally, traveling is a luxurious thing. Why bother yourself and save everywhere, and find your own suffering in traveling. I think the most wonderful place in these high-class hotels is the very long corridor. When you wake up in the morning or are about to sleep, lying on the soft satin sofa, smoking a cigarette and drinking strong tea, the surrounding mountain scenery and sparkling water will envelop your whole mind. At this moment, you will think of the Western Hills of Beijing, Florence of Italy, and Interlaken of Switzerland. You will also think of all the romantic things in your life.

As for the hotels in the Hubin area, I will also report on them. The good thing about Hubin is that it is convenient for transportation and food. If you are not a person who likes loneliness, you can go to Hubin for a walk at any time at midnight or in the early morning. The hotels in Hubin are not bad either. Although the architecture is not as magnificent as the high-class hotels in the inner West Lake, it can still make you live happily. The white bed curtains and soft couches will surely make you sleep soundly after a day of travel.

The hotels in spring are quiet during the day. These travelers go out in the morning and come back at dusk. So the hotels are always very lonely except in the morning and evening. Because the waiters have nothing to do, they always sleep soundly in the afternoon. Spring is originally intoxicating. Under the warm sun, on the terrace in the rocking chair, lying the fat waiter, it can be said to be extremely happy.

The most devout is a group of incense-burning guests. They carry yellow bags of "Pilgrimage to the Mountains to Offer Incense". Whether it is Yuquan, Taoguang, or North Peak, they will move forward step by step. Who can know the bright and happy future.

In fact, the joy of traveling is not in how much the road is rushed, but in the spiritual pleasure. For example, if you get up in the morning and take a walk on Su Causeway, there are weeping willows and singing birds. You can take a walk. You can sit on a chair. You don't have to worry about everything. Undoubtedly, everything in this great nature is in your territory. Or you can muster up the courage and run all the way up North Peak. Qiantang River suddenly appears in front of you. You can know why Qiantang River is also called Zhi River. Because you can only see the shape of the river when you look at Qiantang River from North Peak. It is indeed a "之" character.

In short, Hangzhou is a place that you will never tire of going to. In this short article, I only write about the outline of Hangzhou.

Mountain Scenery and Lake Light 223

West Lake Itinerary 224

The scenic spots of West Lake cannot be fully enjoyed in just ten days. However, considering the economy of time and money, if the itinerary is slightly arranged, one can get a general overview in three to four days. Here is a proposed itinerary based on four days for your reference.

Day 1: Yue Fei's Tomb, Solid Stone Hill, Ge Hill, Ziyun Cave, Yellow Dragon Cave, Jade Spring Mountain, Lingyin Temple, Tao Guang Temple, Tianzhu Temple

The above locations are in the northwest of West Lake. You can take a rickshaw. Along the way, you will pass scenic spots such as the park, Xiling Seal Art Society, Su Xiaoxiao's Tomb, Qiu Jin's Tomb, and Xu Martyr's Tomb.

Day 2: Autumn Moon over the Peaceful Lake, Mid-Lake Pavilion, Three Pools Mirroring the Moon, Jingci Temple, Leifeng Pagoda Site, Liu Manor, Small Wanliu Hall, Gao Manor, Song Manor, Gushan Island, Crane Release Pavilion, Echoing Valley, Broken Bridge.

These are famous scenic spots on the lake. It is advisable to travel by boat.

Day 3: Zhang Cangshui Shrine, Stone House Cave, Yanxia Cave, Lian Temple, Nine Creeks and Eighteen Gullies, Dragon Well, South Peak, Faxiang Temple

The above locations are in the southwest of the lake. It is advisable to take an auto rickshaw and also walk.

Day 4: Jiuyao Mountain, Hupao Temple, Liuhe Pagoda, Zhakou, Nanxing Bridge, Wansongling

The above locations are in the south of the lake. You can take a car or rickshaw. After the tour, take advantage of the remaining time to purchase some famous Hangzhou products and then prepare for your return trip.

Tour of the Fuchun River 227

The steamboat departs from Nanxing Bridge. In less than half an hour, you will enter the well-known Fuchun River. You will immediately feel the clear mountains and waters, completely free of vulgarity. The scenery along the river is enough to please the eye. After about three hours, you will arrive at Tonglu. Tongjun Mountain stands in the middle of the river. On top of it is Tongjun Temple, which is said to be the place where a person from the Yellow Emperor's time gathered herbs. He could distinguish the properties of herbs and transformed beside a paulownia tree, hence the name Tongjun. After a while, you can reach Qililong. Yan Ziling's Fishing Platform is at the entrance of the Long. To the west, there is another platform, with a pavilion built on it, where Mr. Xie Gaoyu cried bitterly. Climbing the platform and looking down, the streams are deep and the abyss makes one's hair stand on end. It is already more than a hundred feet above the water. Xie Tingjian has a stele with the inscription "Eternal Pure Breeze." In Yan's ancestral hall, there is a couplet: "The fishing platform on the rock is high, let the whales stir up the waves in the vast sea, managing the fishing line, uniquely observing the world situation. The cloud path is close to the small boat, carrying a lone crane, indulging in the mountains and rivers, arranging poetry and wine, listening to the sound of the rapids from Qili." Beside the ancestral hall is the Guest Star Tower, where the deities of Xie Gaoyu and Su Dongpo are enshrined. In the tower, there is a couplet: "The Great Han for thousands of years, Mr. Yan alone." Also referring to Mr. Yan, the praise is extremely appropriate. At this point, it makes people recall the noble character and integrity of the two gentlemen, and deeply reflect on the competition for fame and profit. The scenery is outstanding, and visitors often linger and forget to return.

The Hangzhou branch of our company has organized a Fuchun River tour group. Those who wish to participate, please register at the Shanghai General Office on Sichuan Road.

Travelogue of Xuedou Mountain 228

— Yang Haoran

On the morning of the 29th, at 7:30 AM, I drove to the Ningbo-Fenghua Road station and took the 8:30 AM bus to Xikou. The fare was only 87 cents. (A small chartered car costs 11 yuan, which can go directly to the mountain pavilion). In about an hour, I reached my destination (Xikou). Then I walked to Wuling School. The school was founded by Mr. Chiang Kai-shek. The architecture is magnificent and can be called a model elementary school. After visiting, I went to Wenchang Pavilion (one of Chiang's residences). I was stopped by the guards, who said that I needed a permit from the principal of Wuling School to be allowed to enter and visit. So I turned to Chiang's ancestral hall, a place to honor ancestors and pursue the past, which made people feel respectful. After a week of inspection, it was already 11:00 AM. So I hired a sedan chair to go up the mountain. About five li to Baiyan (Chiang's mother's tomb), I went down and up the mountain. The guards asked if I had come to prepare a hotel here, and they were very polite. They led me from the gate to Chiang's mother's tomb, about three li. On both sides, pine and cypress trees were towering and green, and bamboo forests were forming. The middle was gravel. The road was very steep, and it was very difficult to walk straight up. Especially since I was wearing leather shoes, there was a danger of jumping every step. After walking about two li, I saw a few bungalows. An old woman greeted and led me to the inner room. There was an image of Chiang's mother in the room, with only two vases of flowers next to it. There was nothing else. In the next room, there were all inscriptions, such as Sun Yat-sen, Tan Yankai, and other relics, as well as sacrificial texts written by other party and state leaders Yu Youren, Dai Jitao, etc., displayed all over the wall. It can be said that it was a feast for the eyes to admire the calligraphy of many party and state elders. After the tour, I asked the old woman where Chiang's mother's tomb was. I only knew that it was still one li up the mountain. At this time, I was suddenly lost, thinking that since I came with great interest, how could I return halfway? So I still mustered up my courage to go up the mountain. When I reached the top of the mountain, I felt very tired. I turned to the tomb. The architecture was extremely ordinary. Only the tombstone was written by Sun Yat-sen. After hesitating for a while, I hurried down the mountain and moved forward. Not five li, I arrived at the mountain pavilion. The pavilion was built with funds from Mr. Du Yuesheng. There are monks from Xuebao Temple here to entertain tourists. It was already 1:00 PM. I was hungry, so I continued to move forward. About five li, all uphill, passed through the Han Hua Yushu Pavilion. The hostel built by our company was already in sight. I went to Xueshi Temple to fill my stomach first, and then went to the hostel with Dong (the foreman of the construction factory building the hostel) to inspect the interior. After the tour, I went to Miaogao Terrace.

On the morning of the 30th, after a light breakfast, I went with Mr. Dong and others to Yintan. From Shangxue Road, I passed through Xikan to visit the Peasant Reading Center. After passing Eighteen Bends, I climbed Xiefeng. About three li, I reached Fengci Temple. I turned back to the road to Yintan and forked to Yintan Temple. There were also dozens of peasant children reading books inside the temple. After leaving the temple and crossing a stone bridge, I arrived at Shangyintan. Then I went to Qianzhang Cliff and looked up at Yizhi Bridge (the waterfall viewing bridge). There was a pavilion next to it. The architecture was very elaborate, but no one lived there. It looked like it was dilapidated. Leaning on the bridge and looking up at the Qianzhang Cliff waterfall, the shape and sound were magnificent and unparalleled. After crossing the bridge and following the road under the pavilion, I returned to the temple via the Yushu Pavilion. It was already 5:00 PM.

On the morning of the 1st, I visited Xuedou Temple. The temple is one of the Ten Zen Temples and has a magnificent architecture. The temple is divided into three buildings. At the entrance, there are five characters "The First Mountain of Siming" written by Chiang Kai-shek himself, as well as two ginkgo trees. Now I append a tourist itinerary for your reference.

Day 1: Take a bus to Xikou at 7:00 or 8:00 AM. (Soon it will be possible to go directly to the mountain, but a small chartered car can already go directly). Visit Wuling School, Wuling Farm, Wenchang Pavilion, and Chiang's ancestral hall.

(You must first obtain a permit from the principal of Wuling School). Then take the sedan chair to Baiyan to visit Chiang's mother's tomb. (The sedan chair fee from Xikou to our hostel is $1.20). Then pass through the Inshan Han Hua Yushu Pavilion to our hostel for lunch. In the afternoon, visit Feixue Pavilion, see the Qianzhang Cliff Waterfall and Miaogao Terrace.

Day 2: After breakfast, take the sedan chair from Shangxue Road through Xikan. Visit the Xuebao Peasant Reading Center. Then visit Fengci Temple. Return to the hostel for lunch. In the afternoon, visit Shangyintan and Xiayintan. Then turn to Qianzhang Cliff and look down at the waterfall from Guanpu Bridge, and return to the hostel for dinner.

Day 3: Visit Xuedou Temple, have lunch, and then depart from the hostel at 12:30 PM. Arrive at Xikou to catch the 2:00 or 3:00 o'clock bus back to Ningbo, and you can still catch the boat to Shanghai.

I love the cinnabar spring. Neither cool nor hot. There is sulfur and mercury below.

Spraying like pearls. Dug into a square pool. The water is fragrant and clean.

A line leaking from a stone cave. Trickling into the pool, the temperature is excellent.

Huaqing does not have this wonder. Tangshan is also inferior. Bathers are increasing day by day.

Wide acceptance regardless of rank. Makes the body clean. Further makes the spirit happy.
