Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Amateur Chat

A Review of Singleness 231

— Jun Wen

In today's society, there are many women who have received secondary or even higher education, who are blindly advocating or practicing singleness. Although this non-doctrine doctrine does not seem to have aroused the discussion of great scholars in women's issues, its importance is by no means diminished by this. Before we discuss the issue of singleness, it may be helpful to briefly describe its origin. The trend of singleness is not limited to women alone, but men also have this custom. Undoubtedly, its most prosperous era was when religious power was at its strongest and divine power was above all else. Because at that time, people believed that only the power of God was the greatest; believing in God would not only allow them to enter heaven after death, but also increase their happiness in their current lives through the protection of God. Thus, many people sacrificed the happiness of their lives, suppressed their desires, remained unmarried, and devoted themselves to serving God; or limited themselves to embracing singleness for a certain period. The most common example is the monks and nuns in Buddhism, followed by priests in ancient Egypt and Greece, the vestal virgins in Rome, and the Saigu in the Grand Shrine of Ise in Japan; in addition, ascetics in the Brahmin clan and a sect in Christianity all embrace singleness. This kind of singleness sacrificed for God, this immoral ascetic behavior, only shows the low level of human knowledge in that era, and has no other significance.

Since the existence of mankind, there has been the matter of male and female intercourse; of course, this sexual desire is innate. We Chinese have an old saying that food and sex are human nature. Havelock Ellis also said: old maids and ascetic youths are easily spotted in any country, in any region. The force of suppressed natural impulses is dangerous evidence. Female nymphomania and various hysterias are mostly caused by this. From this, it can be seen that obstructing the impulse of sexual desire is an abnormal act that violates physiology and nature. Therefore, in the eleventh century, many people in Europe who had to embrace asceticism were influenced by the licentious customs of Rome, and used various unreasonable methods to satisfy their desires. Therefore, at that time, the life in many monasteries and temples that were called ascetic was more romantic than the life in brothels. At the same time, during the Crusades, many women organized women's armies to be comforters for soldiers on the battlefield due to the difficulty of getting married. These old facts powerfully prove that human beings, whether male or female, need the opposite sex equally. Therefore, from the temporary pairing marriage in ancient times to today's free love, although the system has undergone many changes, marriage is still a major issue, and this is the reason.

Rousseau once said in his book Emile: The duty of women is to assist us men, comfort us men, gain the love and affection of men, and be comforters for men, so that men can easily and happily walk the path of life. Whether this statement is appropriate, we will not say for the time being; however, the importance of the spiritual needs of both sexes can be seen from this. Kant expressed this idea most thoroughly. He said: Men and women can only become complete people when they are combined. The healthy development of mankind is based on the proper combination of the two sexes. The satisfaction of sexual desire is an essential element for the physical and mental health of men and women. As for Havelock Ellis's opinion, he believes that human beings are not animals, and physical harmony is not enough to satisfy their higher desires. Therefore, there must be spiritual harmony and attraction. If there is no spirit, sexual intercourse will only become a mechanical and immoral act. We no longer need to quote other people's words, it is enough to prove that singleness runs counter to human spiritual harmony and excitement. At the same time, we can make further discussions here. The reason why women are currently advocating singleness is of course not for the sake of God; however, they think that marriage is an accompanying event that increases spiritual pain, especially for women who are engaged in occupations, they regard marriage as a waste in life, and even observe various hardships from actual life, so they regard marriage as a dangerous road. In fact, this kind of observation is enough to show their short-sightedness, because based on the principle of marriage, marriage is not a painful thing; in other words, it is an abnormal phenomenon to increase pain and hinder the progress of career for the sake of marriage. In theory, under the mutual encouragement and help between the two sexes, there should be extra progress for his or her career. Therefore, from the perspective of this spiritual need, advocating singleness is simply heading for self-destruction.

The soundness of a nation and the strength of a country, although not a simple issue, are inseparable from the fundamental element of the people. Therefore, although countries are suffering from depression and unemployment, governments are still encouraging production. Especially in China, due to years of war, years of natural disasters, and the death of people due to ignorance of hygiene, the mortality rate is higher than in all other countries. If we advocate the so-called singleness at this time, it will not only fail to make the country and nation strong, but also be an active national suicide policy. Therefore, from the standpoint of the country, this kind of singleness is definitely not needed.

Outlying Postal Agency

Women of the Land of Abundance 232

— Yao

Chengdu Correspondence

The so-called cultural center of the "Land of Abundance" is Chengdu, the capital of Sichuan Province. All the foreign goods enjoyed by modern Shanghai women are available in the department stores of Chengdu, catering to the needs of modern Chengdu women. Moreover, Shanghai women's modern attire and dating styles are also流行 (popluar) in all aspects of Chengdu women's lives along with various commodities and film dramas. It is no wonder that many Sichuan people call it "Little Shanghai." Anyone who has lived in Sichuan must admit that many women from various counties envy the material culture and open-mindedness enjoyed by Chengdu women. However, there is another matter that we cannot fail to mention: outside the urban area of Chengdu, alongside any of the thoroughfares that connect with the countryside, stand countless "Martyr Women's Monuments" or "Filial Piety Memorial Arches." These feudal relics have not been eliminated by the traffic of automobiles on the roads. On the contrary, they are still revered by tens of thousands of women. Not only rural women, but also women from Chengdu and other cities, constantly visit these "Martyr Women's Monuments" or "Filial Piety Memorial Arches" to offer incense. From these two situations, it is clear that the lives of Chengdu women are arranged between two extremes: the extremely new and the extremely old. The following is a detailed account, divided into sections, for the reference of those who study social issues.

(I) Their Lives and Status in the Family

(A) Urban Housewives

The city's women can be roughly divided into three categories:

The first category is the women of wealthy families. This includes the wives and daughters of military officers and important officials, the mistresses of big businessmen, and the women of large landowners. They enjoy material civilization in great abundance: their use of servants and maids is quite in the style of the feudal aristocracy. Like those undisciplined warlords, they often use their power to dominate others, either running over pedestrians on the road in their private cars or fighting for seats with others in public entertainment venues.

The second category is the housewives of middle-class merchants, salaried professionals, and small landlords. Although their economic power is not as great as that of wealthy families, sufficient for their own extravagant waste, their family finances are constantly in a precarious state. Under the pressure of snobbery, they appear even more eager to flaunt their status. Therefore, most women from these middle-class families like to keep slaves and maids (called "丫頭" (丫頭) in Chengdu). Various kinds of flattering superiors and condescending to inferiors are prominent in them. The ability to calculate for themselves and glib talk can be said to be their special strengths.

The third category is the housewives of poorer or manual labor families. Their husbands are mostly coolies or peddlers. In order to help support their families, they spend most of

Page 24

their time washing clothes, sewing, changing weft threads for silk weaving workshops, sewing sock openings for sock factories, and doing various similar jobs for others. They have relatively independent living skills. Unfortunately, even with year-round hard work, it is difficult for them to afford their children even a basic education. But, strangely enough, precisely because they have experienced more of the ways of the world in their lives, they are particularly envious of the enjoyment and boasting of women from wealthy and middle-class families.

(B) Rural Housewives

As for rural housewives, they can also be divided into three categories:

The first category is the women of wealthy gentry families. Although they are purely landlords or grain households, due to the influence of various warlords, local bullies, and evil gentry, they also tend to follow the trend of the times. On the one hand, they try to gloss over their family's economic affluence, and on the other hand, they put on the airs of aristocratic ladies. This can be clearly seen in their interactions with ordinary people in the countryside, or in their attire, showing their arrogance and extravagance. Especially during festivals when "喜神會" (喜神會) are held in small towns under their control, or when "城隍" (城隍) and "關聖人" (關聖人) parades are organized, their power can be seen everywhere.

The second category is the housewives of middle peasants or tenant farmers. These are the typical simple rural women. In addition to taking care of all the household chores, such as clothing, food, and shelter, they also have to raise young children. During the busy farming season, they also have to go to the fields, sinking their bound feet into the muddy paddies. The result of their hard work may barely sustain their livelihood, but when heavy taxes and levies make their family situation difficult, they often lament that they have suffered their entire lives, without even enjoying the material life of being a maid or wet nurse in the city.

The third category is the housewives who own only two or three acres of land or who are purely hired laborers or wet nurses. Their husbands are usually engaged in farming, either for others or for themselves, without fixed hours. In their spare time, they engage in small-scale mobile businesses with a capital of one or two dollars, earning a small income by transporting vegetables, fruits, coal, and other goods. However, this meager income is not enough to cover household expenses; therefore, most of them are forced to go out to work as maids.

(II) Women Going to School

Since the "May Fourth Movement" and the advocacy of "Women Must Receive Education" became popular throughout the country, Chengdu was the first to open girls' classes in various primary, middle, universities, and vocational schools. Many schools had already converted to co-educational classes several years ago. As for the number of students in women's normal schools or women's schools, it seems to be even more enthusiastic than in general men's schools. Up to now, it can be said that the appearance of women's education in Chengdu is quite impressive.

So, how much real knowledge do they actually learn in school? Considering the financial difficulties of Chengdu's education and the self-deception of the general faculty and staff due to the lack of job security, the average female student certainly does not receive adequate education (not the "合格" (合格) graded by the teachers, but the "合格" (合格) of the ordinary required level). On average, each semester is only twelve or thirteen weeks, at most sixteen or seventeen weeks, and rarely twenty weeks of instruction; there are also holidays and even times when classes are suspended due to various disturbances. Therefore, in terms of knowledge cultivation, eight or nine out of ten of them are very deficient.

What about moral education? Many schools are indeed stricter in their management, but many schools do not even do the bare minimum. We have encountered poor female students working as prostitutes and unexpectedly meeting their "夫子大人" (夫子大人) at a lavish banquet of drinking and flower wine. At that time, the students recognized the teacher, but the teacher did not recognize the student? This is naturally the result of the imperfection of the educational institutions. However, at the same time, we should mention the arrogant and extravagant power of many aristocratic young ladies in the school, which often guarantees their habit of "校外自由" (校外自由) outside of school; this habit has long made it impossible for the faculty and staff to control them. They flaunt their power with the bodyguards and guards raised by their family members and friends. Faculty and staff often have no choice but to turn a blind eye to avoid disputes outside the school.

Although the number of aristocratic women and poor prostitute-like female students mentioned above is not large in the school, their level of modernness and their arrogant and vain temperaments undoubtedly play a leading role in the school. Therefore, the absolute majority of pure women are unknowingly affected. In such an environment, I have seen modern female students tell their classmates that their parents who came from the countryside to Chengdu schools to send her money are her "傭僕" (傭僕) (servants). The reason is probably because their parents are dressed too simply! There are many interesting anecdotes similar to this strange situation. Of course, we should know that many female students are still tightly controlled by the subconsciousness of old families, but the so-called progress, openness, modernness…etc. tendencies are, after all, more powerfully attracting them in school. Therefore, school education has ultimately failed to show them a true path for new women.

(III) Women Seeking Careers

In recent years, many sock factories or sewing companies have been established in Chengdu. Many small entrepreneurs have spent a lot of effort studying how to promote industry and calling on women to participate in production. As a result, many women are also enthusiastically wanting to acquire a "一技之長" (一技之長) (skill) to seek independent living or to transform their families. Sure enough, many women have indeed learned skills very well, but unfortunately, the announcement of "公司關門" (公司關門) (company closure) was announced in a short moment.

Many women, after graduating from the factory, mostly cannot find normal work. Some return to various counties to purchase a dozen machines to engage in their own business, but eight or nine out of ten fail. Because those ten-yarn (local cotton yarn) and non-electric dyed thread socks or silk stockings are not as cheap and good as Shanghai or imported products. Even if there are people who occasionally have access to business, they cannot but roll up their flags and rest due to the impact of donations and taxes and wars. Moreover, most of the sock-making machines they are currently using in Chengdu are still old machines from Shanghai and foreign countries several years ago. Because those small entrepreneurs, seeing the business slump, "見風轉柁" (見風轉柁) (turned with the wind) and turned the factory into a side business, and held so-called vocational schools, on the one hand, they could collect a large amount of tuition fees, and at the same time, they had to sell old machines. Machines that cost twenty or thirty yuan in Shanghai, they forced the female students who went to the factory to learn to order one each. The price is set at around one hundred yuan. Little do they know that once they move them home and actually use them, they find that they are scrap iron.

In Chengdu, in addition to this large number of professional women who are displaced, there are also several obstetrics schools. However, their level of immaturity is not much different from the unlicensed obstetrics hospitals in Shanghai that recklessly recruit nurses and take advantage of them to obtain hundred-yuan deposits.

The "花瓶" (花瓶) (decorative) system of employing women in shops and offices has not yet been pioneered. The employment of female waitresses cannot be found in the whole city.

As for those professional women who make a living by selling their bodies, on the surface, it seems that they are not as powerful as the prostitutes in Beijing and Shanghai. However, the two famous areas of "興化街" (興化街) and "五台山" (五台山) are still openly paying flower donations to the authorities. In addition, there are many private prostitutes who dress up as female students or aunts and young ladies, attracting bees and butterflies everywhere. Although their business is not bad, their tragic lives are imaginable!

(IV) Their Love and Marriage

People in Chengdu have long considered the hypocrisy of "自由戀愛" (自由戀愛) (free love) to be terrible. Therefore, many parents still adopt the method of "父母之命媒妁之言" (父母之命媒妁之言) (parents' orders and matchmakers' words) for their children's marriages. Generally, more enlightened parents usually look for families that are well-matched, first discuss the marriage contract without fixing it, and try to let their children meet once or twice. As long as they do not have major dissatisfaction with each other, they can get engaged under the "勢利相投" (勢利相投) (common interests). Under this passive "enlightened" method, men usually have not been in contact with women, and women do not seem to have any fixed prejudices. Therefore, in this semi-free and semi-constrained marriage relationship, it is not combined by love, nor by academic thoughts, nor by the country and society—it is only that most declining families pursue power and profit through their children's marriage problems. As a result of this situation, seven or eight out of ten are depressed and decadent, and two or three out of ten are preparing to publish divorce notices in the newspaper shortly after marriage. Therefore, to put it bluntly, women in Chengdu rarely have true love at all. In fact, many women are destroyed and sacrificed by feudal forces under the false names of freedom or love.

Many women from poor families see the power relations in Chengdu very clearly. Many parents are determined not to marry their daughters unless they are military officers. Therefore, even lower-ranking officers such as platoon leaders or adjutants can easily find women to date or marry. But the most unfortunate women are precisely them. In most cases, the officers eventually bury them within the ranks of private prostitutes.

In addition, many women from well-off families, after marrying hard-working craftsmen or self-cultivating farmers, often have countless happy and truly loving couples because of everyone's hard work and cooperation in life. This is the only remaining fruit of Chengdu's petty-bourgeois economy and free rural areas. They live a beautiful and leisurely life in the "Land of Abundance", and even their personalities become particularly peaceful and generous. What a pity is that the number of such women who combine love and life is gradually decreasing and disappearing very quickly.

Celebrity Interview

Interview with Sculptor Jiang Xiaoqian 233

— Ruoyu

Having visited the Shanghai Art Preview Exhibition, which showcased such a rich collection of ancient bronze and jade carvings, I couldn't help but think of several modern artists engaged in carving.

What we were able to see in this preview was only a fraction of all the "antiques," yet it was enough to spend half a day appreciating them. The sheer quantity was astonishing. After seeing the vast amount of "antiques" left behind by the hard work of previous artists, it is inevitable that we have high expectations for modern carving artists. However, if we look back at the works achieved by modern carving artists, it is questionable whether their artistic value can be compared with "antiques." In terms of quantity, it is indeed a little disheartening. From this, we can imagine that the efforts and hard work of previous artists in art are indeed worthy of emulation by those who engage in art later on.

Because I am more easily interested in the art of carving, I seemed to be not fully satisfied after visiting the art preview. So, we found an acquaintance to introduce us, and then ran to Hongqiao Road to visit the famous modern sculptor Mr. Jiang Xiaoqian, because I had long heard that his home has many carvings and modern "antiques" (?).

When we arrived there, it was already about four o'clock in the afternoon, and the weather was so dark and about to rain; therefore, at the moment we met, Mr. Sun hurriedly explained the purpose of our visit on my behalf.

Before meeting Mr. Jiang, I had already sketched such an outline of his appearance in my mind: a fair face, long hair, wearing a suit, and often interspersing one or two English or French sentences when speaking. However, when Mr. Sun introduced me, I was suddenly surprised. It turned out that his attitude and face were exactly the same as Mr. Li Shizeng, the current member of the Central Committee. The sleeves of a crimson gown were already a little furry and "拖鬚擺柳" (拖鬚擺柳) (trailing like willow branches); he wore a pair of cloth shoes, showing a very mature and prudent demeanor when walking.

After listening to Mr. Sun's introduction, he happily led us to sit down in a delicate guest room: after some greetings, I found a question and started the interview.

"Mr. Jiang probably went to visit the art preview recently held in Shanghai?" This question is not very practical, I thought to myself.

"I wanted to see it, but I haven't had time these two days. You must have visited it?" He smiled.

"I did see it, but it's like 'Grandma Liu entering the Grand View Garden,' I don't understand anything! If Mr. Jiang went to take a look, he could give an artistic evaluation of the many ancient carvings." I said humbly.

"I dare not make a light criticism." He shook his head slightly, and then said: "But after seeing it, maybe there are many things worth learning from; I think a person engaged in art is like a person studying literature, he must humbly accept the legacy of his predecessors. The success of previous artists in skills does make us later 'artisans' a little '望塵莫及' (望塵莫及) (unable to catch up). Now, just take myself as an example, as a person engaged in carving for nearly twenty years, I have always dared not consider any of my works to be successful. From this, you can imagine that carving art is indeed not an easy job to do well." He frowned, showing a dissatisfied depression.

"In what year did Mr. Jiang's carving career begin?" I asked.

"It's a long story," he took a puff of cigarette, slowly reminiscing: After a while, he said, "At first, I originally studied portrait painting in Japan. Later, I felt that portrait painting seemed to have many places that could not be expressed as a whole. Even if the painting skills were learned to the point of perfection, it was still impossible to express a person's image as a whole from the paper as much as he wanted. So, after living in Japan for five years, I ran to France to start learning the art of sculpture. I also lived in France for five full years, and finally learned a little bit of what I wanted to learn; however, the reason why I was able to gain some insights into learning sculpture is entirely due to my foundation in learning portrait painting. Because if you study sculpture without the experience of painting, it takes a lot of time, but it is still difficult to achieve success."

"What is Mr. Jiang's first successful work?"

"I dare not say that. I said just now that I don't dare to consider any of the works I have completed to be successful. Moreover, I have now almost formed a state of professional life for carving, and for a work, I am often restricted by the other party due to economic reasons; it seems like a craftsman, although I have a very good performance for a work, the customer's favorite is not necessarily your so-called proud work. If I reluctantly say that there are one or two works that I am satisfied with, then there are only the bronze statue of the late Shanghai yarn tycoon Wu Linshu and the statue of Mr. Ma Xiangbo now, but this is only what I think is satisfactory." He laughed heartily: "Now these two statues are still in the factory over there, you might as well go and take a look."

We came out of that guest room, and he walked in front; after passing through a small garden, not far ahead was a factory building built of white iron, like a "glass shed" in a movie studio, with an area of ​​more than ten acres.

The first room when entering the door is the carving room. Here are dozens of plaster statues that have been turned over to bronze and "泥胎" (泥胎) (clay figures) that are being carved. Each unfinished "泥胎" (泥胎) (clay figure) has a very thick piece of damp cloth wrapped around it, like wounded soldiers with injured skulls in a hospital. Suddenly seeing it, I can't help but feel a slight contraction in my nerves.

He rushed into this carving room, busily instructing the workers to uncover the damp cloths on all the "泥胎" (泥胎) (clay figures) one by one, and told me what these "泥胎" (泥胎) (clay figures) were, how much carving work there was, and after how much time could they be turned into plaster models. He talked so eloquently while pointing and drawing, as if a biology teacher was teaching students

Statue of Mr. Ma Xiangbo 234

— One of Mr. Jiang Xiaoqian's recent works —

Portrait of Mr. Wu Linshu, Founder of Tongyi Cotton Mill 235

Page 27

as detailed as if he were giving a lesson.

Finally, I saw the statues of the cotton industry tycoon Wu Linshu and Mr. Ma Xiangbo that he had mentioned.

Wu Linshu's bronze statue is in a sitting pose, which is rare for general commemorative bronze statues. However, the sculpting skill is indeed beyond description.

"Isn't this pose for the bronze statue probably unique in China?" I felt a little strange.

"Yes, general commemorative bronze statues are all three-dimensional, but this one is an exception. However, this is the work I am most satisfied with. When sculpting this bronze statue, I was not restricted in my thinking. However, when I first contacted them, it took a lot of persuasion. In the end, I was willing to compromise on the remuneration before they agreed to let me complete this work according to my ideas." A joyful expression filled his face.

Walking in from the sculpture studio is the bronze casting factory. It is equipped with two large copper smelting furnaces and a rolling machine that can roll up to fifteen tons. In the center of the factory building, three iron chains as thick as fingers are hung high on the beam. Under these iron chains is a copper smelting furnace. After the copper is melted in the furnace, the hot copper is lifted high with iron chains and poured into the copper mold, and then the "bronze body" is successfully made.

This kind of bronze casting equipment doesn't seem that complicated, but it is still unique in modern China for a sculptor to also run a bronze casting factory.

"This method of bronze casting existed in China during the Six Dynasties. However, ancient artists often had an unavoidable bad habit: they preferred to keep a unique skill they learned secret until they died, rather than passing it on. Therefore, this method of bronze casting gradually became unknown. Now that we want to use it, we still have to run to foreign countries to ask for help! After I returned to China, I immediately took on a bronze statue of Mr. Chen Yingshi, with a deadline of ten months. However, I sculpted the 'clay model', but there was no way to solve the bronze casting for a while. Although it would be very convenient to send it to Japan for casting, the time was already very tight. At the same time, I felt that a person engaged in sculpture shouldn't have to ask others for help with their basic skills. As a result, I decided to cast it myself. I temporarily found many coachmen and servants from relatives' homes to be workers and trained them for more than a month. Everyone was very interested in this work and learned some applied techniques. The bronze statue of Mr. Chen Yingshi was completed in this small, makeshift bronze casting factory after nine experiments, and I completed my debut work of bronze casting one month before the deadline. Now, these workers who used to be coachmen have very good bronze casting skills. Recently, almost all of my works, regarding the bronze casting part, have been done automatically by them."

As he spoke, he led us into a very small engraving room. It consisted of two connected rooms: one contained brand-new copper engraving machines and many engraved copper molds of various sizes; the other contained dozens of bronze objects with mottled colors. Judging from the style and the writing on them, most people probably couldn't tell that they were imitations made by modern people.

"When I bought this copper engraving machine, even the foreign company that sold it couldn't tell me how to use it, and I had no experience with this kind of machine. However, in order to achieve an art craft in the future, I had to buy such a machine. As a result, I bought it back. Every day, I and the general workers do this kind of experimental work like apprentices. Now, we have achieved some success and engraved a lot of copper molds and seals." He took out more than a dozen kinds of copper molds and seals from the glass cabinet for me to see.

"It will be easy to establish an art factory in the future," I said.

"You have to keep moving forward like this, but whether it can proceed smoothly still requires a lot of effort!" He said with a very modest expression.

A Week of Travel

A Visit to "Yuan's Tomb" 236

— Bai Ying

The other day, on the Pinghan Railway, although I had circled around a few times, I had not specifically gotten off the train to sightsee in Zhangde City, which is close to the railway. This time, from Hankou to Beiping, the train happened to pass Zhangde and I happened to run into an old friend, Mr. Pan. He originally worked on the railway but was recently transferred here, so he strongly invited me to get off the train and stay for a few days.

When we got out of the platform, what greeted us was a gust of wind mixed with yellow sand. This welcoming ceremony almost made me unable to open my eyes, and immediately gave me a few bad impressions. When we were about to enter the city (the station is about two li away from the city), the dilapidated city wall in the medieval style aroused my bad feelings again. After entering the city gate, the low houses and dirty streets aged my mood!

The next day was the second day of the third month of the lunar calendar (two days before the Qingming Festival). Mr. Pan invited me to visit "Yuan's Tomb" and Yuan's Garden—the so-called "Yuan's Tomb" is the tomb of Yuan Shikai, which is simply called Yuan's Tomb by the locals. It is about seven or eight li away from Zhangde City, and a rickshaw can go directly there. However, because the road was near, we were willing to walk, so as to take a look at the spring suburbs of the North. However, the spring suburbs of the North are not as beautiful as those in the South, and the weather was gloomy this day, making the wilderness feel even more bleak. The strong wind did not understand the mood of the tourists, and gusts of dust and sand slammed into our faces, so the awareness that the North had no spring became more intense!

When we were about to arrive at Yuan's Tomb, what caught our attention first was the majestic screen wall, which was entirely made of stone. It was about four zhang high and more than ten zhang wide. The "dragon coiling" and "phoenix dancing" carved on it were not very exquisite, and were much inferior to the old carvings. From the screen wall to the tomb is about two li, separated by a small ditch. After crossing the ditch, there is a wide asphalt road (maybe "three-in-one soil") leading directly to the cemetery.

The cemetery covers an area of about twenty mu, and is planted with Chinese arborvitae and dwarf pines all around, which are about to become a forest. In this desert-like plain, the addition of these young pines and cypresses makes it feel green and lovely. The cemetery has four entrances. The first entrance (Langtou Gate) is an open dam paved with rough stones. A pointed pavilion stands in the center, covered with a square tombstone about two zhang high. The tombstone is inlaid with marble. On the front is written "Tomb of President Yuan Shikai" in large letters, with the words "Established on an auspicious day in × month of the eighth year of the Republic of China" next to it. On the other three sides, there is no description of his "deeds." At that time, I was very suspicious as to why the descendants of this great man with a glorious life did not write his great achievements on the tombstone to pass on to future generations. If it were described, there would be titles such as "Minister of Internal Affairs of the Qing Dynasty", "President of the Republic of China", and "Hongxian Emperor". How magnificent this is! Then I realized that there were unspeakable reasons, so I admired the cleverness of his descendants!

The second entrance is also an open dam paved with rough stones. Lions, elephants, tigers, leopards, cattle, and horses stand on both sides. These beasts are all carved from marble, which can be regarded as precious things in this northern land without stone! I know that "lions," "tigers," and "leopards" symbolize power and also have the meaning of "suppressing evil spirits" and "configuring feng shui," while "elephants" symbolize many blessings and longevity, which also has a profound reason. As for the origins and functions of "cattle" and "horses," I am a bit vague. Could it be to indicate that future generations have horses to ride and cattle to till the fields? Or does it imply that this "great man" used the people as cattle and horses during his lifetime? Only "feng shui masters" can answer this. I don't care.

The third entrance is the tomb itself. The tomb platform is more than a zhang high and round, with a diameter of about four zhang. The tomb is more than two zhang high, with a diameter of more than two zhang. In front of the tomb is a flat stele, on which the god of fortune and longevity birds are carved, and the carving is relatively delicate. The railings around the tomb platform are stone pillars strung with iron chains, just like the railings of the residences of wealthy people in big cities. In total, the tomb platform, tombstone, tomb itself, as well as the stone pillars and stairs, are all inlaid with marble. If it weren't for the fact that the years had been a bit long and it had been eroded by wind and rain, it would really be a piece of white, as if walking into a silver world!

Behind the tomb is a wall. Entering through the side door is the fourth entrance. All the houses inside are vermilion doors and pink walls, which are obviously the places where the tomb keepers live. However, we peered into every room, and there was no so-called "filial son guarding the tomb," not even a servant. The houses were full of dust, as if no one had ever been there. The doors were locked tightly, seemingly unopened for a long time.

The cemetery is not guarded, so people can come and go without restraint. On the marble stele and tomb platform, many inscriptions of amateur poets were found, some of which were casual poems, and some ridiculed "Lord Yuan"! As for the pavilions and arches, in short, all places that can shelter from the wind and rain have become resting places for cowherds and hostels for beggars. It is said that every summer, most of the nearby farmers come here to cool off and sleep here at night. The flat stone slabs are naturally more comfortable than their dirty earthen dams. Lord Yuan truly deserves to be a great man of his generation, even the burial place after his death shelters the common people. However, it is said that there are four tombs of Lord Yuan in total (he is from Xiangcheng, and there is always a more magnificent tomb in his hometown. I heard that there is also a tomb in Xinxiang County, but I don't know where his remains are buried). The one left in Zhangde is the least magnificent and occupies the least amount of land. In this case, the other three must be even more spectacular.

Walking out of the cemetery and stepping onto the asphalt road, a cool breeze blew and drizzle sprinkled on our heads. As a result, our original plan to visit Yuan's Garden after visiting Yuan's Tomb failed.

Miscellaneous Works

Gleanings of Dialect 237

— Cun

The Chinese language is the most complex and non-unified, which is a major obstacle to the unification and development of Chinese culture. It is no wonder that many insightful people consider it a regrettable thing. Many people with good intentions have been working hard to promote phonetic alphabets, the standard Mandarin, and the collection of dialects, slang, and folk songs. We hope that gradually there will be some achievements, which will not only facilitate the advancement of Chinese culture, but also facilitate travelers and pedestrians a lot.

In general daily language, not only are the pronunciations different in various places, the sentence structures vary with space, and there are even many metaphorical riddles mixed in the conversations, making it incomprehensible to outsiders. People who generally pay attention to language unification have never mentioned the collection of such riddles, but I think it is also necessary to collect them. Riddles in daily language exist in the languages ​​of all provinces and regions, and some riddles are very interesting. It is especially popular in the countryside. Although there are many miswritten characters and mispronounced sounds, it can be seen that the farmers' ability to imagine analogies is not weak. We also need to fully understand the terms they use in order to easily communicate with them and understand what they mean. I don’t know if there are such riddles mixed in languages ​​elsewhere. Now, let’s list some examples of the riddles circulating in our countryside for everyone’s reference. (Some of them are very vulgar and ugly words, but because they are for studying language, it is okay to list them. Readers can ignore their meaning.)

Original Riddle Riddle's Meaning

"Take off your pants and fight a tiger" "Shameless and reckless"

"A crooked-mouthed woman looking in a mirror" "Laughing to your face"

"Take off your pants and spank your butt" "Redundant effort"

"A sparrow jumping into coarse chaff" "Empty joy"

"The City God Temple's fence" "Resisting ghosts" (meaning resisting others in the middle, preventing them from completing good deeds)

"Giving away things and burning incense" "Pretending to be a decent person" (in our countryside, prostitutes are called "giving away things")

"A deaf-mute eating Coptis chinensis" "Unable to express the bitterness"

"Turtles in jars" "Easy to catch"

"The brains of a tailor" "Taken seriously" ("Taken seriously" is a mispronunciation of "taking a needle." Tailors often take needles and put them on their heads when sewing clothes. The needle is easy to stick into the cloth after it is exposed to sweat)

Page 28

"Mama Wang's bound feet" "Smelly and long"

"Light shadows scratching the back" "Doubled flattery" (light shadows are leather figures carved from cowhide, used to sing shadow plays on a screen. The hands of the leather figures are simply carved into two fingers. Doubled flattery means to flatter twice as much)

"Robbers selling baskets" "Concealment" (meaning to conceal their own faces with this)

"Eating porridge with rice water" "Incurably poor" (people are too poor to afford dry rice, so they eat porridge and add rice water, so they are said to be incurably poor)

"Mice climbing on a steelyard" "Self-praise" (meaning self-praise)

"Duck's foot" "Twisted" (meaning to cause trouble, ducks walk in a twisted way)

"Deer eating gray noodles" "Messed up his nose with ash" (meaning that people are not appreciated, and their faces are covered in shameful ash)

"Rats eating rice soup" "Covering the mouth" (rats are mice, covering the mouth means just eking out a living)

"Rats accumulating cow horns" "The more you accumulate, the tighter it gets"

"Rats crossing the street" "Asking for a beating"

"Beggars sitting on smoking baskets" "Ungrateful"

"Dogs biting mosquitoes" "Randomly bumping"

The above are just the riddles that I can remember. There are many more such riddles. When farmers in the countryside speak, they often only say one riddle. If you don't understand the meaning of the riddle, you simply don't understand what they are saying. I think it is necessary for friends who go to the countryside to work to know these riddles.

Biography of Celebrities

The Pure Poet Shelley (1) 239

— Written by Japanese Tsurumi Yusuke, Translated by Zhou Leshan and Qi Junfu

One

It is a great practical joke of fate that Shelley and Byron were produced in the common-sense, utilitarian England.

Therefore, the life of these two geniuses is a great tragedy. The two poets were tossed, vomited, and scolded by the great power of society, like two tiny drops of oil floating on the vast water.

However, there is probably no one who hates the power and money desires and ordinary views of life held by the British who does not love Shelley's purity and Byron's hot blood! The reason why England can become a great power in the world is not because of their materialism, desire for conquest, and human manipulation, but because in their country, there will sometimes be people like Shelley who have no materialism, Byron who has no compromise, and Moore who is foolishly honest. The greatness of the British lies in the incredible confusion of common sense and non-common sense. The British only know how to pay attention to their appetites, so they are scolded by the French and Germans. However, it produces people like Shelley who have no appetite at all. This is England's incredible power.

Therefore, Shelley, who was persecuted so much during his lifetime, had his commemorative statue built by Oxford University, which had expelled him a hundred years after his death. This is enough to prove that the blood of the pure and eccentric Shelley still flows in the five bodies of those meat-eating, greasy, and wine-fat John Bulls. The British Empire knows not only how to cast gold coins groaning in the vaults of the Bank of England.

However, what kind of person is Shelley (Percy Bysshe Shelley) after all?

On August 4, 1792, he was born in the home of Baron Bysshe Shelley, a wealthy and old family in England. The baron was his grandfather. His father was a member of the Lower House at the time, called Timothy Shelley. He was born with all the luck that people envied. Moreover, he was destined to inherit 2 million yuan of property, vast cities, titles, a seat in the House of Lords, and a noble family background.

He was a beautiful young man like an ancient Greek sculpture, with a graceful posture, sunlight-shining golden hair, eyes as clear as a mountain lake, marble-like white and smooth skin, rose-like red cheeks, a high nose bridge, and thin red lips.

Whether male or female, as long as they saw him, they would be captured by his beauty.

If he had just grown up like this: inheriting wealth and titles, being praised by women, and living like a star in the political and social circles, then he would have been restrained, but Heaven placed a great gift under his head, which was his uninhibited genius.

Because of this genius, he suffered all his life.

Because he was unwilling to be an aristocratic politician and enjoy life, mankind was able to have a collection of Shelley's poems. His life of tears is a shining gem that remains in the hall of human culture. No, all the happiness and progress of mankind are the shade of tears and suffering of certain people in the past. Human tears are by no means useless.

Three

His sadness began in his youth.

He was sent to Eton College, which educates the wealthy sons of England. At that time, Eton adopted Spartan education, and the free thought of the youths was still in its infancy, and was trampled and ravaged without remainder. Upper-grade students treated lower-grade students like slaves, abusing and exploiting them. Noisy quarrels were recognized. There were even teenagers who were beaten to death.

Shelley, who had the beauty of a maiden and an independent spirit, became the target of mockery for the entire school as soon as he entered this school. A game called "Shelley Bait" became popular among the students, and he was humiliated by the whole school. (To be continued)

Jiang Ruting, Zhu Jiesheng: Luoxia Guwu [Sunset and the Lone Duck]

Zhongxi (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening: "Gold and Love"

What is the most powerful thing in the world? Only precious gold and silver. It is often said that money can make the devil push the millstone. Therefore, it is gold that buys the hearts of beauties. Just look at the countless loves that are false. In the field of romance, feelings are the most fickle. Men are greedy for lust. Women love gold and silver. They deceive and love each other with gold and silver. What talk of oaths of eternal love until old age. When the money runs out at the bedside, their hearts will change. Modern female students are the most civilized. They sing that love is sacred. Only for vanity, gold, and lust. They want Western-style houses and modern cars. Look at the days when love is frustrated and they turn against each other. Love goes bankrupt and they separate. Nowadays, the morals of rural women are bad. They are fickle and get to know people. Some of them run away with their husbands' money. Some have illicit affairs in mulberry fields and on the Huai River. When they see through the affair, they send it to the authorities. Temporary couples are like floating clouds. Furthermore, there are middle-aged women with good charm. They give money to young gigolos. Giving gold and silver, entrusting their whole lives. They set the date for love on flowery mornings and moonlit evenings. When beauty fades and money runs out, love ends. Their reputation is ruined and they cut off relations with their families. Young girls become minor stars. Willing to marry old feudal lords in their sixties. They covet gold and silver and do not cherish their bodies. Pear blossoms are destroyed and sea begonias' hearts are broken. Once the old man goes to heaven. The pipa is played again and remarries. Seeing through that, countless loves are bought with gold and silver. How can there be true love in the world? It is foolish to talk about love.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

Paul Muni Says He Can Be Happy with Twenty-Five Dollars a Week (Part 1) 243

— Suyin

Paul Muni is the protagonist in "I Am a Fugitive from a Chain Gang." We have long admired and respected his acting skills. One day, he said to a reporter, "I have twenty-five dollars a week! I can be very happy." The reporter couldn't help but be puzzled. He asked, "Really? Is twenty-five dollars a week really enough?" Paul Muni is one of the most honest people, but after he became a star and enjoyed all the fruits of success, this was too bizarre and unbelievable.

After hearing this question, Paul Muni remained silent for a while. He was not annoyed that people did not believe him, but after thinking quietly for a while, he said, "Yes, I am telling the truth - but there is one condition. I can be happy with twenty-five dollars a month - but I must have some creation."

Indeed, his attitude could not be clearer. What he had said before was now clear. He once said, "If I could be free, I wouldn't necessarily want to be a star. But, whether I'm a star or not, I don't want to make more than two films a year... And those films must be of my own choice... I don't want personal publicity. I also don't like people seeing me and staring with big eyes or asking me for autographs... I don't care about being a big shot... Social fame cannot tempt me... I have never been completely satisfied with everything I have done... I wouldn't be angry if people didn't know my name... What I want is for people to get a sense of feeling and enlightenment from the characters I play..."

From the many words said above, I can see that the protagonist of "I Am a Fugitive from a Chain Gang" has a consistent and unwavering opinion. All he wants is a good role, and he doesn't care about all the other vain names.

Paul Muni also said: "I was very happy when I used to earn twenty-five dollars a month. Why can't I do it now? Money has never had much connection with me. You see, my family has always been poor. But we are not like other poor people who want to get rich all day long or envy the rich. We don't have time to fantasize or envy. We have to work all day long.

"When we work, we are very happy. When we are not happy, it is when we don't have work, but our unhappiness is not because we can't get wages. When I was in Chicago, the theater where I was employed closed down. I got a position in a gas company, and the salary was higher than what I got in the theater. But do you think I was happy at that time? Of course not happy. I simply suffered a great crime. I suffered because I could not move forward in my career."

We must know that Paul Muni is an idealist. Idealists have no harsh demands or extravagant hopes for life. He only asks to do it according to his ideals. Paul Muni said: "I admit that I want to live comfortably, and I like good things. I like to have money because with money I can buy good books, go to concerts, and buy good oil paintings. But those things can also be enjoyed by people who don't have money. I can still go to the library to borrow books, and I can still go to the art museum to appreciate them on holidays. In the summer, there are often concerts in the park, which don't cost any money. Usually, there is also free electricity, which can be heard without spending money. Therefore, when I only earn twenty-five dollars a week, what I enjoy now can still be enjoyed at that time."

Paul Muni also said: "Some of what I said above seems to be sophistry, because I have also told people that the reason why I entered the film industry is because the film industry gives me a large salary. Someone will ask me, since I said that I can be happy with twenty-five dollars a week, why did I make movies because of the high salary given by the film company? Yes, I make movies specifically for money. But my need for money has my own special reasons, not because having money can enjoy comfort and luxury. I have two big reasons. (To be continued)

Film Review

Review of "Homecoming" 244

— Hualun

—Golden City Film—

First of all, we should admire the playwright Wang Bin's attempt to depict the unfortunate suffering and heroic struggles of three women in the waves of famine, unemployment, vanity, and extravagance. Although due to his failure to extract material from the superficial phenomena of the current society and to explore the essence, followed by imperfect handling, plus some restrictions in the production process, it does not appear to be successful on the screen. However, compared with the past products of the same company, it is obviously a new attitude of the present.

The so-called improper handling can be explained from the point that the whole play has no focus. The author worked hard to touch on the problems of famine and unemployment, and introduced Li Xiaomei to a considerable extent from these problems, and also portrayed Jiang Xuejun; but he did not make a deep and broad development from the problems he grasped, and at the same time put down the characters he created without giving them vivid postures and actions, and turned to the disillusionment of Jiang Xiaoxia's love, and the facts of being abandoned. Therefore, only three women can be placed on two lines, and what is depicted is only a superficial outline.

In fact, in terms of characters, Li Xiaomei is superfluous in the play. In the front, the author borrows to explain some of Jiang Xuejun's background and personality that are not very clear, but cannot apply her well, that is, giving up the problems that he has touched and should be developed, and puts her on Jiang Xuejun's side, completely becoming the latter's shadow. If there were no her, and the author wrote directly from Xuejun, then not only would she not feel lacking, but it would be able to introduce the person the author wants to describe to the audience more appropriately, I think.

Secondly, Xiao Ke's character has no personality. It is not until the complete play that one can recognize that he is a frivolous young man who is not dedicated to love. Before Jiang Xiaoxia left for the so-called "freedom of love", although her sister Xuejun briefly said that Xiao Ke was a "bastard", the audience did not know why he was a bastard. Therefore, they would sympathize with Xiaoxia's struggle for love, and feel that her sister's actions were unreasonable or superfluous.

Speaking of Xiaoxia's personality, it is also contradictory. Because the author wrote her as a woman who smokes cigarettes wildly, walks, and wears clothes that are close to gangsters after she was abandoned, it caused the audience to lose sympathy for her, and forgive Xiao Ke's sins of this rascal. This is a regret.

Writing about the fact that the "Jingkui" family rents fields, and that people with "fame" owe rent is also inappropriate. In fact, most of these famous people are local rulers, who collect rent. The bankruptcy of the "Jingkui" family is not as common and profound as that of ordinary poor people. In fact, even if they are not famous people, they will oppose their daughters becoming concubines. As for writing about the oppression of tenant farmers by landlords, with female lust being more important than economic relations, it is a mistake to write primitive feudal landlords in the image of urban capitalists.

The director is mediocre, and the picture is too clumsy. On the one hand, letting the protagonists act too much is inevitably too exaggerated and pretentious (such as Jiang Xuejun's performance after contracting the disease). On the other hand, many plays are missed (such as the scene when the sisters quarrel over the coat). The whole sense of thinness.

Among the three songs, "Great Hand" is better. The dubbing committed the common problem of randomly matching foreign tunes. When Xiaomei knocked on the door for the first time in Shanghai, it was unknown whether she forgot to dub it, or the door was knocked on without any sound.

Except for the landlady, all the speech has a contrived stage meaning. As for the lack of emotion in the timbre, this is a matter of the actors' cultivation.

The acting skills are also mediocre. Although the actor who plays Li Xiaomei lacks vitality, he has more than enough simplicity. That kind of country girl's posture is something that ordinary stars who have become famous in urban life cannot match. Xiaoxia's role is easy to play, but she has not achieved a deep success.

Shen Bao Film Special Submission Guidelines 245

This publication is a film publication that assists cultural propaganda and art. It welcomes external manuscripts, and the remuneration will be generous upon publication.

Once the text is published and paid for, the copyright belongs to Shen Bao.

The text of this publication is mainly in vernacular and must use modern punctuation.

Each submission must be stamped, otherwise it will be returned without payment.

The length of this publication is limited, and the text should be as short as possible. Each manuscript should be around 500 words.

If the submission is a translation, it should be accompanied by the original. English should be omitted as much as possible.

Unless otherwise stated in advance and a stamped return envelope is attached, this publication is not responsible for preserving or returning texts, photos, etc.

Do not write on both sides of the paper or write horizontally, and do not use colored pens.

If two submissions are made for one manuscript or if the text is plagiarized or copied from instructions, no remuneration will be given upon discovery.

Film Novel

Amateur Reporter (After Office Hours) (10) 246

— Tongyun

When Sharon heard what Jim said, she became more and more upset and jumped up, saying, "He was here last night! Here! I was with him! From the time we left the riverside clubhouse until this morning, he hasn't been anywhere else!" She walked closer to Jim's side and said to him hatefully, "Please leave. I can't let Mr. Peniston stay here any longer because of you." As she spoke, she deliberately acted affectionately towards Peniston, pulling him to sit beside her. Peniston sat down and leaned his smooth, seal-like head on Sharon's shoulder, patting her soft hand. She didn't know that the strength of that hand could kill. He also said, "Let's go somewhere to get married." Sharon deliberately answered flirtatiously. Jim watched, helpless, and walked away.

That night, Jim Brown ran to Peniston's place again. He brought Baal with him. Baal complained unwillingly, "You're like a hunting dog, sniffing something and not letting go. But you should know that when people are pushed too hard, they rebel, and when dogs are desperate, they jump over the wall. You already know Peniston is a murderer. What if he starts shooting?" Brown replied, "He's not at home right now. He's at St. Regis with..." Baal interjected, "I know, with that foreign girl. But just because you're so infatuated with that foreign girl, it doesn't mean you have to pin the murder on that man's door, does it?"

Jim ignored him. He said, "You stand on the steps of this wooden house. When you hear the sound of music, shout as loud as you can." Baal asked suspiciously, "Hear music?" But after a while, he indeed heard the sound of a phonograph. He thought that Brown was sometimes like a madman, and sometimes very clever. So he straightened his throat and shouted desperately, "I want a raise... I am an artist... With this little bit of pay... What do you take me for..." He shouted again and again, shouting out the words he had been planning in his heart for several years.

A moment later, Jim came over and said, "Why didn't you shout when I told you to?" Baal, rubbing his throat, replied, "They should have heard it on Mars. Didn't you hear it?" Jim heard it and suddenly seemed to realize something. He muttered to himself, "If she's inside the house, of course she won't hear anything. He must have returned here after taking her home, put the dead man from the wooden house in Julia's own motorboat, rowed it over, and put her on her own bed in her own house..."

Baal asked, "But Julia's motorboat was found in Patterson's boathouse. Then how did he get back?" Brown said impatiently, "Idiot, haven't you heard that Peniston was a champion rower in school? When he went, he put the small boat in the big boat. When he got there, he secured the big boat and rowed the small boat back. Understand, idiot?"

As he spoke, he picked up the small boat and tapped it against the rain. Suddenly, the headlights of a car shone on him. Sitting in the car were Peniston and Sharon. Jim and Baal hurriedly jumped into the small boat and rowed away. Peniston shouted from behind, "I'm going to call the police!" Jim smiled and tipped his hat to Sharon, saying, "That would be great. But tell them to bring a swimmer. Julia lost a powder compact here when she came ashore. Please have them look for it in the water." Peniston silently helped Sharon ashore and took her into the house. He said he was going to change his clothes and left Sharon sitting alone, retreating outside. A few minutes later, Sharon glanced out the window. She saw Peniston swimming in the river. He swam down, then swam up again after a long time, then swam down again. (To be continued)

Movie Ramblings 247

— Luo Ping

"Saxon Heroic Legend After the Calamity" will be brought to the screen by Twentieth Century Pictures.

Ramon Novarro will open a film company in Spain.

We do not disregard the social significance of works, but sentimentalism and pessimism are fundamentally unrealistic and of no value in art. Precisely because they are unrealistic, they are harmful to society.

If people acknowledge that playwrights can describe real life without any criticism, then they should not say "fill the work with the spirit of 'life's door'!" "Life's door" is precisely the author's critical standpoint!

Pessimism and the spirit of "life's door" must be opposed, but we must not therefore believe that sad themes will make the audience depressed, nor can we say that faithfully reflecting the tragic reality is filled with the spirit of "life's door" and will make the audience despondent!
